Joint Game Killing by Non-Muhrims in the Haram: One Penalty Shared
Ruling on non-muhrims jointly killing game in the Haram: they share one penalty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on two non-muhrims jointly killing game in the Haram and explain the reasoning based on the unity of the locus (mahal).

Core Idea
When the violation is against the Haram's single sanctity, one penalty suffices for multiple non-muhrims.

In this lesson, we examine a specific case where two non-muhrims jointly kill game inside the Haram. Unlike muhrims, whose ihram adds a personal sanctity, non-muhrims are bound only by the sanctity of the place. The Hanafi school rules that a single fidyah is due, to be divided equally. This ruling hinges on the concept of 'mahal' — the locus of the violation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the act
Two non-muhrims (halal) jointly kill game within the Haram. Determine who is involved and what they did.
Non-muhrim means not in ihram; they are not pilgrims.
2
Determine the ruling
The text states: upon them is one fidyah. This is the Hanafi position.
The ruling is wajib.
3
Understand the basis (ta'lil)
The penalty is not due to ihram (since they are not muhrim) but due to the sanctity of the Haram, which is a single locus (mahal).
Mahal is a key technical term.
4
Distinguish from the muhrim case
If they were muhrim, each would owe a separate penalty because each ihram is a separate sanctity.
This contrast is essential for clarity.
5
Apply the rule: one mahal, one penalty
Therefore, the two non-muhrims share one fidyah, half each.
The text adds: 'aqwal: if mahal is one, one penalty becomes due.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اشترک حلالان في قتل صيد الحرم فعليهما جزاء واحد [۶] (۶۲) اگر دو حلال حرم کے شکار کے قتل میں شریک ہوئے تو دونوں پر ایک ہی بدلہ ہے۔
یہاں دونوں حلال ہیں اس لئے احرام کی وجہ سے بدلہ نہیں ہے بلکہ حرم کے احترام میں شکار کا بدلہ لازم ہے۔ اس لئے محل ایک ہے اس لئے دونوں حلال پر ایک شکار کا بدلہ لازم ہوگا اور دونوں پر آدھا آدھا بدلہ ہوگا۔
اقوال محل ایک ہو تو ایک بدلہ لازم ہوتا ہے۔
And if two non-muhrims (halal) jointly kill a game of the Haram, then upon them is one fidyah. (62) If two non-muhrims jointly kill a game in the Haram, then they owe one penalty. Here, both are non-muhrims, so the penalty is not because of ihram but because of the respect of the Haram. Therefore, the locus is one, so the two non-muhrims owe one penalty for the game, and each will owe half the penalty. Statements: if the locus is one, one penalty becomes due.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This ruling distinguishes the case of non-muhrims (those not in ihram) from muhrims. When two non-muhrims jointly kill game within the Haram, they are only liable for a single fidyah between them, which they share equally. The reasoning is that the violation is against the sanctity of the Haram, which is a single entity (mahal). Since there is only one 'place' (the Haram) being violated, the penalty is one. This contrasts with the muhrim case where each person's individual ihram is an additional sanctity. The author notes that the penalty is divided equally between the two non-muhrims.

Key Terms
حلال (halal): A person not in ihram; a non-muhrim.
محل (mahal): The 'locus' of the violation; here, the sanctity of the Haram is the single mahal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do two non-muhrims share one penalty for killing game in the Haram?
A) Because they both committed the same act.
B) Because the Haram's sanctity is one, so one violation occurs.
C) Because each is only half responsible.
D) Because they were not in ihram.

Key Takeaway
When non-muhrims jointly kill game in the Haram, the Hanafi school imposes one shared fidyah because the sanctity of the Haram is a single locus.

Muhrim's Sale of Game: Void Ab Initio
States that a muhrim's game transaction is void due to lack of ownership.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a muhrim's sale or purchase of game, explain the ownership condition, and distinguish batil from fasid.

Core Idea
A muhrim cannot own game, so any sale or purchase of it is void (batil) from the outset.

In this passage, the author addresses a specific scenario: a person in the state of ihram (muhrim) engaging in a transaction involving game. The ruling is clear: such a contract is not merely defective (fasid) but completely void (batil). The reason strikes at the heart of contract validity—the seller must own the item. Since the muhrim never acquires ownership of game during ihram, the contract is invalid. We'll unpack the logic and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? What is the hukm (batil) and who performs it?
The act is sale or purchase of game by a muhrim.
2
Locate the underlying reason (illah)
Why is the sale batil? The passage states the muhrim cannot own the game.
Ownership (milkiyyah) is a condition for a valid sale.
3
Distinguish batil from fasid
Batil means the contract has no legal effect; fasid can be corrected. Here the deficiency is fundamental.
In Hanafi, batil is void ab initio, fasid is voidable.
4
Note cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Other schools may permit sale if the game was owned before ihram or obtained through valid means.
The Hanafi position is strict: no ownership possible during ihram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا باع المحرم صيدا او (۶۳) اگر محرم نے شکار بچایا خریدا تو بیع باطل ہے۔
احرام کی وجہ سے محرم شکار کا مالک ہی نہیں بنا اور نہ بن سکے گا اس لئے اس کا خرید نا یا بیچنا باطل ہے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ موجود ہے
And if a muhrim sells game or (63) if a muhrim sells or buys game, the sale is invalid. Because of ihram, the muhrim did not become the owner of the game and cannot become its owner, so his buying or selling is invalid. (2) There is an indication of this in the hadith.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This ruling states that any transaction involving game (sale or purchase) by a muhrim is void (batil). The reason is that a muhrim cannot acquire ownership of game because the prohibition of hunting prevents him from owning it. Since ownership is a prerequisite for valid sale, the contract is invalid. The author notes that there is a hadith indicating this principle.

Key Terms
باطل (batil): Completely void; the contract has no legal effect.
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, subject to prohibitions including hunting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a muhrim's sale of game considered batil?
A) Because the muhrim is under a religious restriction.
B) Because the muhrim cannot own the game due to ihram.
C) Because the price is not fixed.
D) Because the game is not halal to eat.

Key Takeaway
A muhrim's transaction involving game is void because he never acquires ownership; batil means no legal effect.

Two Muhrim Share Killing Game in Haram
Ruling with proof on joint game killing by muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two muhrim jointly kill game in the Haram and explain the evidence (dalil) supporting individual compensation.

Core Idea
Each muhrim owes full compensation for killing game, even if shared—the violation is personal.

When two people in ihram jointly kill a single game animal, does the compensation get divided or multiplied? The Hanafi school answers clearly: each owes the full penalty. In this lesson, we will examine the reasoning and proof behind this ruling, grounded in the sanctity of ihram and a transmitted athar from Imam Malik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is two muhrim jointly killing a game animal in the Haram. The ruling is that each muhrim owes full compensation (jaza' kamil), not half or shared.
The compensation is typically a dam (sheep) in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is an athar from Imam Malik in the Muwatta, where he states: 'I think that each person among them owes compensation.'
This is a qawl sahabi (companion-like) statement, considered zanni al-thubut but sufficient for obligation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Malik's statement directly indicates individual liability. Additionally, the reasoning is that each muhrim has violated the sanctity of their own ihram, so the consequence is also personal.
This is supported by a previous hadith: pointing to game for a non-muhrim to kill already imposes compensation; actual participation is stronger.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may hold that only one compensation is required if the killing was cooperative. The Hanafi position is that the violation is personal, so each pays.
This is mukhtalaf fih—a valid difference of opinion.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi view is preferred because the evidence (athar of Malik) is explicit, and the principle of multiple violations demands multiple compensations.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اشترک محرمان في قتل صيد الحرم فعلى كل واحد منهما الجزاء كاملا [۷۷۵] (۶۱) 

(۷۷۴] (۶۱) اگر دو محرم ایک شکار کے قتل میں شریک ہو جائے تو ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک پر پورا پورا بدلہ لازم ہوگا۔ (1) یہاں احرام کے احترام کی وجہ سے شکار کا بدلہ لازم ہوتا ہے اور دونوں کا احرام ہے اور دونوں نے اپنے اپنے احرام کی بے احترامی کی ہے اس لئے دونوں پر الگ الگ پورا پورا دم لازم ہوگا۔ چاہے شکار ایک ہی ہو (۲) مسئلہ نمبر ۳۷ میں حدیث گزری کہ اگر شکار کے لئے اشارہ بھی کیا اور دوسرے حلال نے اس کو قتل کیا تو محرم پر بدلہ لازم ہے۔ یہاں تو اشارہ سے بڑھ کر شکار کے قتل کرنے میں شریک ہوا اس لئے بدرجہ اولی شکار کا بدلہ لازم ہوگا (۳) اثر میں ہے قال مالک فی القوم يصيبون الصيد جميعا وهم محرمون او في الحرم قال ارى ان كل انسان منهم جزاء ان حكم عليهم بالهدى فعلى كل انسان منهم هدى (الف) (موطا امام مالک، باب جامع الفديه ص ۲۵۲) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہر ایک محرم پر الگ الگ شکار کا بدلہ لازم ہو گا۔

حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت امام مالک نے فرمایا تمام ہی قوم نے شکار پر حملہ کیا اور وہ محرم تھے یا شکار حرم میں تھا تو فرمایا میں سمجھتا ہوں ہر ایک پر بدلہ لازم ہے۔ اگر ان پر ہدی کا فیصلہ کیا جائے تو ہر ایک پر ہادی لازم ہوگی۔
And if two muhrim [those in ihram] share in killing game of the Haram, then upon each one of them is the full compensation. (61) If two muhrim share in killing one game, each one is required to pay full compensation. ... The athar: Malik said concerning a group that strikes game all together while they are muhrim or in the Haram: I think that each person among them owes compensation; if judgment is passed that they owe hady, then each owes a hady. (Footnote: Imam Malik said: all the group attacked the game and they were muhrim or the game was in the Haram...).
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof for a situation where two persons in the state of ihram (muhrim) jointly kill a single game animal within the Haram. The ruling is that each muhrim owes full compensation (jaza') individually, not half. The reasoning is that the prohibition is attached to the state of ihram of each person; each has violated the sanctity of ihram by participating in killing. Even if the game is one, the sin is multiple. The author supports this with three points: (1) the principle that respect for ihram demands compensation per person; (2) a previous hadith (in issue 37) that even pointing to game for a non-muhrim to kill obligates compensation, so actual participation is stronger; and (3) an athar from Imam Malik in the Muwatta that each of a group of muhrim owes a separate hady. This highlights the Hanafi view that the cause (ihram violation) is personal, so the consequence is not shared.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
جزاء (jaza'): Compensation for killing game; an animal sacrifice or equivalent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling when two muhrim jointly kill one game animal in the Haram?
A) One compensation total.
B) Half each.
C) Full each.
D) No compensation.

Key Takeaway
Each muhrim who participates in killing game in the Haram owes his own full compensation, because the violation is personal.

Two Non-Muhrim Jointly Killing Game in Haram: One Compensation
Ruling on joint killing by non-muhrim in Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when two non-muhrim jointly kill game in the Haram and explain why they share one compensation.

Core Idea
When multiple non-muhrim jointly kill game in the Haram, they owe a single compensation divided equally, because the sanctity is attached to the place, not the persons.

In previous lessons, we learned that a muhrim who kills game owes a full compensation. But what happens when two people who are NOT in ihram jointly kill a single animal inside the Haram? This lesson addresses that scenario, clarifying that the ruling hinges on the sanctity of the Haram itself, not the state of the hunters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and their state
Note that both are halal (not muhrim). This is crucial because the prohibition here is from the Haram, not ihram.
2
Apply the principle of joint liability
The place (Haram) is one, so the violation is one. Each participant is liable for a share.
The commentary states: 'mahall wahid' (place is one).
3
State the outcome
One compensation divided equally between the two.
This contrasts with the case of muhrim, where each owes full compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اشترک حلالان في قتل صيد الحرم فعليهما جزاء واحد [۷۷۵] (۶۲) 

(۷۷۵) (۶۲) اگر دو حلال حرم کے شکار کے قتل میں شریک ہوئے تو دونوں پر ایک ہی بدلہ ہے۔
یہاں دونوں حلال ہیں اس لئے احرام کی وجہ سے بدلہ نہیں ہے بلکہ حرم کے احترام میں شکار کا بدلہ لازم ہے۔ اس لئے محل ایک ہے اس لئے دونوں حلال پر ایک شکار کا بدلہ لازم ہوگا اور دونوں پر آدھا آدھا بدلہ ہوگا۔
اقوال محل ایک ہو تو ایک بدلہ لازم ہوتا ہے۔
And if two non-muhrim share in killing game of the Haram, then upon both of them is one compensation. (62) If two non-muhrim share in killing game of the Haram, then upon both is one compensation. Here, both are halal (not in ihram), so compensation is not due because of ihram, but due to respect of the Haram. Therefore, the place is one, so upon both is one game compensation, and they split it half and half. Statements: if the place is one, one compensation is due.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement contrasting the previous case. Here, two persons not in ihram (halal) jointly kill game within the Haram. The ruling is that they owe a single compensation (dam) between them, divided equally. The reasoning is that the prohibition of hunting in the Haram is attached to the place (the Haram), not to the state of the person. Since the place is one, the violation is one, and therefore the compensation is one. This distinguishes the case from the previous where each muhrim owed full compensation because the prohibition was attached to each person's ihram. The phrase 'place is one' (mahall wahid) means the Haram is a single sanctity, so one violation triggers one compensation even if multiple perpetrators.

Key Terms
حلال (halal): A person not in the state of ihram.
حرم (haram): The sacred territory of Makkah.
بدلہ (badlah): Compensation; same as jaza' or dam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Each owes full compensation.
B) They owe one compensation divided equally.
C) No compensation due.
D) They owe two compensations.

Key Takeaway
When two non-muhrim jointly kill game inside the Haram, they owe a single compensation divided equally, because the sanctity of the Haram is one.

The Qarin's Exception: One Dam Instead of Two
Explanation of exception to qarin's two dams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a qarin owes only one dam instead of two, and explain the legal reasoning for the exception.

Core Idea
A qarin owes two dams, but crossing the miqat without ihram reduces it to one.

The qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram) generally must offer two animal sacrifices (dam): one for Hajj and one for Umrah. However, if a person crosses the miqat boundary without assuming ihram and only later enters ihram for both, only one dam is required. This lesson unpacks that exception and its reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
Identify the default obligation of a qarin: two dams, one for each rite.
This is established by the athar of Ibrahim.
2
Identify the exception
Find the condition: crossing the miqat without ihram, then later becoming a qarin.
The text says "unless he crosses the miqat without ihram, then assumes ihram for both."
3
Understand the legal reasoning
The ruling is based on the moment of crossing the miqat: at that time the person was not yet a qarin, so only one dam is owed for the passage violation.
The later qarin status does not retroactively impose the second dam.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Note that the Shafi'i school holds a qarin owes only one sacrifice overall, not two.
This difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Apply to a real scenario
Test the exception: a traveler flies past the miqat without ihram, then lands and assumes ihram for Hajj and Umrah together.
Only one dam is due, not two.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المفرد دما فعليه دمان دم لحجته ودم لعمرته [۷۷۳] (۲۰) الا ان يتجاوز الميقات من غیر احرام ثم يحرم بالعمرة والحج فيلزمه دم واحد

ابن ابی شیبہ میں ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال هديان (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۱۸ ما يجب عليه من الهدى اذا جمع بینھما فاحصر، ج ثالث ،ص ۱۳۳، نمبر ۱۲۷۹۶) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ قارن پر دو ہری ہے۔

[۷۷۳] (۲۰) مگر یہ کہ میقات سے بغیر احرام کے گزر جائے پھر عمرہ اور حج کا احرام باندھے تو اس کو ایک ہی دم لازم ہوگا۔ اس صورت میں ایک ہی دم اس لئے لازم ہے کہ میقات سے گزرتے وقت وہ قارن نہیں تھا۔ قارن تو بعد میں بنا ہے اور بعد میں حج اور عمرہ کا احرام باندھا ہے اس لئے میقات سے بغیر احرام کے گزرنے کا ایک دم لازم ہوگا۔
The one performing [Hajj] alone? owes two dams: a dam for his Hajj and a dam for his Umrah. [773] (20) Unless he crosses the miqat without ihram, then he assumes ihram for Umrah and Hajj, so one dam is obligatory upon him. Ibn Abi Shaybah has: from Ibrahim, he said: two hadis. ... This athar indicates that the qarin owes two dams. [773] (20) But if he crosses the miqat without ihram, then ties ihram for Umrah and Hajj, one dam is obligatory upon him. In this case, one dam is obligatory because at the time of crossing the miqat he was not a qarin. He became a qarin later and tied ihram for Hajj and Umrah later; therefore, one dam is owed for crossing the miqat without ihram.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school regarding the qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah). The base ruling states that a qarin owes two dams—one for his Hajj and one for his Umrah. This is proven by the athar from Ibrahim transmitted by Ibn Abi Shaybah. However, there is an exception: if a person crosses the miqat boundary without assuming ihram, and only later assumes ihram for both Hajj and Umrah, then only one dam is due. The reasoning is that at the moment of crossing the miqat, he was not yet a qarin, so the sin of passing the miqat without ihram is separate; the later combination does not retroactively make him liable for two dams. This shows the precision of Hanafi fiqh in applying rules based on the actual state at each moment.

Key Terms
قارن (qarin): One who combines Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram.
دم (dam): An animal sacrifice required for certain violations or compensations in Hajj.
ميقات (miqat): The designated boundary for entering the state of ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a qarin owe only one dam instead of two?
A) If he performs Umrah before Hajj.
B) If he crosses the miqat without ihram and then assumes ihram for both.
C) If he is a resident of Mecca.
D) If he offers a hady instead of dam.

Key Takeaway
A qarin generally owes two dams, but crossing the miqat without ihram and later becoming a qarin reduces it to one.

Muhrim's Transaction of Game is Void
Ruling with proof on muhrim's transaction of game.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim's sale or purchase of game, explain the hadith-based proof, and distinguish why the contract is batil rather than fasid.

Core Idea
A muhrim cannot own game; any sale or purchase is void from the start.

This lesson addresses a specific restriction during ihram: the prohibition on trading game. The Hanafi school rules that any sale or purchase of game by a muhrim is absolutely void (batil). We will examine the proof from the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) refused a gift of game while in ihram, establishing that a muhrim cannot acquire ownership of game. This ruling has practical implications for pilgrims and those teaching Hajj rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine exactly what action is being ruled upon: a muhrim selling or buying game (sayd). The ruling is that the transaction is batil (void).
Batil means the contract has no legal effect; no ownership transfers.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Sa'b ibn Jaththamah where the Prophet returned a gift of a wild donkey because he was muhrim. This hadith is from Sahih Bukhari.
The hadith is ahad, but its thubut is qati due to Bukhari's authenticity, though its dalala is zanni.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's refusal of the gift shows that a muhrim cannot accept ownership of game. Since ownership is prohibited, any transaction (sale or purchase) that would transfer ownership is invalid.
The author uses qiyas: if ownership cannot be established via gift (a valid means), it also cannot be via purchase.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may differ; some might consider the transaction fasid (voidable) or merely makruh. The Hanafi position is clear: it is batil.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf_fih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi position
The ruling is mufta bihi and from Zahir al-Riwayah. The proof is strong because the Prophet explicitly linked the refusal to ihram.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded.

واذا باع المحرم صيدا او ابتاعه فالبيع باطل.

(۷۷۶ (۶۳) اگر محرم نے شکار بےچا یا خریدا تو بیع باطل ہے۔
احرام کی وجہ سے محرم شکار کا مالک ہی نہیں بنا اور نہ بن سکے گا اس لئے اس کا خریدنا یا بیچنا باطل ہے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ موجود ہے

عن الصعب بن جثامة الليثى انه اهدى لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حمارا وحشيا وهو بالابواء او بودان فرده عليه فلما رى ما في وجهه قال انا لم نرده عليك الا انا حرم (ب) (بخاری شريف، باب اذا اهدى الحرم حمرا وحشيا لم يقبل ص ۲۳۶ نمبر ۱۸۲۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ کو وحشی گدھا زندہ ہدیہ دیا گیا تو آپ نے صرف اس وجہ سے اس کو قبول نہیں کیا کہ آپ محرم تھے۔ اس سے اشارہ ملتا ہے كه محرم شکار کا مالک نہیں ہوتا۔ اس لئے یہ نہ بیچ کر سکتا ہے اور نہ اس کو خرید سکتا ہے (۲) ہدیہ میں لیکر بھی مالک بنتا ہے اور خریدنے سے بھی مالک بنتا ہے اس لئے جب ہدیہ میں قبول کر کے مالک نہیں بنا تو خرید کر کے بھی مالک نہیں بن سکتا۔

حاشیہ : (الف) صعب بن جثامہ سے روایت ہے کہ انہوں نے حضور کو وحشی گدھا مقام ابواء یا مقام ودان میں ہدیہ دیا تو آپ نے اس کو واپس کر دیا۔ پس جب اس کے چہرے پر غمگینی کے اثرات دیکھے تو آپ نے فرمایا کہ اس کو آپ پر واپس نہیں کیا مگر یہ لہ میں محرم ہوں۔
And if a muhrim sells game or buys it, the sale is void. (63) If a muhrim sells or buys game, the sale is void. Because due to ihram, the muhrim has not become the owner of the game and cannot become owner; therefore his buying or selling is void. (2) The hadith alludes to this. From Sa'b ibn Jaththamah al-Laythi: he gave a wild donkey as a gift to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) while he was at al-Abwa or Waddan, and he returned it to him. When he saw what was on his face, he said: 'We did not return it to you except that we are in ihram.' (Bukhari) This hadith indicates that a muhrim does not own game. Therefore he can neither sell it nor buy it. (2) One becomes owner by taking a gift and also by buying; so when he did not become owner by accepting a gift, he cannot become owner by purchasing. Footnote: (a) Sa'b ibn Jaththamah narrated that he gave the Prophet a wild donkey as a gift...
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof regarding the legal capacity of a muhrim concerning game. The ruling is that any sale or purchase of game by a muhrim is void (batil). The reason is that the state of ihram prevents the muhrim from acquiring ownership of game; game is considered 'non-property' for a muhrim. The proof is the well-known hadith of Sa'b ibn Jaththamah where the Prophet (peace be upon him) refused to accept a gift of game while in ihram, explaining that the prohibition is due to ihram. The author draws an analogy (qiyas): if ownership cannot be established via gift (which is a means of ownership), it also cannot be established via purchase. Therefore, any transaction concerning game by a muhrim is inherently invalid, as the object (game) is not legally capable of being owned by him.

Key Terms
باطل (batil): Void contract; no legal effects.
صيد (sayd): Hunted game animal (land animal or bird).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a muhrim's purchase of game invalid?
A) Because the game is not halal.
B) Because the muhrim cannot own game while in ihram.
C) Because the seller is usually a non-muhrim.
D) Because the price is too high.

Key Takeaway
A muhrim's sale or purchase of game is batil because the muhrim cannot lawfully own game during ihram.

Ihsar: The Hanafi Position on Being Prevented from Completing Hajj/Umrah
Definition and ruling of ihsar with proofs and dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ihsar (being prevented from completing Hajj/Umrah), cite the Quranic and hadith proofs, and explain the difference with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school extends ihsar beyond enemy to illness and injury; the Quranic wording is general, and a hadith explicitly mentions broken bones.

Ihsar is a situation where a muhrim cannot complete Hajj or Umrah due to an obstacle such as an enemy, illness, or injury. This lesson examines the Hanafi definition and ruling, the primary proofs from the Quran and Sunnah, and the disagreement with Imam al-Shafi'i, who restricts ihsar to enemy prevention only.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of ihsar
Ihsar linguistically means prevention; legally, it refers to being stopped from completing Hajj or Umrah by any cause that makes continuation impossible.
The Hanafi school includes three categories: enemy, illness, and injury (e.g., broken bone).
2
Identify the primary Quranic proof
Allah says in Surah al-Baqarah 2:196: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah. But if you are prevented, then [offer] whatever sacrificial animal is easy.' The general term 'prevented' (uhsirtum) is not restricted to enemy.
The verse commands sending a hadi and postponing shaving until it reaches its place.
3
Recognize the hadith proofs
The Prophet (saw) was prevented at Hudaybiyyah by the Quraysh (Bukhari). Additionally, a hadith from al-Hajjaj ibn Amr states: 'Whoever breaks a bone or becomes lame has become halal, and upon him is Hajj the following year.' This explicitly includes injury and illness.
These hadiths are used to extend the ruling beyond enemy prevention.
4
Contrast the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that ihsar only occurs due to an enemy, citing the incident of Hudaybiyyah and a statement of Ibn Abbas: 'There is no ihsar except the ihsar of an enemy.'
The Hanafi response: the hadith of al-Hajjaj is explicit, and the Quranic wording is general; the Hudaybiyyah incident was just one example.
5
Apply the Hanafi ruling
A mahsur (prevented person) should send a sacrificial animal (goat or sheep) to the Haram to be slaughtered on a specified day. On that day, he becomes halal (exits ihram). If the Hajj was obligatory, he must make it up the following year.
The sending of the hadi is wajib; tahallul becomes permissible upon its slaughter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[۷۷۷] (۱) جب محرم دشمن کی وجہ سے مصر ہو جائے یا اس کو مرض لاحق ہو جائے جو اس کو آگے بڑھنے سے روک دے تو جائز ہے اس کو حلال ہوتا۔ اور اس کو کہا جائے گا کہ بکری بھیجو جو حرم میں ذبح کی جائے۔ احصار دشمن کی وجہ سے بھی ہو سکتا ہے اور مرض کی وجہ سے بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ بہر حال کسی وجہ سے بھی اعمال حج یا عمرہ ادا نہ کرسکتا ہو تو حصار ہوگا۔ اب اس کے لئے یہ ہے کہ بکری حرم بھیجے جو وہاں ذبح کی جائے۔ یا کسی جانے والے کو بکری دیدے اور متعین دن میں ذبح کرنے کا وعدہ کروالے اور اس دن محصر حلال ہو جائے۔ جس طرح دشمن سے احصار ہوتا ہے اسی طرح مرض سے بھی احصار ہوتا ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے سـمـعــت الـحـجـاج ابن عمرو الانصاري قال قال رسول الله الله من كسر او عرج فقد حل وعليه الحج من قابل قال عكرمة فسألت ابن عباس وأبا هريرة عن ذلك فقالا صدق وفي رواية آخر او مرض (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الاحصارص ۲۶۴ نمبر ۱۸۶۲/ ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الذى يحل بالج فیکسر او يعرج ص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۹۴۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ صرف دشمن ہی کی وجہ سے نہیں بلکہ مرض اور پاؤں ٹوٹنے کی وجہ سے بھی احصار ہو سکتا ہے۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک صرف دشمن کی وجہ سے احصار ہوتا ہے۔ ان کی دلیل عمرہ اور صلح حدیبیہ کا واقعہ ہے جس میں صرف دشمن کفار مکہ کی وجہ سے احصار ہوا ہے (۲) عن ابن عباس قال لا حصر الا حصر العدو (و) (سن للبیھقی ، باب من لم ير الا حلال بالا حصار بالمرض ج

Chapter of Ihsar. Book of Hajj. [7] (1) When the muhrim is prevented (ihsar) by an enemy or is afflicted by an illness that prevents him from proceeding, it is permissible for him to exit ihram (tahallul). And necessary notes on Bab al-Ihsar: Ihsar means being prevented from Hajj or Umrah. Its proof is this verse: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah. But if you are prevented, then [offer] whatever sacrificial animal is easy. And do not shave your heads until the sacrificial animal reaches its place of slaughter.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196, part). From this verse it is understood that when ihsar occurs, one should send a hadi (sacrificial animal) to the House of Allah and become halal. (2) The hadith proof of ihsar is that Ibn Abbas said: 'The Messenger of Allah was prevented (uhsira), so he shaved his head, had intercourse with his wives, and sacrificed his hadi, until he performed Umrah the following year.' (Bukhari, chapter on when a person performing Umrah is prevented, p. 243 no. 1809). This hadith proves that ihsar can occur in Umrah, because the Prophet was prevented by the polytheists of Quraysh at Hudaybiyyah and was prevented from Umrah. [777] (1) When a muhrim is prevented (mahsur) by an enemy or is afflicted with an illness that prevents him from moving forward, it is permissible for him to become halal. And he will be told to send a goat to be slaughtered in the Haram. Ihsar can be due to an enemy and also due to illness. In any case, if he cannot perform the actions of Hajj or Umrah, he becomes mahsur. Now for him, he should send a goat to the Haram to be slaughtered there, or give a goat to someone going and take a promise to slaughter on a specified day, and on that day the mahsur becomes halal. Just as ihsar occurs from enemy, similarly ihsar occurs from illness. Its proof is this hadith: 'I heard al-Hajjaj ibn Amr al-Ansari say: The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever breaks a bone or becomes lame has become halal, and upon him is Hajj the following year.' Ikrimah said: 'I asked Ibn Abbas and Abu Hurairah about that, and they said: He spoke the truth.' And in another narration: 'or becomes ill.' (Abu Dawud, chapter on ihsar, p. 264 no. 1862/ Tirmidhi, chapter on what has been narrated about one who becomes halal due to Hajj and breaks or becomes lame, p. 187 no. 940). From this hadith it is understood that ihsar can occur not only due to enemy but also due to illness and broken bones. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, ihsar occurs only due to enemy. Their proof is the event of Umrah and Hudaybiyyah, in which ihsar occurred only due to the enemy, the polytheists of Makkah. (2) From Ibn Abbas: 'There is no ihsar except the ihsar of an enemy.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on those who consider ihsar only by illness, not by enemy). Footnote: (a) Complete Hajj and Umrah for Allah. Then if you are prevented, then whatever sacrificial animal is easy, and do not shave your heads until the sacrificial animal reaches its place. (b) Ibn Abbas said: The Prophet was prevented, so he shaved his head, had intercourse with his wives, and sacrificed his hadi, until he performed Umrah the following year. (c) He said: Whoever breaks a bone or becomes lame becomes halal, and upon him is Hajj the following year. Ikrimah said: I asked Ibn Abbas and Abu Hurairah about that, and they said he spoke the truth. (1) Ibn Abbas said: There is no ihsar except the ihsar of an enemy.
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute passage. The author defines ihsar as being prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah, and states that a muhrim may exit ihram (tahallul) if prevented by an enemy or illness. The primary proof is Quran 2:196, which commands sending a sacrificial animal (hadi) and not shaving until it reaches its destination. The author then presents a hadith from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet (saw) was prevented at Hudaybiyyah, shaved his head, and later performed Umrah. The text also cites a hadith about breaking a bone or lameness as valid causes for ihsar. The dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i is highlighted: Shafi'i holds that ihsar applies only to enemy prevention, citing the same incident and a statement of Ibn Abbas. The Hanafi position, supported by the hadith of al-Hajjaj ibn Amr, includes illness and injury as causes. The commentary explains the practical ruling: a mahsur should send a goat to the Haram to be slaughtered on a specified day, and on that day he becomes halal. The text emphasizes that ihsar can be due to enemy or illness, contrary to Shafi'i's narrower view.

Key Terms
احصار (ihsār): Being prevented from completing the rites of Hajj or Umrah by any obstacle such as enemy, illness, or injury.
محصر (muḥṣar): A person who is prevented (mahsur) from completing Hajj/Umrah due to ihsar.
هدى (hady): A sacrificial animal (e.g., goat, sheep) sent to the Haram for slaughter in case of ihsar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows tahallul due to any cause of prevention, backed by general Quranic command and explicit hadith on illness/injury, unlike the Shafi'i restriction.

Ihsar: Causes and Place of Sacrifice (Hanafi vs Shafi'i)
Inter-madhhab dispute with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the causes of ihsar (prevention from completing Hajj/Umrah) and the place where the sacrificial animal (hady) must be sent, and compare it with the Shafi'i view, identifying the proofs and the practical consequence of the difference.

Core Idea
Ihsar can result from enemy or illness; the hady must reach the Haram — the Hanafi ruling, supported by authentic hadith.

Ihsar, or being prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah, triggers specific rulings about exiting ihram and offering a sacrifice. This passage presents a key point of disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: what counts as a valid cause of ihsar, and where must the sacrifice be offered? We will work through the proofs cited by each school and see how the Hanafis establish their broader ruling.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two causes of ihsar according to the Hanafis (enemy and illness) and the required action (send a goat to be slaughtered in the Haram).
The text explicitly states: 'Ihsar can occur due to enemy or illness.'
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State that Imam al-Shafi'i restricts ihsar to enemy prevention only, and allows the sacrifice to be offered wherever the person is prevented, not necessarily in the Haram.
The Shafi'i view is based on the incident of Hudaybiyyah and the report of Ibn Abbas.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: the hadith that 'no ihsar except from enemy' (Ibn Abbas) and the fact that the Prophet and companions sacrificed at Hudaybiyyah, which is outside the Haram.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafis counter: they cite the authentic hadith of al-Hajjaj ibn Amr that includes broken bone and illness, and the command to replace the Hudaybiyyah sacrifices, showing they were not valid.
The Hanafis argue that the general proof (broken bone/illness) overrides the specific incident.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence: a Hanafi muhrim prevented by illness can send a sacrifice to the Haram and become halal; a Shafi'i in the same situation cannot exit ihram because illness is not a valid cause.
The difference affects pilgrims who face illness or accident during their journey.

ضروری نوٹ احصار حج یا عمرہ سے روک دیے جانے کو کہتے ہیں۔ اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے واسموا الحج والعمرة لله فان احصرتم فما استيسر من الهدى ولا تحلقوا رؤوسكم حتى يبلغ الهدى لمحله (الف) ( آیت ۹۶ اسورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ احصار ہو جائے تو ہدی بیت اللہ بھیجے اور حلال ہو جائے (۲) حدیث احصار کی دلیل یہ ہے فقال ابن عباس قد احصر رسول الله فحلق رأسه وجامع نسائه ونحر هديه حتى اعتمر عاما قابلا (ب) (بخاری شریف، باب اذا احصر المعتمر ص۲۴۳ نمبر ۱۸۰۹) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ عمرہ میں احصار ہو سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور کو صلح حدیبیہ کے موقع پر کفار قریش نے روکا تھا اور عمرہ سے
احصار کیا تھا۔
[۷۷۷] (۱) جب محرم دشمن کی وجہ سے مصر ہو جائے یا اس کو مرض لاحق ہو جائے جو اس کو آگے بڑھنے سے روک دے تو جائز ہے اس کو حلال ہوتا۔ اور اس کو کہا جائے گا کہ بکری بھیجو جو حرم میں ذبح کی جائے۔ احصار دشمن کی وجہ سے بھی ہو سکتا ہے اور مرض کی وجہ سے بھی ہو سکتا ہے۔ بہر حال کسی وجہ سے بھی اعمال حج یا عمرہ ادا نہ کرسکتا ہو تو حصار ہوگا۔ اب اس کے لئے یہ ہے کہ بکری حرم بھیجے جو وہاں ذبح کی جائے۔ یا کسی جانے والے کو بکری دیدے اور متعین دن میں ذبح کرنے کا وعدہ کروالے اور اس دن محصر حلال ہو جائے۔ جس طرح دشمن سے احصار ہوتا ہے اسی طرح مرض سے بھی احصار ہوتا ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے سـمـعــت الـحـجـاج ابن عمرو الانصاري قال قال رسول الله الله من كسر او عرج فقد حل وعليه الحج من قابل قال عكرمة فسألت ابن عباس وأبا هريرة عن ذلك فقالا صدق وفي رواية آخر او مرض (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الاحصارص ۲۶۴ نمبر ۱۸۶۲/ ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الذى يحل بالج فیکسر او يعرج ص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۹۴۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ صرف دشمن ہی کی وجہ سے نہیں بلکہ مرض اور پاؤں ٹوٹنے کی وجہ سے بھی احصار ہو سکتا ہے۔ امام شافعی کے نزدیک صرف دشمن کی وجہ سے احصار ہوتا ہے۔ ان کی دلیل عمرہ اور صلح حدیبیہ کا واقعہ ہے جس میں صرف دشمن کفار مکہ کی وجہ سے احصار ہوا ہے (۲) عن ابن عباس قال لا حصر الا حصر العدو (و) (سن للبیھقی ، باب من لم ير الا حلال بالا حصار بالمرض ج
حاشیہ : (الف) حج اور عمرہ کو پورا کرو۔ پس اگر تم روک دیئے گئے تو جو ہدی آسان ہو۔ اور سر کا حلق مت کر اؤ یہاں تک کہ ہدی اپنی جگہ تک پہنچ جائے (ب) ابن عباس نے فرمایا حضور کو انصار کیا تو آپ نے اپنا سر حلق کرایا۔ اور اپنی بیوی سے جماع کیا اور ہدی کا نحر کیا یہاں تک کہ اگلے سال محمرہ کیا ۔ (ج) آپ نے فرمایا جس کا کچھ ٹوٹ گیا پالنگڑا ہو گیا تو حلال ہو جائے اور اس پر اگلے سال حج ہے۔ حضرت عکرمہ نے فرمایا میں نے ابن عباس اور حضرت ابو ہریرہ کو اس بارے میں پوچھا تو فرمایا کہ بیچ فرمایا (1) ابن عباس نے فرمایا حصر نہیں ہے مگر دشمن کی جانب سے حصر ہو سکتا ہے۔

محرم بالعمرة فاحصر فقال عبد الله ابعثوا بالهدى واجعلوا بينكم وبينه يوم امار فاذا ذبح الهدى بمكة حل هذا قال ابو عبيد قال الكسائي الامار العلامة (ج) ( سنن بیھقی ، باب من رای الاحلال بالا حصار بالمرض ج خاص ص ۱۳۶۱، نمبر ۱۰۱۰) للبيهقى اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مکہ جانے والے کو ہدی دیدے اور کسی خاص دن کا وعدہ لے لے اور اس دن حلال ہو جائے۔ انده امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ جس جگہ مصر ہوا ہے اس جگہ ہری ذبح کر دے حرم بھیجنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے وقال مالک و غیره ينحر هديه ويحلق فى اى موضع كان ولا قضاء عليه لان النبى الله واصحابه بالحديبية نحروا وحـلـقـوا وحلوا من كل شيء قبل الطواف وقبل ان يصل الهدى الى البيت ثم لم يذكر ان النبي الله امر احدا ان يقضى شيئا ولا يعودوا له والحديبية خارج من الحرم (د) (بخاری شریف، باب من قال ليس على الحصر بدل من ۲۳۳ نمبر ۱۸۱۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جہاں احصار ہوا ہے وہیں ہری ذبح کرے گا۔ کیونکہ صحابہ اور حضور نے حدیبیہ میں ہدی ذبح کی اور حدیبیہ حرم میں نہیں

حاشیہ : (الف) اور جو تم میں سے جان کر شکار کو تل کرے تو اس کا بدلہ اس کے مثل ہے جو قتل کیا جانور میں سے اس کا فیصلہ کرے دو انصاف در آدمی ہدی جو کعبہ تک پہنچنے والی ہو ( ب ) ابی میمون بن مہران بیان فرماتے ہیں کہ میں عمرہ کے لئے نکلا۔ پس این عباس کے پاس آیا اور ان کو پوچھا، انہوں نے فرمایا ہدی کو بدلو اس لئے کہ حضور نے اپنے صحابہ کوحکم دیا تھا کہ وہ ہی بدل دیں جو فر فر مایا تھا حدیبیہ کے سال عمرۃ القضا میں یعنی دوبارہ ہری ذبح کیا (ج) عبدالرحمن بن یزید نے فرمایا ہمارے ساتھ ایک آدمی نے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا۔ پس اس کو چھونے کاٹ لیا۔ پس کچھ سوار ظاہر ہوئے ان میں عبد اللہ بن مسعود تھے ان سے لوگوں نے پوچھا تو انہوں نے فرمایا ہری بھیجو اور تمہارے اور ان کے درمیان ایک دن متعین کر لو۔ پس جب وہ دن گزر جائے تو حلال ہو جائے (د) امام مالک اور ان کے علاوہ نے فرمایا ہادی تحرکرے اور جس جگہ چاہے حلق کرائے اور اس محصر پر قضا نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور اور ان کے اصحاب نے حدیبیہ میں تحرکیا اور ہر چیز سے حلال ہوئے طواف سے پہلے۔ اور بیت اللہ تک ہری پہنچنے سے پہلے۔ پھر کسی نے ذکر نہیں کیا کہ حضور نے کسی کو کچھ قضا کرنے کا حکم دیا ہو۔ اور نہ اس کی قضا کے لئے واپس ہوئے ہوں۔ اور حدیبیہ حرم سے باہر

Chapter of Ihsar. Book of Hajj. [7] (1) When the muhrim is prevented by an enemy or is afflicted with an illness that prevents him from proceeding, it is permissible for him to become halal. And it is said to him: send a goat to be slaughtered in the Haram. (In the Urdu commentary) Important note: Ihsar means being prevented from Hajj or Umrah. Its proof is this verse: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah. But if you are prevented, then [sacrifice] whatever offering is easy. And do not shave your heads until the offering reaches its place.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196) From this verse it is learned that if ihsar occurs, one should send the hady to the House of Allah and become halal. (2) The hadith evidence for ihsar is: 'Ibn Abbas said: The Messenger of Allah was prevented (uhsira), so he shaved his head, had intercourse with his wives, and sacrificed his hady, until he performed Umrah the following year.' (Sahih al-Bukhari) This hadith proves that ihsar can occur in Umrah, because the Prophet was prevented by the Quraysh disbelievers at Hudaybiyyah and was prevented from Umrah. [777] (1) When the muhrim is prevented by an enemy or is afflicted with an illness that prevents him from proceeding, it is permissible for him to become halal. And he will be told to send a goat to be slaughtered in the Haram. Ihsar can occur due to enemy or illness. In any case, if he cannot perform the acts of Hajj or Umrah for any reason, it will be ihsar. Now for him, he should send a goat to be slaughtered in the Haram, or give a goat to someone going and make a promise to slaughter on a specific day, and on that day the muhsar becomes halal. Just as ihsar occurs from enemy, similarly it occurs from illness. The proof for this is the hadith: 'I heard al-Hajjaj ibn Amr al-Ansari say: The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever breaks a bone or becomes lame, he has become halal, and upon him is Hajj the following year.' Ikrimah said: 'I asked Ibn Abbas and Abu Hurairah about that, and they said: He spoke the truth.' In another narration: 'or becomes ill.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) From this hadith it is learned that ihsar can occur not only from enemy but also from illness and broken bone. According to Imam al-Shafi'i, ihsar only occurs from enemy. His proof is the incident of Umrah and the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah in which only the enemy, the Quraysh of Mecca, caused ihsar. (2) From Ibn Abbas: 'There is no ihsar except the ihsar of the enemy.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) (Footnotes: ...) ... And it is said to him: send a goat to be slaughtered in the Haram. From this athar it is learned that only the enemy causes ihsar. The goat should be slaughtered in the Haram to open the ihram. Its proof is the verse: 'But if you are prevented, then [sacrifice] whatever offering is easy. And do not shave your heads until the offering reaches its place.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196) In this verse it is said: until the offering reaches its place, i.e., the Haram. The place of the hady is the Haram. Its proof is the verse: 'And whoever among you kills it intentionally, the penalty is an equivalent from cattle, judged by two just men among you, as an offering reaching the Ka'bah.' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:95) From this verse it is clear that the hady reaches the Ka'bah and is slaughtered there. Therefore, the hady of ihsar must be slaughtered in the Haram, then he becomes halal. (2) In a hadith: 'Abu Maymun ibn Mithran said: I went out for Umrah... then I came to Ibn Abbas and asked him. He said: Replace the hady, for the Messenger of Allah ordered his companions to replace the hady that they had sacrificed in the year of Hudaybiyyah during the Umrah of qada.' (Abu Dawud) This hadith states that the companions were ordered to re-sacrifice the animals they had slaughtered at Hudaybiyyah because that sacrifice was not valid. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, the hady of ihsar must be slaughtered in the Haram. (3) From Ibn Mas'ud regarding one who was stung while in ihram for Umrah and was prevented: 'Abdullah said: Send the hady and set a sign (amār) between you and it; when the hady is sacrificed in Mecca, this one becomes halal.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) From this athar it is learned that one should give the hady to someone going to Mecca and take a promise for a specific day, and on that day he becomes halal. As for Imam al-Shafi'i, his view is that he should sacrifice the hady at the place where he was prevented; there is no need to send it to the Haram. His proof is the hadith: 'Malik and others said: He should slaughter his hady and shave in any place, and there is no qada (make-up) upon him, because the Prophet and his companions at Hudaybiyyah slaughtered, shaved, and became halal from everything before tawaf and before the hady reached the House. Then it is not mentioned that the Prophet ordered anyone to make up anything or to return for it. And Hudaybiyyah is outside the Haram.' (Sahih al-Bukhari) From this athar it is learned that he will slaughter the hady where he was prevented, because the companions and the Prophet slaughtered the hady at Hudaybiyyah, and Hudaybiyyah is not in the Haram. (Footnotes: ...)
Source pages p. 471

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute on the causes of ihsar (prevention from completing Hajj/Umrah) and the place where the sacrificial animal (hady) must be slaughtered. The Hanafi school holds that ihsar can occur due to two causes: an enemy or an illness that physically prevents the muhrim from proceeding. In either case, it is permissible (ja'iz) for the muhrim to exit ihram (tahallul) by sending a goat to be slaughtered in the Haram (the sacred territory of Mecca), or by appointing someone to do so on a specified day. The text first cites the primary evidence: the Quranic verse (2:196) which commands completing Hajj and Umrah, but if prevented, to sacrifice an offering and not shave until it reaches its place (mahallahu). The Hanafis interpret 'its place' as the Haram. They also cite the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet was prevented at Hudaybiyyah and shaved, had intercourse, and sacrificed, then performed Umrah the next year. This establishes that ihsar applies to Umrah as well. A stronger proof is the hadith of al-Hajjaj ibn Amr that the Prophet said: 'Whoever breaks a bone or becomes lame, he has become halal, and upon him is Hajj the following year.' This explicitly includes physical ailments like broken bones and illness, not just enemy action. The Hanafis thus generalize the ruling to any cause that prevents completion. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i restricts ihsar to enemy prevention only. His evidence includes the report of Ibn Abbas that 'there is no ihsar except the ihsar of the enemy,' and the incident of Hudaybiyyah where only the enemy caused prevention. The Hanafi response is that the hadith of broken bone/illness is authentic and general, and the Hudaybiyyah incident was specific to that situation; the sacrifice performed there was later ordered to be replaced in the Haram, as shown in another hadith. On the place of sacrifice, the Hanafis insist it must be in the Haram, citing the Quranic verse 'reaching the Ka'bah' (5:95) and the command to replace the Hudaybiyyah sacrifices. The Shafi'is counter that the Prophet and his companions sacrificed outside the Haram at Hudaybiyyah and no qada was required, so the sacrifice can be done wherever one is prevented. The Hanafis interpret this as a special case, not a general rule. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the Hanafi view, which is based on stronger and more general proofs. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a Hanafi muhrim prevented by illness can become halal by sending a sacrifice to the Haram, while a Shafi'i in the same situation must either remain in ihram until able or sacrifice on the spot.

Key Terms
احصار (ihṣār): Prevention from completing the rites of Hajj or Umrah due to an enemy, illness, or any cause that physically prevents the muhrim from proceeding.
محرم (muḥrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah and is thus bound by its restrictions.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal (e.g., goat, sheep, cow, camel) sent to the Haram as an offering for the completion of Hajj or Umrah, especially in cases of ihsar.
حرم (ḥaram): The sacred territory around Mecca and Medina within which certain rituals must be performed and where the sacrifice must be slaughtered according to Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following can cause ihsar (prevention from completing Hajj/Umrah)?
A) Only an enemy blocking the route
B) Only illness that prevents travel
C) Both enemy and illness
D) Neither enemy nor illness

Key Takeaway
Ihsar in the Hanafi school includes both enemy and illness, and the required sacrifice must reach the Haram; this ruling is based on the Quran and authentic hadith.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Obligation to Send Hady to the Haram for the Muhsir
Establishes the ruling with evidence and refutes Shafi'i opinion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on where a muhsir must slaughter his hady and explain why the Shafi'i evidence from al-Hudaybiyyah does not override the Quranic command according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The muhsir's hady must reach the Haram — the Quranic 'mahall' is the Ka'bah, not the place of prevention.

This passage confronts a critical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: where should a pilgrim who is prevented (muhsir) from completing Hajj or Umrah slaughter his hady? The Hanafi position, grounded in explicit Quranic verses and the practice of the Companions, requires the hady to be sent to the Haram. As you work through this lesson, you will examine the proofs from both sides and understand why the Hanafi school holds to the Haram as the exclusive place of sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
First, clearly identify what the Hanafi school rules regarding the location of slaughter for the muhsir's hady.
The position is that the hady must be slaughtered in the Haram (Mecca or its precincts).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that the Shafi'i school disagrees and permits slaughter at the place where the pilgrim was prevented.
Imam al-Shafi'i's view is based on the incident at al-Hudaybiyyah.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the Shafi'i evidence: the Prophet and his companions slaughtered at al-Hudaybiyyah, which is outside the Haram, and no compensation was ordered.
This is a strong hadith-based argument.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand how the Hanafis address this proof: they argue that the Hudaybiyyah incident was a specific situation (truce) and that the general Quranic command requires the Haram; also, the companions were later ordered to repeat the sacrifice.
The Hanafis emphasize that the Quranic command is general and not abrogated by a single event.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: a muhsir who slaughters at the place of ihsar according to the Hanafi school has not fulfilled his obligation and remains in ihram, while the Shafi'i school would consider him halal.
This difference has real implications for pilgrims.

خامس ص ۲۱۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ صرف دشمن سے حصر ہوتا ہے۔ بکری حرم میں ذبح ہوتب احرام کھولے اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے فان احصرتم فما استيسر من الهدى ولا تحلقوا رؤوسكم حتى تبلغ الهدى محله ( آیت ۹۶ ۱ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں کہا گیا ہے کہ جب تک ہدی اپنی جگہ یعنی حرم میں نہ پہنچ جائے اپنا سر نہ منڈا واؤ۔ ہدی کی جگہ حرم ہے اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے ومن قتله منكم متعمدا فجزاء مثل ماقتل من النعم يحكم به ذوا عدل منكم هديا بالغ الكعبة (الف) ( آیت ۹۵ سورۃ المائدة ۵) اس آیت سے پتہ چلا کہ ہدی کعبہ تک پہنچے اور وہیں ذبیح ہو۔ اس لئے احصار کی ہدی بھی حرم میں ذبیح ہو تب حلال ہوگا (۲) حدیث میں ہے يحدث ابی میمون بن مهران قال خرجت معتمرا ... فاتيت ابن عباس فسألته فقال ابدل الهدى فان رسول الله امر اصحابه ان يبدلوا الهدى الذي نحروا عام الحديبية في عمرة القضاء (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب الاحصارص ۶۴ نمبر ۱۸۶۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ صحابہ نے صلح حدیبیہ میں جوقربانیاں حدیبیہ میں ذبح کی تھی اس کو دوبارہ ذبح کرنے کا حکم دیا۔ کیونکہ وہ قربانی ادا نہیں ہوئی۔ اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک احصار کی ہدی حرم ہی میں ذبح کرنا ہوگا (۳) عن ابن مسعود في الذي لدغ وهو محرم بالعمرة فاحصر فقال عبد الله ابعثوا بالهدى واجعلوا بينكم وبينه يوم امار فاذا ذبح الهدى بمكة حل هذا قال ابو عبيد قال الكسائي الامار العلامة (ج) ( سنن بیھقی ، باب من رای الاحلال بالا حصار بالمرض ج خاص ص ۱۳۶۱، نمبر ۱۰۱۰) للبيهقى اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ مکہ جانے والے کو ہدی دیدے اور کسی خاص دن کا وعدہ لے لے اور اس دن حلال ہو جائے۔ انده امام شافعی کے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ جس جگہ مصر ہوا ہے اس جگہ ہری ذبح کر دے حرم بھیجنے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے وقال مالک و غیره ينحر هديه ويحلق فى اى موضع كان ولا قضاء عليه لان النبى الله واصحابه بالحديبية نحروا وحـلـقـوا وحلوا من كل شيء قبل الطواف وقبل ان يصل الهدى الى البيت ثم لم يذكر ان النبي الله امر احدا ان يقضى شيئا ولا يعودوا له والحديبية خارج من الحرم (د) (بخاری شریف، باب من قال ليس على الحصر بدل من ۲۳۳ نمبر ۱۸۱۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جہاں احصار ہوا ہے وہیں ہری ذبح کرے گا۔ کیونکہ صحابہ اور حضور نے حدیبیہ میں ہدی ذبح کی اور حدیبیہ حرم میں نہیں
حاشیہ : (الف) اور جو تم میں سے جان کر شکار کو تل کرے تو اس کا بدلہ اس کے مثل ہے جو قتل کیا جانور میں سے اس کا فیصلہ کرے دو انصاف در آدمی ہدی جو کعبہ تک پہنچنے والی ہو ( ب ) ابی میمون بن مہران بیان فرماتے ہیں کہ میں عمرہ کے لئے نکلا۔ پس این عباس کے پاس آیا اور ان کو پوچھا، انہوں نے فرمایا ہدی کو بدلو اس لئے کہ حضور نے اپنے صحابہ کوحکم دیا تھا کہ وہ ہی بدل دیں جو فر فر مایا تھا حدیبیہ کے سال عمرۃ القضا میں یعنی دوبارہ ہری ذبح کیا (ج) عبدالرحمن بن یزید نے فرمایا ہمارے ساتھ ایک آدمی نے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا۔ پس اس کو چھونے کاٹ لیا۔ پس کچھ سوار ظاہر ہوئے ان میں عبد اللہ بن مسعود تھے ان سے لوگوں نے پوچھا تو انہوں نے فرمایا ہری بھیجو اور تمہارے اور ان کے درمیان ایک دن متعین کر لو۔ پس جب وہ دن گزر جائے تو حلال ہو جائے (د) امام مالک اور ان کے علاوہ نے فرمایا ہادی تحرکرے اور جس جگہ چاہے حلق کرائے اور اس محصر پر قضا نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور اور ان کے اصحاب نے حدیبیہ میں تحرکیا اور ہر چیز سے حلال ہوئے طواف سے پہلے۔ اور بیت اللہ تک ہری پہنچنے سے پہلے۔ پھر کسی نے ذکر نہیں کیا کہ حضور نے کسی کو کچھ قضا کرنے کا حکم دیا ہو۔ اور نہ اس کی قضا کے لئے واپس ہوئے ہوں۔ اور حدیبیہ حرم سے باہر ہے۔
ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ حرم کے علاوہ میں احصار کی بدی ذبح کی جاسکتی ہے۔
Book of Hajj. And it was said to him: send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram. Fifth p. 219) From this athar it became known that ihsar occurs only from an enemy. A goat slaughtered in the Haram, then he may open his ihram. Its proof is this verse: 'But if you are prevented, then [send] whatever offering is easy [to obtain], and do not shave your heads until the offering reaches its place [of sacrifice]' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196). In this verse it is said: until the hady reaches its place, i.e., the Haram, do not shave your head. The place of hady is the Haram. Its proof is this verse: 'And whoever kills it intentionally from among you, the penalty is an equivalent of what he killed from livestock, judged by two just men among you, as an offering reaching the Ka'bah' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:95). From this verse it is learned that the hady reaches the Ka'bah and is slaughtered there. Therefore, the hady of ihsar must also be slaughtered in the Haram; then he becomes halal. (2) There is a hadith: [I] heard Abu Maymun ibn Mihran say: I went out for Umrah... and I came to Ibn Abbas and asked him, and he said: Replace the hady, for the Messenger of Allah ordered his companions to replace the hady that they sacrificed in the year of al-Hudaybiyyah in the Umrah of al-Qada (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Ihsar, p. 64, no. 1864). In this hadith it is that the companions were ordered to sacrifice again the animals they slaughtered at al-Hudaybiyyah because that sacrifice was not fulfilled. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, the hady of ihsar must be slaughtered in the Haram. (3) From Ibn Mas'ud regarding one who was stung while in ihram for Umrah and was prevented: 'Abdullah said: Send the hady and set a sign between you and it on a day; when the hady is slaughtered in Mecca, he becomes halal. Abu 'Ubayd said: al-Kisa'i said: al-amar is the sign (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab man ra'a al-ihlal bi al-ihsar bi al-marad, j. khas, p. 1361, no. 1010). From this athar it is understood that one should give the hady to someone going to Mecca and take a promise for a specific day, and on that day he becomes halal. Now, according to Imam al-Shafi'i, he should slaughter the hady at the place where he was prevented; there is no need to send it to the Haram. Their proof is this hadith: And Malik and others said: He slaughters his hady and shaves his head in whatever place he is, and there is no compensation upon him, because the Prophet and his companions at al-Hudaybiyyah sacrificed and shaved and became halal from everything before tawaf and before the hady reached the House; then it is not mentioned that the Prophet ordered anyone to make up anything or to return for it, and al-Hudaybiyyah is outside the Haram (Bukhari, Bab man qala laysa 'ala al-hasr badal, p. 2233? no. 1813). From this athar it is understood that he will slaughter the hady where the ihsar occurred, because the companions and the Prophet sacrificed the hady at al-Hudaybiyyah, and al-Hudaybiyyah is not in the Haram. Footnote: (a) And whoever among you kills game intentionally, the compensation is the like of what he killed from cattle, judged by two just men among you, an offering reaching the Ka'bah. (b) Abu Maymun ibn Mihran says: I went out for Umrah... then I came to Ibn Abbas and asked him, he said: Replace the hady, because the Prophet ordered his companions to replace the hady that they sacrificed in the year of al-Hudaybiyyah in the Umrah of al-Qada, i.e., to sacrifice again. (c) 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Yazid said: A man with us tied ihram for Umrah, then a scorpion stung him. Then some riders appeared, among them 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud. The people asked him, and he said: Send the hady and set a day between you and them; when that day passes, become halal. (d) Imam Malik and others said: He slaughters the hady and shaves his head in whatever place he wishes, and there is no compensation upon this muhsir, because the Prophet and his companions at al-Hudaybiyyah sacrificed and became halal from everything before tawaf and before the hady reached the House of Allah. Then no one mentioned that the Prophet ordered anyone to make up anything, nor did they return for it, and al-Hudaybiyyah is outside the Haram. It is concluded from this that the hady of ihsar can be slaughtered outside the Haram.
Source pages p. 472

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the location of slaughtering the hady for a muhsir (one prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah). The author begins by stating the Hanafi ruling: the muhsir must send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram. He then provides multiple proofs. First, Quran 2:196 explicitly says not to shave until the hady reaches its place, and the 'place' is understood as the Haram. Second, Quran 5:95 indicates that the hady must reach the Ka'bah. Third, a hadith from Abu Dawud shows that the companions had to repeat their sacrifice because it was not done in the Haram. Fourth, an athar from Ibn Mas'ud instructs sending the hady to Mecca with a specific day. Then the Shafi'i position is presented: they allow slaughter at the place of ihsar, citing the example of the Prophet at al-Hudaybiyyah which is outside the Haram. The Hanafi response is implicit: the Prophet's action was a specific concession, but the general principle from the Quran requires the Haram. The footnote provides additional context. The concluding line clarifies that the Shafi'i evidence leads to permissibility outside the Haram.

Key Terms
احصار (ihsar): Prevention from completing Hajj or Umrah due to an enemy or illness.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal sent to the Haram by a pilgrim who is prevented (muhsir) or as a penalty.
محلل (mahall): The place where the hady is slaughtered, specifically the Haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where must the muhsir's hady be slaughtered?
A) At the place where he was prevented
B) In the Haram (Mecca or its precincts)
C) Anywhere he chooses
D) In his hometown

Key Takeaway
The muhsir must send the hady to the Haram; slaughtering at the place of ihsar is not sufficient according to the Hanafi school.

Sending Hady for the Muhsir and the Qarin
Explains the method of sending hady and the obligation for a qarin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the muhsir's obligation to appoint a specific day for his hady and explain the additional requirement for a qarin.

Core Idea
A muhsir must specify a slaughter day for his hady; a qarin must send two animals.

This passage addresses the practical scenario of a pilgrim prevented from completing Hajj (muhsir). The Hanafi school clarifies that the muhsir must appoint a carrier and specify a day for slaughter, becoming halal only after that. If he is a qarin (combining Hajj and Umrah), two animals are required because he exits two ihrams. These rulings are grounded in Quran, Sunnah, and athar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
For a muhsir, sending a hady is wajib. He must appoint a carrier and specify a day for slaughter.
This is from the Hanafi position box.
2
Understand the proof
The Quran (2:196) conditions shaving on the hady reaching its place; a hadith shows the Prophet sacrificed before shaving. The athar of Ibn Mas'ud supports specifying a day.
See dalil_block.
3
Apply to the qarin
A qarin has two ihrams, so he must send two animals to become halal from both.
Evidence from Malik and Ibrahim.
4
Recognize the consequence
Without specifying a day, the muhsir does not become halal until the animal is slaughtered on that day.
Common misunderstanding averted.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
The muhsir becomes halal only after the specified slaughter; the qarin must send two animals.
Mufta bihi.

Source Text

۷۷۸) (۲) یا وعدہ کرائے اس آدمی کو جو بکری لے جائے ایک متعین دن کا جس میں بکری ذبح کرے پھر مصر حلال ہو جائے۔ ت محصر کسی آدمی کے ساتھ بکری حرم تک بھیجے اور اس سے وعدہ لے لے کہ کس دن اس بکری کو حرم میں ذبح کرے گا اس دن وہ حلال ہو جائے۔ کیونکہ بکری ذبح ہونے سے پہلے حلال ہونا حنفیہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ آیت میں ہے ولا تحلقوا رؤوسكم حتى يبلغ الهدى محله ( آیت ۹۶ اسورة البقرة ٢) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جب تک ہدی ذبح نہ ہو سرمت منڈاؤ (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے پہلے ہدی نحر کی پھر حلق کروایا عن المسوران رسول الله الله نحر قبل ان يحلق وامر اصحابه بذلک (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الخر قبل الحلق في الحصر ص ۲۴۲۳ نمبر ۱۸۱) اس حدیث میں آپ نے فرمایا پہلے ہدی کا تحر کرو پھر سر منڈواؤ۔ اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک پہلے حر کرنے پھر حلق کرائے (۳) او پر عبداللہ بن مسعود کا اثر گزرا جس میں ہے کہ جس کے ساتھ ہدی بھیجے اس سے متعین دن کا وعدہ لے لے، اور اس دن محصر حلال ہو جائے ( سفن البیہقی ، نمبر ۱۰۱۰) ۷۷۹ (۳) پس اگر محصر قارن ہو تو دودم بھیجے۔ قارن دو احرام باندھے ہوئے ہے۔ ایک احرام حج کا اور ایک احرام عمرے کا اس لئے دو احرام سے حلال ہونے کے لئے دو دم بھیجنا پڑے گا۔ قال مالک و من قرن الحج والعمرة ثم فاته الحج فعليه ان يحج قابلا ويقرن بين الحج والعمرة ويهدى هدين هديا لقرانه الحج مع العمرة وهديا لما فاته من الحج (موطا امام مالک، باب ہدی من فاته ص ۴۰۶ (۲) دوسرے اثر میں ہے عن ابراهیم قال هدیان (ب) مصنف ابن ابی شیبه ۱۸ ما یجب علیه من الهدی اذا جمع بینھما فاحصر، باب الاحصارص ۵۹، ج ثالث . ص ۱۳۳، نمبر ۱۲۷۹۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ قارن محصر ہو جائے تو دو ہدی لازم ہوگی۔
(2) Or he makes an appointment with the person who will carry it for a specific day on which he will slaughter it, then he becomes halal. So the muhsir sends a goat with a person to the Haram and takes a promise from him as to which day he will slaughter the goat in the Haram; on that day he becomes halal. Because becoming halal before the goat is slaughtered is not permissible according to the Hanafis, due to the verse: 'And do not shave your heads until the hady reaches its place' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196). In this verse it is said: until the hady is slaughtered, do not shave your head. (2) There is a hadith that the Prophet first sacrificed the hady and then had his head shaved: from al-Miswar that the Messenger of Allah sacrificed before shaving and ordered his companions to do that (Bukhari, Bab al-Nahr qabl al-Halaq fi al-Hasr, p. 2423? no. 181). In this hadith the Prophet said: first sacrifice the hady, then shave your head. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, one first sacrifices then shaves. (3) And above, the athar of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud passed, in which he said: with the one who sends the hady, take a promise for a specific day, and on that day the muhsir becomes halal (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, no. 1010). (3) So if the muhsir is a qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah), he sends two animals. The qarin has tied two ihrams: one for Hajj and one for Umrah. Therefore, to become halal from two ihrams, he must send two animals. Malik said: And whoever combines Hajj and Umrah and then misses Hajj, he must perform Hajj the next year and combine Hajj and Umrah and offer two hadys: one for combining Hajj with Umrah and one for missing Hajj (Muwatta Imam Malik, Bab Hady man Fatahu, p. 406). (2) Another athar: from Ibrahim, he said: two hadys (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, 18, ma yajibu 'alayhi min al-hady idha jama'a baynahuma fa-ihsar, Bab al-Ihsar, p. 59, j. thalith, p. 133, no. 12796). This athar states that if a qarin becomes muhsir, two hadys are obligatory.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage provides two specific details about the muhsir's hady. First, the muhsir must appoint a person to carry the hady to the Haram and specify a day on which the animal will be slaughtered. He becomes halal only on that day after the slaughter, not before, as proven by Quran 2:196 and a hadith from Bukhari showing the Prophet sacrificed before shaving. The athar of Ibn Mas'ud also supports this. Second, if the muhsir is a qarin (someone in ihram for both Hajj and Umrah), he must send two sacrificial animals because he is exiting from two ihrams. This is supported by a hadith from Malik's Muwatta and an athar from Ibrahim. Both rulings are based on naqli evidence and are consistent with the Hanafi position that the hady must be slaughtered in the Haram before the muhsir can become halal.

Key Terms
قارن (qarin): A pilgrim who combines Hajj and Umrah in one ihram with the intention of performing both.
دم (dam): Blood, specifically a sacrificial animal required as a penalty or for ihsar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many sacrificial animals must a qarin muhsir send according to the Hanafi school?
A) One animal
B) Two animals
C) Three animals
D) None, because a qarin is not considered muhsir

Key Takeaway
The muhsir must ensure his hady is slaughtered on a specified day before he becomes halal; a qarin must send two animals.

Location of Muhsir's Hady: Slaughter Must Be in the Haram
Confirms location in Haram for muhsir's hady.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that the muhsir's hady must be slaughtered in the Haram and identify the Quranic evidence for this.

Core Idea
The muhsir's hady is valid only if slaughtered within the Haram.

This lesson focuses on the first part of the passage: the mandatory location for slaughtering the muhsir's hady. Understanding this is essential because slaughtering outside the Haram does not fulfil the obligation and the muhsir remains in ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is slaughtering the dam of ihsar (muhsir's hady). The ruling is that it is wajib to slaughter in the Haram.
This applies to both the muhsir in Hajj and Umrah.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites the Quranic verse: 'And do not shave your heads until the hady reaches its place' (2:196). The word 'mahillahu' refers to the Haram.
The hadith mentioned earlier also supports this.
3
Understand the consequence
If the muhsir slaughters outside the Haram, he does not become halal; he remains in ihram until a valid slaughter is performed in the Haram.
This is a matter of fardh (obligation) according to some variations, but here it is treated as wajib.

[۷۸۰] (۴) اور نہیں جائز ہے احصار کے دم کا ذبح کرنا مگر حرم میں ۔ احصار کا دم حرم میں ذبح کرے، اس کے علاوہ میں ذبح کرنے سے حلال نہیں ہوگا۔ اوپر گزر چکی ہے آیت بھی اور حدیث بھی۔ ولا تحلقوا رؤوسكم حتى يبلغ الهدى محله ( آیت ۹۶، سورة البقرة ٢) [۷۸۱] (۵) اور جائز ہے احصار کی ہدی کا ذبح کرنا یوم انحر سے پہلے ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین نے فرمایا حج کے محصر کی ہدی کو ذبح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے مگر دسویں ذی الحجہ کو۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے حلق کرنے سے پہلے فرفرمایا اور صحابہ کو بھی اس کا حکم فرمایا (ب) حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا قارن پر دوہری ہیں۔
[780] (4) And it is not permissible to slaughter the dam of ihsar except in the Haram. The dam of ihsar must be slaughtered in the Haram; outside it, slaughtering does not make him halal. The verse and hadith have already passed: 'And do not shave your heads until the hady reaches its place' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196). [781] (5) And it is permissible to slaughter the hady of ihsar before Yawm al-Nahr according to Abu Hanifa, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not permissible for the muhsir of Hajj to slaughter except on the tenth of Dhu al-Hijjah. Footnote: (a) The Prophet ordered shaving after sacrificing, and ordered his companions to do that. (b) Ibrahim said: on the qarin are two hadys.
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings. First, it reaffirms that the dam of ihsar must be slaughtered in the Haram, citing the same Quranic verse as before. Second, it presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of slaughter for the muhsir in Hajj. According to Abu Hanifa, the slaughter may take place before Yawm al-Nahr (the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah). However, the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the muhsir's hady can only be slaughtered on the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah itself. The commentary notes that other evidence has been mentioned earlier. The footnotes add supporting evidence for the order of sacrifice before shaving and the obligation of two hadys for a qarin.

Key Terms
محصر (muhsir): One who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah.
ہدی (hady): The sacrificial animal offered during Hajj, including for the muhsir.
حرم (Haram): The sacred precinct around Makkah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The muhsir's hady must be slaughtered within the Haram; otherwise, he remains in ihram.

Timing of Muhsir's Hady: Abu Hanifa's View vs. Sahibayn
Presents intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of muhsir's hady.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the timing of the muhsir's hady and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa allows the muhsir to slaughter before Yawm al-Nahr; the Sahibayn restrict it to the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah.

This lesson addresses the second part of the passage: a disagreement between the three main Hanafi imams on when the muhsir may slaughter. Understanding this ikhtilaf helps you apply the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The issue is the timing of slaughtering the hady for a muhsir in Hajj (one prevented from completing Hajj).
This does not apply to a muhsir in Umrah, as different rules may apply.
2
State Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa holds that the muhsir may slaughter before Yawm al-Nahr (the 10th of Dhu al-Hijjah).
His reasoning: the muhsir is not performing the Hajj rituals, so his sacrifice is not tied to the Hajj days.
3
State the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the muhsir's slaughter is only valid on Yawm al-Nahr itself.
Their reasoning: the muhsir's sacrifice is a substitute for the Hajj sacrifice, which is fixed to that day.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi school gives preference to Abu Hanifa's view; the muhsir may slaughter at any time after being prevented, even before the 10th.
This is more practical for the muhsir who may become halal earlier.
