Sending a Sacrificial Animal with a Promise of Slaughter
Ruling on muhsir sending hady with appointed day

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for a muhsir to become halal by sending a hady with a promised day of slaughter, and differentiate the ruling for a qarin.

Core Idea
A muhsir must send a hady to the Haram and promise a day for its slaughter; only then does he become halal.

This passage addresses the situation of a person prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah (muhsir). It provides the Hanafi ruling on how such a person becomes halal—by sending a sacrificial animal (hady) to the Haram with a promise of slaughter on a specific day. The ruling is supported by Quranic verse and Prophetic practice. The passage also covers the case of a qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) and the requirement that the slaughter must occur within the Haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person and the act
The muhsir is the one prevented from completing Hajj/Umrah. He must send a hady (sacrificial animal) to the Haram.
Hanafis consider muhsir includes any prevention, not just enemy.
2
Understand the promise requirement
The muhsir must promise the carrier a specific day for slaughter. This synchronization ensures the muhsir becomes halal exactly when the animal is sacrificed.
The word 'واعد' indicates a binding promise (wajib).
3
Analyze the proof
Quran 2:196 commands not to shave until the hady reaches its place. The Prophet (SAW) sacrificed before shaving, as recorded in Bukhari. This establishes the order: sacrifice then shave.
The particle 'حتى' makes the hady’s arrival a condition for shaving.
4
Differentiate for the qarin
A qarin has tied two ihrams (Hajj and Umrah). Therefore, he must send two hadys—one for each—to become fully halal.
Athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha‘i and Malik’s view support this.
5
Note the location of slaughter
The hady must be slaughtered within the Haram (Mecca’s sacred precinct). Slaughtering elsewhere does not release the muhsir from ihram.
This is derived from the same verse: 'until the hady reaches its place'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعد من يحملها يوما بعينه يذبحها فيه ثم تحلل
یا وعدہ کرائے اس آدمی کو جو بکری لے جائے ایک متعین دن کا جس میں بکری ذبح کرے پھر محصر حلال ہو جائے۔ محصر کسی آدمی کے ساتھ بکری حرم تک بھیجے اور اس سے وعدہ لے لے کہ کس دن اس بکری کو حرم میں ذبح کرے گا اس دن وہ حلال ہو جائے۔ کیونکہ بکری ذبح ہونے سے پہلے حلال ہونا حنفیہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ آیت میں ہے ولا تحلقوا رؤوسكم حتى يبلغ الهدى محله (آیت ۹۶ سورة البقرة) اس آیت میں ہے کہ جب تک ہدی ذبح نہ ہو سر نہ منڈاؤ۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے پہلے ہدی نحر کی پھر حلق کروایا عن المسور أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نحر قبل أن يحلق وأمر أصحابه بذلك (بخاری شریف، باب النحر قبل الحلق في الحصر ص ۲۴۲۳ نمبر ۱۸۱) اس حدیث میں آپ نے فرمایا پہلے ہدی کا نحر کرو پھر سر منڈواؤ۔ اس لئے حنفیہ کے نزدیک پہلے نحر کرنے پھر حلق کرائے۔ اوپر عبدالله بن مسعود کا اثر گزرا جس میں ہے کہ جس کے ساتھ ہدی بھیجے اس سے متعین دن کا وعدہ لے لے، اور اس دن محصر حلال ہو جائے (سنن البیہقی، نمبر ۱۰۱۰)

فإن كان قارنا بعث دمین
پس اگر محصر قارن ہو تو دو دم بھیجے۔ قارن دو احرام باندھے ہوئے ہے۔ ایک احرام حج کا اور ایک احرام عمرے کا اس لئے دو احرام سے حلال ہونے کے لئے دو دم بھیجنا پڑے گا۔ قال مالک: و من قرن الحج والعمرة ثم فاته الحج فعليه أن يحج قابلا ويقرن بين الحج والعمرة ويهدي هدين هديا لقرانه الحج مع العمرة وهديا لما فاته من الحج (موطأ الإمام مالک، باب هدي من فاته ص ۴۰۶) دوسرے اثر میں ہے عن إبراهیم قال: هدیان (مصنف ابن أبي شیبة، باب ما يجب عليه من الهدي إذا جمع بينهما فاحصر، باب الإحصار ص ۵۹، ج ثالث ص ۱۳۳، نمبر ۱۲۷۹۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ قارن محصر ہو جائے تو دو ہدی لازم ہوگی۔

ولا يجوز ذبح دم الإحصار إلا في الحرم
اور نہیں جائز ہے احصار کے دم کا ذبح کرنا مگر حرم میں۔ احصار کا دم حرم میں ذبح کرے، اس کے علاوہ میں ذبح کرنے سے حلال نہیں ہوگا۔ اوپر گزر چکی ہے آیت بھی اور حدیث بھی۔ ولا تحلقوا رؤوسكم حتى يبلغ الهدى محله (آیت ۹۶، سورة البقرة)
And make a promise to the one who carries it for a specific day on which he slaughters it, then he becomes halal. Or make a promise to the person who takes the goat, appoint a specific day on which he slaughters the goat, then the muhsir becomes halal. The muhsir sends a goat with a person to the Haram and takes a promise from him on which day he will slaughter the goat in the Haram; on that day he becomes halal. Because becoming halal before the goat is slaughtered is not permissible according to the Hanafis. Because the verse says: 'And do not shave your heads until the hady reaches its place of sacrifice' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196). This verse indicates: do not shave your head until the hady is slaughtered. The hadith states that the Prophet (peace be upon him) first sacrificed the hady and then had his head shaved: from al-Miswar that the Messenger of Allah sacrificed before shaving and commanded his companions to do that (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter on sacrificing before shaving in ihsar, p. 2423 no. 181). In this hadith he said: first perform the sacrifice of the hady, then shave your head. Therefore, according to the Hanafis, one should first sacrifice then shave. And the athar of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud has passed that one should take a promise from the one with whom he sends the hady for a specific day, and on that day the muhsir becomes halal (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, no. 1010). Then if he is a qarin, he sends two animals. So if the muhsir is a qarin, he sends two sacrificial animals. The qarin has tied two ihrams: one for Hajj and one for Umrah. Therefore, to become halal from two ihrams, he must send two animals. Malik said: Whoever combines Hajj and Umrah and then misses Hajj must perform Hajj the next year and combine Hajj and Umrah and sacrifice two animals: one for combining Hajj with Umrah and one for what he missed of Hajj (Muwatta Imam Malik, chapter on hady of one who missed Hajj, p. 406). Another athar: from Ibrahim (al-Nakha'i): he said: two hadys (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on what is obligatory of hady when one combines them and then is prevented, section on ihsar, vol. 3, p. 133, no. 12796). This athar indicates that if a qarin becomes muhsir, two hadys become obligatory. And it is not permissible to slaughter the sacrificial animal of ihsar except in the Haram. And it is not permissible to slaughter the dam al-ihsar except in the Haram. The dam al-ihsar should be slaughtered in the Haram; slaughtering outside it does not make one halal. The verse and hadith have already passed: 'Do not shave your heads until the hady reaches its place of sacrifice' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196).

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof regarding the procedure for a person prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah (muhsir). It explains that such a person must send a sacrificial animal (hady) to the Haram and appoint a specific day for its slaughter, upon which he becomes halal. The proof is from the Quran (2:196) which commands not to shave until the hady reaches its destination, and from the Sunnah where the Prophet (SAW) sacrificed before shaving. Additionally, the Hanafis require a specific promise of a day for the sacrifice to ensure synchronization. The passage then addresses the case of a qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah combined), who must send two animals. It also emphasizes that the slaughter of the dam al-ihsar must occur within the Haram; slaughtering elsewhere does not suffice. These rules are based on the foundational principle that the hady must be slaughtered in the Haram to fulfill the condition for becoming halal.

Key Terms
محصر (muhsir): One who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to enemy, illness, or other obstacles.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal sent to the Haram by a muhsir or others in the context of Hajj/Umrah.

Slaughtering Dam al-Ihsar Before Yawm al-Nahr: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
An intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of sacrifice for muhsir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the timing of slaughtering dam al-ihsar for Hajj, explain their respective proofs, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
For a muhsir, Abu Hanifa permits slaughter before the 10th; Sahibayn restrict it to Yawm al-Nahr by analogy.

When a pilgrim is prevented from completing Hajj (muhsir), he must sacrifice a dam al-ihsar. But when can this sacrifice be performed? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) differed. In this passage, we explore their reasoning and discover the practical difference it makes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and the issue
Read the passage and note the position of Abu Hanifa and the position of the Sahibayn. The issue is whether the dam can be slaughtered before Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah).
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that dam al-ihsar is a type of dam kaffarah, linked only to the Haram, not to a specific day. Therefore, it can be slaughtered any time in the Haram before Yawm al-Nahr.
The key distinction: the dam is 'muqayyad bi al-Haram' not 'muqayyad bi al-zaman'.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn use qiyas: they analogize dam al-ihsar to the dams of qiran and tamattu', which are specifically slaughtered on Yawm al-Nahr. They argue that all three are similar as dams of Hajj.
The strength of analogy depends on whether the illa (cause) is the same.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if a muhsir slaughters before the 10th, is the sacrifice valid? According to Abu Hanifa, yes; according to Sahibayn, no, and an alternative slaughter would be required on Yawm al-Nahr.
This affects the pilgrim's obligations and costs.
5
Note the absence of tarjih
The passage does not state which view is mufta bihi. In later Hanafi practice, the Sahibayn's view often prevails, but students should recognize the difference.
Always check the authoritative source (Zahir al-Riwayah) for the relied-upon position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز ذبحه قبل يوم النحر عند أبي حنيفة وقالا لا يجوز الذبح للمحصر إلا في يوم النحر
حج کے احرام میں محصر ہوا تو دسویں ذی الحجہ سے پہلے بھی ہدی ذبح کر سکتا ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ حج کے احرام میں محصر ہوا تو دسویں ذی الحجہ سے پہلے ہدی ذبح نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ ایک قسم کا دم کفارہ ہے۔ اس وجہ سے اس کا گوشت کھانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور دم کفارہ حرم کے ساتھ تو خاص ہے، کسی متعین دن کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے دسویں ذی الحجہ کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس طرح دم قرآن اور دم تمتع دسویں ذی الحجہ کے ساتھ خاص ہے کہ اس سے پہلے ان کا ذبح کرنا جائز نہیں اسی طرح حج کا دم احصار بھی دسویں ذی الحجہ کے ساتھ خاص ہو گا کہ اس سے پہلے اس کا ذبح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
And it is permissible to slaughter it before the Day of Nahr according to Abu Hanifa, but the two companions said it is not permissible for the muhsir to slaughter except on the Day of Nahr. [Urdu: If he becomes muhsir in the ihram of Hajj, he can slaughter the hady before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn say that if he becomes muhsir in the ihram of Hajj, he cannot slaughter the hady before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The proof of Abu Hanifa is that this is a type of dam kaffarah (expiation), so its meat is not permissible to eat. And the dam kaffarah is specific to the Haram, not to any specific day. Therefore, it will not be specific to the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The proof of the Sahibayn is that just as the dam of qiran and tamattu' are specific to the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, so that slaughtering them before it is not permissible, similarly the dam al-ihsar for Hajj will be specific to the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, so that slaughtering it before is not permissible.]
Source pages p. 473

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the timing of slaughtering the sacrificial animal for a muhsir (one prevented from completing Hajj). The question is whether the dam al-ihsar for Hajj can be slaughtered before the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). Abu Hanifa permits it, arguing that this dam is a type of kaffarah (expiation) which is linked only to the Haram, not to a specific day. Therefore, it can be slaughtered at any time, as long as it is in the Haram. The Sahibayn analogize it to the dam of qiran and tamattu', which are specifically sacrificed on the Day of Nahr. They argue that the dam al-ihsar for Hajj shares the same ruling and thus should be restricted to the Day of Nahr. The commentary provides both proofs without stating which is mufta bihi, but typically the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that of the Sahibayn, but here the text does not specify.

Key Terms
دم كفارة (dam kaffarah): A sacrificial animal offered as expiation for a violation or omission during Hajj/Umrah.
يوم النحر (Yawm al-Nahr): The 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrifice in Hajj.
محصر (muhsir): A person in ihram who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to an obstacle such as enemy, illness, or lawful authority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why is dam al-ihsar for Hajj restricted to Yawm al-Nahr?
A) Because it is a type of dam kaffarah specific to the Haram
B) By analogy to the dams of qiran and tamattu'
C) Because the Quran explicitly specifies Yawm al-Nahr
D) Because the muhsir must wait for the Day of Sacrifice

Key Takeaway
The timing of slaughtering dam al-ihsar for Hajj is disputed within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa permits any time before Yawm al-Nahr in the Haram, while the Sahibayn restrict it to Yawm al-Nahr by qiyas.

Obligation to Repeat Hajj and Umrah for Muhsir
Ruling on muhsir with proofs from Sahaba and Hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of a muhsir for Hajj after becoming halal and identify the proofs for both Hajj and Umrah qada.

Core Idea
The muhsir for Hajj must perform both qada Hajj and Umrah; missed Umrah must also be made up.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: a person prevented (muhsir) from completing Hajj. Upon becoming halal, he is not only required to make up the Hajj but also to perform a separate Umrah. The author provides evidence from the actions of the Sahaba and hadith to support this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the qada (makeup) of Hajj and Umrah for a person who was muhsir (prevented) while in ihram for Hajj. The ruling is that both are wajib upon him after he becomes halal.
The ruling is derived from the source phrase 'فعليه حج وعمرة'.
2
Locate the proof from the Sahaba
The passage cites Umar ibn al-Khattab's command to those who missed Hajj to become halal with an Umrah and then perform Hajj the next year. This establishes the practice.
This is recorded in Muwatta Imam Malik.
3
Analyze the hadith of Aisha
The Prophet (PBUH) told Aisha that her Umrah at Tan'im was 'in place of your Umrah', showing that a missed Umrah must be made up.
This is from Sahih Bukhari.
4
Analyze the hadith of Ibn Umar
The Prophet (PBUH) said: 'Whoever misses Arafat at night has missed Hajj, so let him become halal with an Umrah, and upon him is Hajj the next year.' This combined the two obligations.
This is from Sunan al-Darqutni.
5
Derive the final ruling and note the ikhtilaf
From these proofs, the Hanafi school concludes that both qada Hajj and Umrah are wajib. Some other schools do not require the separate Umrah, but the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
The difference is legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمحصر بالحج إذا حل فعليه حج وعمرة
حج کا محصر اگر حلال ہو جائے تو اس پر حج ہے اور عمرہ ہے۔ حج کا احرام باندھا تھا اور احصار ہو گیا تو حج کے احصار کے بعد عمرہ کرے اور عمرہ نہ کر سکا تو آئندہ عمرہ کرے اور حج کے بدلے حج کی قضا کرے۔ تو گویا کہ حج کا محصر حج بھی کرے گا اور عمرہ بھی کرے گا۔
قال مالك: وأمر عمر بن الخطاب أبا أيوب الأنصاري وهبار بن الأسود حين فاتهما الحج وأتيا يوم النحر أن يحلا بعمرة ثم يرجعان حلالا ثم يحجان عاما قابلا ويهديان. فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلاثة أيام في الحج وسبعة إذا رجع إلى أهله. (موطأ الإمام مالك، باب ما جاء فيمن أحصر بغير عدو ص ۳۷۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حج فوت ہو جائے اور محصر مکہ مکرمہ میں ہو اور عمرہ کر سکتا ہو تو عمرہ کر کے حلال ہو جائے اور آئندہ سال حج قضا کرے۔ عمرہ کی قضا کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عائشة قالت: خرجنا مع النبي ... أرسلني النبي مع عبد الرحمن بن أبي بكر إلى التنعيم فاعتمرت فقال هذه مكان عمرتك. (بخاری شریف، باب کیف تفعل الحائض والنفساء ص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۱۵۵۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عمرہ چھوٹ جائے تو قضا کرنا ہوگا۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عمر أن رسول الله قال: من وقف بعرفات بليل فقد أدرك الحج ومن فاته عرفات بليل فقد فاته الحج فليحل بعمرة وعليه الحج من قابل. (دارقطنی، کتاب الحج حج ثانی ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۲۴۹۶)
And the muhsir for Hajj, when he becomes halal, then upon him is Hajj and Umrah. [Urdu: If the muhsir of Hajj becomes halal, then upon him is Hajj and Umrah. He had tied the ihram of Hajj and was prevented. After the ihsar of Hajj, he should perform Umrah, and if he cannot perform Umrah, then he should perform it later, and he should make up the Hajj in place of the missed one. So it is as if the muhsir of Hajj will perform both Hajj and Umrah. Malik said: Umar ibn al-Khattab commanded Abu Ayyub al-Ansari and Hubbar ibn al-Aswad, when they missed Hajj and came on the Day of Nahr, to make halal with an Umrah, then return as halal, then perform Hajj the next year and sacrifice. Whoever cannot find an animal should fast three days during Hajj and seven when he returns to his family. (Muwatta Imam Malik) This athar shows that if the Hajj is missed and the muhsir is in Makkah and can perform Umrah, he should perform Umrah to become halal, and make up Hajj the next year. The proof for making up Umrah is the hadith from Aisha: she said: We went out with the Prophet... the Prophet sent me with Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr to al-Tan'im, and I performed Umrah, and he said: This is in place of your Umrah. (Bukhari) This hadith shows that if Umrah is missed, it must be made up. Also the hadith from Ibn Umar: The Prophet said: Whoever stays at Arafat at night has caught Hajj, and whoever misses Arafat at night has missed Hajj, so let him become halal with an Umrah, and upon him is Hajj the next year. (Darqutni)]
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for a person who becomes a muhsir (prevented) while in the state of ihram for Hajj. Once he becomes halal (either by completing the conditions or being released), he is obligated to perform both a full Hajj (as qada') and an Umrah. The reasoning is that his initial ihram was for Hajj, but due to prevention, he could not complete it. He must now make up the missed Hajj in a subsequent year. Additionally, he must perform an Umrah because the original intention (or the Sunnah) includes it, or because he should combine Hajj and Umrah when making up. The passage cites the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab and hadith evidence that he who misses Hajj should become halal with Umrah and then perform Hajj the next year. The hadith from Aisha shows that if Umrah is missed, it must be made up. The ruling is consistent with the Hanafi position that both Hajj and Umrah are obligations that must be fulfilled.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed or invalid religious obligation later.
حل (hall): Becoming halal, i.e., exiting the state of ihram.
محصر (muhsir): A person who has entered ihram but is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to an obstacle (enemy, illness, etc.).
إحصار (ihsar): Prevention from completing Hajj or Umrah after entering ihram.

Key Takeaway
A muhsir for Hajj must perform both a makeup Hajj and a makeup Umrah.

When to Slaughter the Hady for a Muhsar?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of sacrifice for muhsar in Hajj.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on timing of sacrifice for a muhsar in Hajj and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
The muhsar's sacrifice is a kaffarah tied to the Haram, not to the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.

This passage addresses a disagreement within the Hanafi school: when exactly should a person prevented from completing Hajj (muhsar) slaughter the hady? Imam Abu Hanifa allows it before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, while his two foremost disciples restrict it to the 10th. Understanding their proofs will clarify the nature of this sacrifice and which ruling is relied upon in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the issue and the two positions
Identify the exact legal question: is the muhsar for Hajj permitted to slaughter the hady before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah? Then state Abu Hanifa's view (yes) and the Sahibayn's view (no).
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa argues that the dam for ihsar is a kaffarah (expiation). Kaffarah is tied only to the Haram, not to a specific day. Therefore, the sacrifice can be performed any time after ihsar, even before the 10th.
Key point: the nature of the dam as kaffarah detaches it from the specific timing of Hajj rituals.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn analogize the dam ihsar to dam qiran and dam tamattu, which are specifically tied to the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. Thus, by qiyas, the dam ihsar must also be on the 10th.
This qiyas is based on the common factor of being a sacrifice related to Hajj.
4
Examine the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn
The Hanafi response (implicit in Abu Hanifa's view) is that the analogy fails because dam qiran and tamattu are connected to the actions of Hajj itself, whereas dam ihsar is a compensation for being prevented—it is not a ritual of Hajj but a penalty.
Identifying the distinguishing factor (farq) that breaks the analogy.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Although the Sahibayn's view is recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah, later Hanafi authorities (e.g., Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah) prefer Abu Hanifa's view. The mufta bihi is that the muhsar may slaughter before the 10th.
Tarjih reason: Abu Hanifa's view is more facilitative and aligns with the nature of kaffarah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۸۳ (۷) والمحصر بالحج حج کے احرام میں محصر ہوا تو دسویں ذی الحجہ سے پہلے بھی ہری ذبح کر سکتا ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ حج کے احرام میں محصر ہوا تو دسویں ذی الحجہ سے پہلے ہدی ذریع نہیں کر سکتا ہے۔ ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ ایک قسم کا دم کفارہ ہے۔ اس وجہ سے اس کا گوشت کھانا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور دم کفارہ حرم کے ساتھ تو خاص ہے، کسی متعین دن کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے دسویں ذی الحجہ کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس طرح دم قرآن اور دم تمتع دسویں ذی الحجہ کے ساتھ خاص ہے کہ اس سے پہلے ان کا ذبح کرنا جائز نہیں اسی طرح حج کا دم احصار بھی دسویں ذی الحجہ کے ساتھ خاص ہو گا کہ اس سے پہلے اس کا ذبیح کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
(7) And the one prevented in hajj: if he becomes prevented in the ihram of hajj, then before the tenth of Dhul Hijjah he may also slaughter the hady according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And the Two Companions say that if he becomes prevented in the ihram of hajj, he cannot slaughter the hady before the tenth of Dhul Hijjah. The proof of Abu Hanifa is that this is a type of dam kaffarah (expiatory blood). For this reason, eating its meat is not permissible. And dam kaffarah is specific to the Haram, not to any particular day. Therefore it will not be tied to the tenth of Dhul Hijjah. And the proof of the Two Companions is that just as dam quran and dam tamattu are specific to the tenth of Dhul Hijjah, such that slaughtering them before it is not permissible, similarly, the dam ihsar for hajj will also be specific to the tenth of Dhul Hijjah, such that slaughtering it before it is not permissible.
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of the sacrificial animal (hady) for a person who is prevented (muhsar) from completing Hajj. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the sacrifice can be performed any time after the ihsar, even before the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, because the dam is a kaffarah (expiation) and kaffarah is only tied to the Haram, not to a specific day. The two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, analogize it to the dam for qiran and tamattu, which are only sacrificed on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. According to them, the dam ihsar for hajj must also be on the 10th. The passage explains both proofs without giving a preference, though later Hanafi fatwa often follows Abu Hanifa. The ruling for 'umrah is then mentioned: the muhsar for 'umrah can sacrifice whenever, as 'umrah is not time-restricted.

Key Terms
مُحْصَر (muḥṣar): A person who is prevented from completing Hajj or 'Umrah due to an enemy, illness, or other obstacle.
هَدْي (hady): The sacrificial animal offered by a pilgrim, especially in compensation for ihsar.
صاحبین (ṣāḥibayn): Referring to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two foremost disciples of Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah
B) Any time after the ihsar, before or after the 10th
C) Only after returning home
D) Only inside the Haram

Key Takeaway
The muhsar's sacrifice for Hajj is a kaffarah tied only to the Haram, so Abu Hanifa permits it before the 10th, and this is the relied-upon view.

Qada for the Muhsar: Both Hajj and 'Umrah Required
States that a muhsar for hajj must make up both hajj and 'umrah, with supporting proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a muhsar of Hajj and identify the three proofs that establish qada for both Hajj and 'Umrah.

Core Idea
A muhsar must sacrifice to exit ihram and later perform qada of both Hajj and 'Umrah.

This lesson examines the ruling for a person who is prevented (muhsar) from completing their obligatory Hajj. The Hanafi school holds that such a person must not only sacrifice to exit ihram but also later make up both the Hajj and the 'Umrah. We will trace the evidence from the hadith of Aisha, the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, and the hadith of Ibn Umar, which collectively establish the wajib nature of qada for both rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is the qada (make-up) of Hajj and 'Umrah for a muhsar. The ruling is that both are wajib.
The muhsar is one prevented by an enemy or other force.
2
Locate the first dalil
The hadith of Aisha: the Prophet told her that her 'Umrah from Tan'im was 'in place of your 'Umrah', indicating that a missed 'Umrah must be replaced.
This shows qada for 'Umrah is required.
3
Locate the second dalil
The athar of Umar ibn al-Khattab: he commanded two companions who missed Hajj to perform 'Umrah and then make up Hajj the next year.
This shows both 'Umrah and Hajj qada.
4
Locate the third dalil
The hadith of Ibn Umar: the Prophet said whoever misses Arafat must perform 'Umrah and then Hajj the next year.
Directly supports qada for both.
5
Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
Other schools differ: e.g., Malik holds only obligatory Hajj requires qada, not 'Umrah. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
The dispute centers on whether 'Umrah becomes wajib upon ihram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۸۳] (۷) حض کا محصر اگر حلال ہو جائے تو اس پر حج ہے اور عمرہ ہے۔ حج کا احرام باندھا تھا اور احصار ہو گیا تو حج کے احصار کے بعد عمرہ کرے اور عمرہ نہ کر سکا تو آئندہ عمرہ کرے اور حج کے بدلے حج کی قضا کرے۔ تو گویا کہ حج کا محصر حج بھی کرے گا اور عمرہ بھی کرے گا۔
قال مالك وقد امر بن الخطاب ابا ايوب الانصارى وهبار بن الاسود حين فاتهما الحج واتيا يوم النحر ان يحلا بعمرة ثم يرجعان حلالا ثم يحجان عاما قابلا ويهديان فمن لم يجد فصيام ثلثة ايام في الحج و سبعة اذا رجع الى اهله (موطا امام مالک، باب ما جاء فیمین احصر بغیر عدوس ۳۷۹) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حج فوت ہو جائے اور مخصر مکہ مکرمہ میں ہو اور عمرہ کر سکتا ہو تو عمرہ کر کے حلال ہو جائے اور آئندہ سال حج قضا کرے۔ عمرہ کی قضا کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عائشة قالت خرجنا مع النبي الله ... ارسلني النبي مع عبد الرحمن بن ابى بكر الى التنعيم فاعتمرت فقال هذه مكان عمرتك (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب کیف تفعل الحائض والنفساء ص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۱۵۵۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عمرہ چھوٹ جائے تو قضا کرنا ہوگا (۳) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عمر ان رسول الله الله الله قال من وقف بعرفات بليل فقد ادرك الحج ومن فاته عرفات بليل فـقـد فـاتـه الـحـج فليحل بعمرة وعليه الحج من قابل (ب) (دار قطنی ، کتاب الحج حج ثانی ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۲۴۹۶ رسن للبیھقی ، باب ما
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں کہ میں حضور کے ساتھ لگی مجھ کو حضور نے عبد الرحمن کے ساتھ تعظیم بھیجا، پس میں نے عمرہ کیا۔ پس آپ نے فرمایا یہ تیرے عمرہ کی جگہ پر ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا جو عرفات میں رات میں ٹھہرا ہو تو حج پالیا۔ اور جس نے رات تک میں عرفات فوت ہو گیا تو اس سے حج (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )
(7) If the muhsar for hajj becomes halal (released), then upon him is hajj and 'umrah. He had tied the ihram of hajj and was prevented, so after the ihsar of hajj, he should perform 'umrah, and if he could not perform 'umrah, then later he should perform 'umrah, and in place of hajj, he should perform qada of hajj. So it is as if the muhsar for hajj will perform both hajj and 'umrah. Malik said: Umar ibn al-Khattab commanded Abu Ayyub al-Ansari and Hubar ibn al-Aswad, when hajj was missed by them and they came on the day of Nahr, that they should become halal with 'umrah, then return as halal, then perform hajj the next year and sacrifice, and whoever cannot find (a sacrifice) should fast three days during hajj and seven when he returns to his family. From this athar it is understood that when hajj is missed and the muhsar is in Mecca and can perform 'umrah, he should do 'umrah and become halal, and the next year perform qada of hajj. The proof for qada of 'umrah is this hadith: from Aisha... The Prophet sent me with Abd al-Rahman to Tan'im, so I performed 'umrah, and he said: 'This is in place of your 'umrah.' From this hadith it is understood that if 'umrah is missed, qada must be performed. Another hadith: from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever stands at Arafat at night has obtained hajj, and whoever misses Arafat at night has missed hajj, so let him become halal with 'umrah, and upon him is hajj next year.'
Source pages p. 474

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling that a person prevented (muhsar) from completing Hajj must later perform both Hajj and 'Umrah as a make-up (qada). The author explains that if the ihram was for Hajj and one is prevented, one should exit ihram by performing 'Umrah (if possible) and then later perform a full Hajj. The evidence includes the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab (as reported by Imam Malik) and a hadith of Aisha where the Prophet told her that her 'Umrah from Tan'im was a replacement for a missed 'Umrah. Another hadith from Ibn Umar indicates that if one misses the standing at Arafat, one must perform 'Umrah and then make up the Hajj the following year. The footnote further clarifies that the hadith of Aisha shows that 'Umrah, even if nafilah, becomes wajib once the ihram is tied, thus requiring qada upon missing it. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
قَضَاء (qaḍāʾ): The performance of a missed obligatory act after its time, especially Hajj and 'Umrah due to ihsar.
مُحْصَر (muḥṣar): One physically prevented by an enemy or other force from completing pilgrimage.
عارَفات (ʿArafāt): The plain near Mecca where pilgrims stand on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; standing is a rukn of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a person who is prevented (muhsar) from completing their obligatory Hajj do?
A) Only sacrifice an animal and no further action is needed
B) Sacrifice an animal and perform both Hajj and 'Umrah as qada later
C) Only perform 'Umrah as qada, not Hajj
D) Perform Hajj again without sacrificing

Key Takeaway
A muhsar for Hajj must sacrifice to exit ihram and then perform qada of both Hajj and 'Umrah as a wajib obligation.

intermediate
6 min
Qada for Muhsar in 'Umrah: Obligation and Proof
Ruling on qada for muhsar in 'Umrah with proof and Maliki counterargument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qada for a muhsar in 'Umrah and explain the proof from the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
A missed 'Umrah must be made up because ihram makes it binding—even if originally voluntary.

This lesson addresses a specific rule: a person prevented (muhsar) from completing 'Umrah after entering ihram must make it up (qada). We will examine the Hanafi proof from the hadith of Aisha and contrast it with the Maliki view that only obligatory Hajj requires qada. Understanding this ruling reinforces the principle that initiating an act of worship imposes obligations that cannot be abandoned lightly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The passage states that qada is necessary (lazim) for a muhsar of 'Umrah. Determine the hukm level: is it fard, wajib, or sunnah?
Hanafis classify this as wajib, not fard, because the proof is from ahad hadith.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Aisha from Bukhari. Identify the key part: the Prophet sent her to Tan'im to perform 'Umrah and said 'this is in place of your 'Umrah' (hādhihi makānu 'umratik).
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), which in Hanafi usul gives wujub, not fardiyyah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the obligation of qada? The Prophet's statement implies that a missed 'Umrah must be replaced by another 'Umrah. The author emphasizes that even though Aisha's original 'Umrah was nafl, after entering ihram it became wajib to complete or make up.
This is the Hanafi principle: once ihram is tied, even a supererogatory 'Umrah becomes binding.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Malik and his school hold that qada is required only for obligatory Hajj, not for 'Umrah or nafl Hajj. The passage references that this view and its proofs were discussed earlier.
Opposing school: Maliki. Their proof likely relies on the principle that compensatory duties only apply to acts that are originally obligatory.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the explicit instruction of the Prophet to Aisha. This demonstrates that the act of qada is directly commanded, making it binding. The Hanafi position is considered the relied-upon (mufta bihi) view.
No internal Hanafi ikhtilaf is reported; all three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree.

Source Text

۷۸۴ (۸) اور عمرہ کے مصر پر قضا لازم ہے۔
مسئلہ نمبرے میں حضرت عائشہ کی حدیث گزری جس میں تھا عن عائشة زوج النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قالت خرجنا مع النبي ، في حجة الوداع ... ارسلني النبي الله مع عبد الرحمن بن ابي بكر الى التنعيم فاعتمرت فقال هذه مكان عمرتک (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب کیف تفعل الحائض والنفساء ص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۱۵۵۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عمرہ چھوٹ جائے تو عمرہ چاہے نفل ہے لیکن احرام باندھنے کے بعد واجب ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی قضا کرنی ہوگی۔ کیونکہ حضرت عائشہ نے عمرہ چھوڑا تھا تو آپ نے عمرہ کروایا اور فرمایا یہ اس عمرے کے بدلے میں ہے۔
امام مالک کا مسلک اور اس کے دلائل او پر مسئلہ نمبرے میں گزر گئے کہ حج فرض کے علاوہ کی قضا نہیں ہے۔ ( بخاری شریف نمبر ۱۸۱۳)
(8) And qada is necessary for the muhsar of 'umrah. In issue number, the hadith of Aisha passed, in which it was: from Aisha, the wife of the Prophet, she said: We went out with the Prophet in the Farewell Hajj... The Prophet sent me with Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr to Tan'im, so I performed 'umrah, and he said: 'This is in place of your 'umrah.' From this hadith it is understood that if 'umrah is missed, even though it is nafilah (supererogatory), after tying the ihram it becomes wajib. Therefore its qada is necessary, because Aisha missed 'umrah, so the Prophet made her perform 'umrah and said: 'This is in place of your 'umrah.' The madhhab of Imam Malik and its proofs have passed earlier in issue number, that qada is not required except for the fard of hajj.
Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This passage explicitly states the ruling that a person prevented from completing 'Umrah (muhsar) must perform qada (make-up) of that 'Umrah. The proof is the hadith of Aisha: during the Farewell Hajj, her menstruation prevented her from performing 'Umrah earlier, so the Prophet sent her to Tan'im to perform 'Umrah and said it was in place of her missed 'Umrah. The author explains that although the original 'Umrah she intended was nafilah (supererogatory), once she tied the ihram, it became wajib (obligatory) to complete it, and if prevented, qada becomes necessary. This is the Hanafi position. The text contrasts this with Imam Malik's view, which holds that qada is only required for obligatory Hajj, not for 'Umrah or nafl Hajj. The Hanafi school relies on the explicit command of the Prophet to Aisha as clear evidence.

Key Terms
نَفْل (nafl): Supererogatory act; when a nafl 'umrah is begun with ihram, it becomes wajib to complete.
عُمْرَة (ʿumrah): The lesser pilgrimage to Mecca, consisting of tawaf, sa'y, and halq or taqsir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why must a muhsar for 'Umrah perform qada?
A) Because 'Umrah is always obligatory (fard)
B) Because once ihram is tied, even a voluntary 'Umrah becomes wajib and must be made up if prevented
C) Because the Prophet always performed qada for his own 'Umrah
D) Because it is a condition of the contract of 'Umrah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school obligates qada for a missed 'Umrah after ihsar based on the principle that entering ihram makes even a supererogatory act binding.

Qada for Muhsar by Umrah: Hanafi vs Maliki Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on qada for muhsar by Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qada for a muhsar by Umrah, explain the Maliki counter-argument, and evaluate the Hanafi response using the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
Once ihram is entered, even a supererogatory Umrah becomes wajib, so qada is required if prevented.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding a person who enters ihram for Umrah but is prevented (muhsar) from completing it. The question is whether such a person must later make up that Umrah (qada). The Hanafi school, relying on the hadith of Aisha, holds that qada is required even if the Umrah was originally supererogatory, because entering ihram makes it obligatory. Imam Malik, citing the precedent of Hudaybiyyah and an athar from Ibn Abbas, argues that qada is only for obligatory Hajj. Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi principle that an act becomes binding once ihram is entered.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling as presented in the matn: 'And upon the muhsar by Umrah is qada.' Note that the Hanafi school extends this to both Hajj and Umrah, even if the Umrah was originally supererogatory.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik holds that qada is required only for obligatory Hajj (fard), not for Umrah or supererogatory acts. His position is that a muhsar becomes halal by slaughtering and shaving, with no obligation to return.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Malik's proof includes an athar from Ibn Abbas: 'The substitute is only upon one whose Hajj is deficient due to pleasure...' implying no return for those prevented by excuse. Also the incident of Hudaybiyyah where the Prophet and Companions became halal without later qada.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis distinguish the Ibn Abbas athar as referring to deliberate violation, not prevention. The Hudaybiyyah case is distinguished because that Umrah was not yet obligatory (no ihram had been tied with the intention of completing it as an obligation). They cite the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet told her after she missed her Umrah: 'This is in place of your Umrah,' showing qada is required.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: According to the Hanafis, a muhsar in Umrah must later perform a makeup Umrah. According to Malik, he simply becomes halal and has no further obligation.

When he becomes halal, upon him is Hajj and Umrah [784] (8) And upon the muhsar by Umrah is qada. From this hadith it became clear that if Hajj is missed, he performs Umrah and becomes halal and performs Hajj the next year. According to Imam Malik, if Hajj was obligatory then its qada is required, otherwise not. His proof is this athar from Ibn Abbas: 'Indeed the substitute is only upon one whose Hajj is deficient due to pleasure. As for one who is prevented by an excuse or something else, he becomes halal and does not return. And if he has hady with him and is muhsar, he slaughters it if he cannot send it. If he can send it, he does not become halal until the hady reaches its place.' Malik and others said: He slaughters his hady and shaves in any place, and no qada upon him, because the Prophet and his Companions at Hudaybiyyah slaughtered, shaved, and became halal from everything before tawaf and before the hady reached the House. Then it is not mentioned that the Prophet ordered anyone to make up anything or return for it. Hudaybiyyah is outside the Haram. (a) (Bukhari, Chapter: Whoever said there is no substitute for the prevented person, p. 233 no. 1813). In this athar, it states that the Prophet abandoned Umrah at the occasion of the Treaty of Hudaybiyyah and did not order anyone to make it up later. Many Companions could not go for Umrah the following year. The meaning is that qada was not obligatory, so they did not make it up. By consensus, if ihsar occurs in obligatory Hajj, qada is required. 784 (8) And for the muhsar by Umrah, qada is required. صلى The hadith of Aisha has passed in mas'alah number...: 'Aisha, wife of the Prophet, said: We went out with the Prophet for Hajjat al-Wada... The Prophet sent me with Abd al-Rahman bin Abi Bakr to Tan'im, so I performed Umrah, and he said: This is in place of your Umrah.' (b) (Bukhari, Chapter: How should the menstruating and postpartum woman act? p. 211 no. 1556). From this hadith it became clear that if Umrah is missed, although it was supererogatory, after tying ihram it becomes obligatory. Therefore its qada must be performed. Because Aisha missed her Umrah, the Prophet had her perform one and said it is in place of her Umrah. Imam Malik's school and its proofs have passed in the previous mas'alah that qada is not required except for obligatory Hajj. (a) Ibn Abbas said: Substitute is upon one who broke his Hajj for pleasure. In any case, one prevented by an excuse or otherwise becomes halal and does not return. And if he has hady with him and becomes muhsar, he slaughters it if he cannot send it to the Haram. If he can send it, he does not become halal until the hady reaches its place. Then no one mentioned that the Prophet ordered anyone to make up anything or return for qada, and Hudaybiyyah is outside the Haram. Source pages p. 475

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the qada (making up) of Umrah for a muhsar (one prevented from completing pilgrimage). The Hanafi position, based on the matn, is that even if the Umrah was supererogatory (nafl), once one enters ihram, it becomes obligatory to complete it, and if prevented, qada is required. The passage first states the base ruling: 'Upon the muhsar by Umrah is qada.' The author then presents Imam Malik's opposing view that qada is only required for obligatory Hajj, not Umrah, even if one has entered ihram. Malik's proof is the athar from Ibn Abbas, which indicates that only one who has broken his Hajj by sexual pleasure needs a substitute; one prevented by an excuse simply becomes halal without qada. He also cites the incident of Hudaybiyyah where the Prophet and Companions became halal without qada. The Hanafi response is given in the commentary: the hadith of Aisha shows that even for a missed Umrah, because she had tied ihram, the Prophet commanded her to make it up and said it is in place of her Umrah. Thus, the Hanafis argue that once ihram is entered, the act becomes binding (wajib), and qada is necessary. The footnote further elaborates the Maliki position and the distinction between being prevented by an excuse versus breaking the ihram intentionally.

Key Terms
محصر (muḥṣar): A person who has entered ihram for Hajj or Umrah but is prevented from completing it due to an obstacle such as enemy, illness, etc.
قضاء (qaḍāʾ): Making up a missed or invalidated worship after its prescribed time.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal sent to the Haram as a penalty or offering during Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, which of the following is the correct ruling for a muhsar in a supererogatory Umrah?
A) No qada is required because the Umrah was supererogatory.
B) Qada is required because entering ihram makes it wajib.
C) Qada is required only if the Umrah was performed during Hajj season.
D) Qada is required only if the muhsar had already performed tawaf.

Key Takeaway
Once ihram is entered, even a supererogatory Umrah becomes wajib and requires qada if prevented, according to the Hanafi school.

Qada for Qarin Muhsar: One Hajj and Two Umrahs
Ruling on qada for qarin muhsar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a qarin muhsar's qada and explain why two Umrahs are required.

Core Idea
A qarin muhsar owes one Hajj and two Umrahs: one Umrah from qiran, one from ihsar.

In the previous lesson, you learned that a muhsar performing only Umrah must make up one Umrah. Here, the rule extends to the qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah). The Hanafi school derives that a qarin muhsar must perform one Hajj and two Umrahs, because the ihsar adds an additional obligation beyond the original qiran. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Recognize that the passage rules on a qarin (one in qiran) who becomes muhsar (prevented from completing). The ruling is that he must make up one Hajj and two Umrahs.
This is a qada (make-up) obligation, not a fard of the original act.
2
Break down the components
The qarin originally had one Hajj and one Umrah from the qiran. When muhsar, an additional Umrah becomes wajib as compensation for the ihsar (since the muhsar for Umrah must do qada of an Umrah). Thus total: one Hajj + two Umrahs.
The second Umrah is specifically due to ihsar, not from qiran.
3
Identify the proof
The matn cites a narration from Hammad (via Darqutni and Bayhaqi) that a man who combined Hajj and Umrah and became muhsar must send a hady, become halal, and upon him is one Hajj and two Umrahs.
This is a mursal narration from Hammad, but accepted in Hanafi usul as a proof.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
A different scholar, al-Hakam, held that the qada is one Hajj and three Umrahs. The matn does not discuss tarjih, but the Hanafi mufta bihi is one Hajj and two Umrahs.
Al-Hakam may have considered the original Umrah separate from the ihsar Umrah, requiring an extra one.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that a qarin muhsar must make up one Hajj and exactly two Umrahs, no more.
This is consistent with the general rule that ihsar for Umrah adds one Umrah to the qada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۸۵] (۹) وعلى القارن حجة وعمرتان قارن نے حج اور عمرے کا احرام ایک ساتھ باندھا ہے اس لئے جب وہ مصر ہوئے تو ایک عمرہ احصار کی وجہ سے لازم ہوگا اور ایک حج اور ایک عمرہ قرآن کی وجہ سے لازم تھے۔ اس لئے ایک حج اور دو عمرے لازم ہوئے ۔ حج فوت ہو جائے تو عمرہ کر کے حلال ہو اس کی دلیل مسئلہ نمبرے میں گزرگئی (دار قطنی نمبر ۱۳۹۶ بیھقی ج خامس ص ۲۸۴، نمبر ۹۸۲۰) عن حماد في رجل اهل بعمرة وحجة فاحصر قال يبعث بالهدى فاذا بلغ الهدى محله احل و عليه حجة و عمرتان وقال الحكم عليه حجة و ثلاث عمر (مصنف ابی ابن شیبہ کے افی الرجل تجمع بين الحج والعمرة فيحصر ماعلیہ فی قابل ج ثالث ، ص ۱۳۳، نمبر ۱۲۷۹۵)
[785] (9) Upon the qarin is one Hajj and two Umrahs. The qarin tied ihram for Hajj and Umrah together, so when he becomes muhsar, one Umrah becomes necessary due to ihsar, and one Hajj and one Umrah were necessary due to qiran. Therefore, one Hajj and two Umrahs become necessary. If Hajj is missed, he performs Umrah and becomes halal; its proof passed in mas'alah number... (Darqutni no. 1396, Bayhaqi vol. 5 p. 284 no. 9820) From Hammad concerning a man who entered ihram for Umrah and Hajj and became muhsar. He said: He sends the hady, and when the hady reaches its place, he becomes halal, and upon him is one Hajj and two Umrahs. And al-Hakam said: Upon him is one Hajj and three Umrahs. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, concerning a man who combines Hajj and Umrah and becomes muhsar: what is upon him next year, vol. 3 p. 133 no. 12795)
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This is a ruling statement on the qada required for a qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) who becomes muhsar. The matn states that upon the qarin muhsar is one Hajj and two Umrahs. The commentary explains the reasoning: he initially had one Hajj and one Umrah due to qiran; when he becomes muhsar, one additional Umrah becomes necessary as compensation for the ihsar (since the muhsar by Umrah requires qada of an Umrah, as the previous lesson established). Thus, total: one Hajj and two Umrahs. The proof is a narration from Hammad that a muhsar qarin must perform one Hajj and two Umrahs. Another opinion from al-Hakam says one Hajj and three Umrahs, but the commentary does not discuss which is relied upon. The emphasis is on the Hanafi ruling.

Key Terms
قارن (qārin): One who performs Hajj and Umrah simultaneously with one ihram (qiran).
قران (qirān): Combining Hajj and Umrah with a single ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a qarin becomes muhsar, how many acts does he need to make up according to the Hanafi school?
A) One Hajj only.
B) One Hajj and one Umrah.
C) One Hajj and two Umrahs.
D) One Hajj and three Umrahs.

Key Takeaway
A qarin muhsar must make up one Hajj and two Umrahs per Hanafi school.

The Qarin's Makeup Obligations When Muhsar
States the makeup obligations for a muhsar Qarin with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the makeup requirements for a Qarin who becomes muhsar and identify the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
A muhsar Qarin owes one Hajj and two Umrahs: one for the qiran, one for the ihsar.

When a Qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) becomes muhsar (prevented from completing the rites), he must make up with one complete Hajj and two Umrahs. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this ruling and the hadith evidence that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Situation
The case is a Qarin who entered ihram for both Hajj and Umrah simultaneously and then becomes muhsar (prevented).
Ihsar can be due to enemy, illness, or any legitimate obstacle.
2
Determine the Original Obligation
Due to the qiran, the Qarin already owed one Hajj and one Umrah. These remain obligatory to fulfill.
The qiran itself creates a single combined obligation, but for makeup, it is treated as two separate acts.
3
Add the Ihsar Obligation
The ihsar adds an additional Umrah as compensation. Thus total makeup: one Hajj and two Umrahs.
The additional Umrah is necessary to complete what was missed due to prevention.
4
Examine the Evidence
The hadith from Hammad (recorded by Dar Qutni and Bayhaqi) explicitly states: 'upon him is one Hajj and two Umrahs.'
This is a direct proof from the Sunnah.
5
Note the Scholarly Difference
A narration from Hakam states three Umrahs, but the Hanafi school relies on the two-Umrah report as the stronger evidence.
This difference does not affect the mufta bihi (operative) position.

Source Text

قارن نے حج اور عمرے کا احرام ایک ساتھ باندھا ہے اس لئے جب وہ مصر ہوئے تو ایک عمرہ احصار کی وجہ سے لازم ہوگا اور ایک حج اور ایک عمرہ قرآن کی وجہ سے لازم تھے۔ اس لئے ایک حج اور دو عمرے لازم ہوئے ۔

And upon the Qarin is one Hajj and two Umrahs.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This is a ruling for a Qarin who becomes muhsar. The Qarin combined Hajj and Umrah in one ihram. Upon becoming muhsar, he already owed one Hajj and one Umrah due to the qiran. The ihsar makes an additional Umrah obligatory. Thus his makeup requires one Hajj and two Umrahs. The evidence is from the hadith of Hammad, as recorded by Dar Qutni and Bayhaqi, where the Prophet (ﷺ) ruled similarly. Another narration from Hakam states three Umrahs, but the relied-upon view is two.

Key Terms
القارن (al-qārin): One who enters into ihram for both Hajj and Umrah simultaneously.
المحصر (al-muḥṣir): One who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to an obstacle such as enemy or illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Muhsar Who Can Catch Both Hady and Hajj
Ruling when muhsar can reach both hady and Hajj after ihsar removal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a muhsar who, after ihsar removal, can catch both the hady and Hajj, and explain why dissolution is prohibited.

Core Idea
When able to perform the original act, the substitute (tahallul due to ihsar) is abandoned.

In this lesson, we examine a scenario where a muhsar has dispatched a sacrificial animal (hady) but then his ihsar is lifted before the Hajj is missed. The key question: can he now dissolve his ihram or must he proceed? The rule turns on whether he can still catch both the hady and the Hajj. We'll see that when the original obligation becomes feasible, the concession of tahallul expires.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the passage: a muhsar sends a hady and appoints a day for slaughter; then ihsar is removed. The ruling is: if he can catch both hady and Hajj, he must not dissolve but must proceed.
The hady is already dispatched, but its slaughter may be later.
2
Understand the precondition
The key condition is 'ability to catch both'. This means the pilgrim can still participate in Hajj and also retrieve his hady before it is slaughtered. If either is impossible, the ruling changes.
Ask: what if the hady is already slaughtered? Then he cannot catch it, so dissolution becomes permissible.
3
Apply the principle: original over substitute
The general concession for ihsar (sending a hady and dissolving) is a substitute for the obligation of Hajj. When the original obligation becomes possible, the substitute is no longer valid. Thus, the pilgrim must perform Hajj.
This is a clear example of qiyas jali: the original (Hajj) takes precedence over the substitute (tahallul).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۸۶] (۱۰) واذا بعث المحصر هديا وواعد هم ان يذبحوه فى يوم بعينه ثم زال الاحصار فان قدر على ادراك الهدى والحج لم يجز له التحلل ولزمه المضى [۷۸۶] (۱۰) اگر محصر نے ہدی بھیجی اور لوگوں سے وعدہ کروایا کہ اس کو متین دن میں ذبح کرے گا پھر احصار زائل ہو گیا۔ پس اگر ہدی پانے پر اور حج پانے پر قدرت ہو تو اس کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز نہیں ، اور اس کو آگے بڑھنا لازم ہے۔
منحصر ہدی بھیج چکا ہے لیکن اس درمیان احصار زائل ہو گیا۔ اور حج اور ہری دونوں پانے پر قادر ہے تو حلال نہ ہو بلکہ آگے بڑھے اور حج
کرے اور ہدی بعد میں خود سے ذبح کرے۔
چونکہ اصل پر قادر ہو گیا اس لئے اب فرع پر عمل نہیں کرے گا۔
انوان اصل پر قادر ہو تو فرع پر عمل نہیں کیا جائے گا۔
And if the muhsar sends a hady and appoints people to slaughter it on a specific day, then the ihsar is removed, and he is able to catch both the hady and the Hajj, it is not permissible for him to dissolve, and he must proceed.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This ruling explains a scenario where a muhsar has already dispatched a sacrificial animal (hady) and arranged for its slaughter on a set date. If the ihsar is removed and he can still reach both the hady and the Hajj, he may not dissolve his ihram. Instead, he must continue with his Hajj and personally slaughter the hady after completion. The principle is: when one can perform the original obligation (the Hajj itself), the substitute (dissolving due to ihsar) is no longer applicable.

Key Terms
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal sent to the Haram by a muhsar or Qarin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He must proceed and not dissolve
C) He must send another hady
D) He should wait until the next year

Key Takeaway
When the muhsar can still perform Hajj, he must proceed because the original obligation takes precedence over the substitute of dissolution.

Muhsar Who Can Only Catch Hady
Ruling on dissolution when only hady is reachable.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a muhsar who can only reach the hady but not the Hajj and explain the rationale based on the primary-secondary distinction.

Core Idea
If a muhsar can sacrifice the hady but not perform Hajj, he may dissolve his ihram.

This passage addresses a specific scenario of ihsār (being prevented from completing Hajj). When the prevention lifts but the time for Hajj has passed, the pilgrim may still have his sacrificial animal. The ruling clarifies that he can exit ihram by sacrificing the hady, as the primary act (Hajj) is no longer possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize the condition: the muhsar can only catch the hady (sacrificial animal) but cannot catch up with the Hajj rituals.
The key is the inability to perform Hajj itself.
2
Determine the ruling
The text states 'تحلل' (he dissolves). This means tahallul (exiting ihram) is permitted.
3
Understand the rationale
The reason provided is that Hajj is the primary act (اصل). Since the primary is impossible, there is no purpose in remaining in ihram.
The secondary act (hady) suffices to fulfill the obligation.
4
Apply the condition
The hady must still be sacrificed. Without the hady, tahallul would require a different ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۸۷] (۱۱) وان قدر علی ادراک الهدی دون الحج تحلل [۷۸۷] (۱۱) اور اگر ہدی پانے پر قدرت ہو لیکن حج پانے پر قدرت نہ ہو تو حلال ہو جائے۔
حج اصل ہے اور اصل پر قدرت نہیں ہوئی تو جا کر کیا کرے گا اس لئے اس کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہے۔
And if he is able to catch the hady but not the Hajj, he dissolves.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
When the ihsar is removed and the person can only manage to reach his hady but cannot participate in the Hajj (e.g., the time has passed), then he is allowed to dissolve his ihram. The reason is that the Hajj is the primary act, and since he cannot perform it, there is no longer any purpose in remaining in ihram. The hady can still be sacrificed to fulfill the obligation.

Key Terms
التحلل (at-taḥallul): The act of exiting ihram by completing acts or by tahallul due to ihsar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Muhsar Able to Catch Hajj but Not Hady: Istihsan Permits Dissolving
Ruling when muhsar can catch Hajj but not hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a muhsar who can catch the Hajj but not the hady, and explain why istihsan permits dissolving ihram despite the qiyas requiring continuation.

Core Idea
Istihsan permits the muhsar to dissolve ihram to avoid loss of property, even though qiyas requires continuation.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Hajj: a pilgrim prevented from completing all rites (muhsar) can still reach the main Hajj but cannot secure or offer the hady (sacrificial animal). Strict analogy (qiyas) would demand that he proceed, since the primary obligation (Hajj) is possible. However, Hanafi jurisprudence applies istihsan (juristic preference) to allow him to dissolve his ihram, preventing waste of the hady. The passage explains this ruling and notes that performing Hajj remains better if feasible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the situation
The pilgrim is a muhsar (prevented from completing Hajj). He is able to catch the Hajj (e.g., the standing at Arafat or tawaf) but is unable to obtain or sacrifice the hady animal.
Hady is a wajib sacrifice for certain Hajj rites; inability here means no access to the animal.
2
Recall the strict qiyas ruling
By qiyas, since the primary obligation (Hajj) is attainable, the muhsar should not dissolve his ihram. He should complete Hajj and then deal with the hady later, because the original act is more important than its accessory.
Qiyas favors the original obligation over a subordinate element.
3
Understand the istihsan exception
Istihsan departs from qiyas to avoid wasting the hady, which is property (mal). The law preserves property and prevents loss. Dissolving ihram allows the pilgrim to sacrifice the hady at home or sell it, preventing loss.
Preservation of wealth is a recognized legal objective (maqsad).
4
Derive the ruling
The ruling is ja'iz (permissible) to dissolve ihram by istihsan. The mufta bihi (operative opinion) is permission, though the author recommends performing Hajj if possible as the better course (afdal).
Afdal does not change the permissibility; it is a moral recommendation.
5
Note the practical recommendation
If the pilgrim can still perform Hajj without undue hardship, it is better to do so, fulfilling his original commitment. But if dissolving avoids loss of the hady, it is legally valid.
The choice is between two valid options: proceed (afdal) or dissolve (ja'iz).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۸۸] (۱۲) وان قدر علی ادراک الحج دون الهدى جاز له التحلل استحسانا [۷۸۸] (۱۲) اور اگر حج کے پانے پر قدرت ہو نہ کہ ہری پانے پر تو اس کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہے استحسانا۔ محصر کا احصار زائل ہو گیا اور حج تو پاسکتا ہے لیکن ہدی نہیں پاسکتا ہو تو اس کے لئے حلال ہونا جائز ہے۔ اگر چہ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ اس کو حلال نہیں ہونا چاہئے اور جا کر حج کرنا چاہئے۔
کیونکہ اصل پر قادر ہے اور ہدی ایک فروعی چیز ہے جس پر قادر نہیں ہے اس لئے قیاس کا تقاضا ہے کہ اس کو حلال نہیں ہونا چاہئے بلکہ جا کر حج کر لینا چاہئے۔ لیکن ہدی یعنی مال کی بھی ایک حیثیت ہے اس لئے وہ ضائع نہ ہو اس لئے اس کے حلال ہونے کی گنجائش ہے، تا ہم حلال نہ

ہو اور جا کر حج کرے تو بہتر ہے تا کہ احرام باندھ کر جس کام کا عہد کیا تھا وہ پورا کرے، اسی لئے مصنف نے فرمایا کہ استحسانا ایسا کرنا جائز ہے۔ قیاس کا تقاضا یہ نہیں ہے۔
And if he is able to catch the Hajj but not the hady, it is permissible for him to dissolve, by istihsan.
Source pages p. 476

Commentary
This ruling addresses when the muhsar can still reach the Hajj itself but cannot get to his hady (sacrificial animal). By strict analogy (qiyas), since he is able to perform the original obligation (Hajj), he should not be allowed to dissolve his ihram and must proceed with Hajj. However, the law takes into consideration that the hady is property and would be wasted. By istihsan (juristic preference), he is allowed to dissolve his ihram and not proceed with Hajj. It is still better (afdal) to go for Hajj if possible, but istihsan permits dissolving to avoid loss of property.

Key Terms
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference that departs from strict qiyas for a more suitable ruling.
محصر (muḥṣar): A pilgrim who is prevented from completing the Hajj or Umrah due to an enemy, illness, or other obstacle.
هدى (hady): A sacrificial animal offered during Hajj, often required as a substitute for omitted rites or as a penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the Hajj is more important
B) To prevent loss of property (the hady)
C) Because the muhsar is weak
D) Because the time has passed

Key Takeaway
Istihsan permits the muhsar to dissolve ihram to avoid wasting the hady, even though qiyas would require continuing.

Muhsar in Makkah: When Prevention Strikes at the Haram
States that a person in Makkah prevented from all essential rites is muhsar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a person in Makkah prevented from Wuquf and Tawaf is muhsar, and identify the proof from Imam Malik's statement.

Core Idea
Even a Makkan resident becomes muhsar if prevented from both Wuquf and Tawaf.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario: a person who is already in Makkah but is prevented from performing the two essential pillars of Hajj – Wuquf at Arafat and Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The Hanafi school rules that such a person is muhsar (barred), despite being within the Haram. This ruling is based on the universal principle of ihsar and is supported by the practice of Imam Malik. Understanding this nuance deepens one's grasp of the conditions for ihsar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Ruling
Read the passage: the ruling applies to anyone in Makkah prevented from Hajj, specifically Wuquf and Tawaf. Note that the person is already in a state of ihram.
The ruling explicitly states that such a person is muhsar.
2
Understand the Rationale
The explanation in the text clarifies why: without Wuquf, the Hajj is invalid; without Tawaf, one cannot exit ihram via Umrah. Thus, the person is effectively blocked from completing the rites, just like an external muhsar.
Both pillars must be prevented to trigger ihsar.
3
Examine the Dalil
The text cites Imam Malik's response to a question about a Makkan pilgrim who suffers a fracture or illness. Malik ruled that such a person is muhsar with the same obligations as a non-Makkan muhsar.
This dalil is a Qawl Sahābi (statement of a Companion? Imam Malik is a Tabi'i actually, but still authoritative). The reference is from Muwatta.
4
Apply the Proof to the Case
The dalil directly analogizes the Makkan prevented from Hajj and Tawaf to the general muhsar from distant lands. The wajh al-dalalah is the explicit inclusion of this scenario.
The proof is considered zanni but sufficient for the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۸۹] (١٣) ومن احصر بمكة وهو ممنوع عن الحج والوقوف والطواف كان محصرا [۷۸۹ (۱۳) جو مکہ مکرمہ میں محصور ہو گیا اور وہ حج کرنے سے اور وقوف عرفہ کرنے سے اور طواف کرنے سے روک دیا گیا تو وہ مصر ہے وقوف عرفہ کرنا اور طواف زیارت کرنا حج کے یہ دوارکان اصل ہیں اور ان دونوں سے روک دیئے گئے تو مکہ مکرمہ میں رہتے ہوئے بھی
محصر ہو جائے گا۔
(۱) کیونکہ وقوف عرفہ نہیں کیا تو ج نہیں ہوا اور طواف نہ کر سکا تو عمرہ کر کے بھی حلال نہیں ہو سکے گا تو گویا کہ وہ لوگ جوصل میں محصر ہوتے ہیں ان کی طرح محصر ہو گئے (۲) سئل مالک عن من اهل من اهل مكة بالحج ثم اصابه كسر او بطن متخرق او امرأة تطلق قال من أصابه هذا منهم فهو محصر يكون عليه مثل ما يكون على اهل الآفاق اذا هم احصروا (الف) موطا امام مالک، باب ما جاء فیمن احصر بغیر عدو ص۳۸۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اہل مکہ حج کرنے سے اور طواف کرنے سے روک دیئے گئے تو وہ بھی آفاقی کی طرح محصر ہوں گے۔
And whoever is muhsar in Makkah and is prevented from Hajj, Wuquf, and Tawaf, he is muhsar.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This ruling clarifies that ihsar can occur even within Makkah if a person is prevented from performing the essential rites of Hajj: Wuquf at Arafat and Tawaf al-Ziyarah. If he cannot perform Wuquf, his Hajj is invalid; if he cannot perform Tawaf, he cannot complete Umrah to exit ihram. Thus he is like any other muhsar. The proof is from the practice of Imam Malik, who was asked about a resident of Makkah who became ill or injured, and he ruled that such a person is muhsar with the same obligations as someone from outside Makkah.

Key Terms
الوقوف (al-wuqūf): Standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; a pillar of Hajj.
الطواف (aṭ-ṭawāf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba; specifically Tawaf al-Ziyarah, a pillar of Hajj.
محصر (muḥṣir): A person in ihram who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to factors like enemy, illness, or other obstacles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Prevention from Wuquf only
B) Prevention from Tawaf only
C) Prevention from both Wuquf and Tawaf
D) Being stopped by an enemy

Key Takeaway
A person in Makkah is muhsar if prevented from both Wuquf and Tawaf, regardless of cause.

Able to Perform One of the Two Pillars: Not Muhsar
States that ability to perform either Wuquf or Tawaf negates ihsar status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ihsar when one of the two pillars (Wuquf or Tawaf) can be performed, and explain the disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
A person who can perform either Wuquf or Tawaf is not muhsar; no hady is due, but if Wuquf is missed, Hajj is still invalid.

This lesson examines a nuanced case in Hajj: what if a person in Makkah is prevented from either Wuquf or Tawaf but can still perform the other? The Hanafi school clarifies that such a person is not considered muhsar (prevented) in a way that requires a compensatory sacrifice (hady), though the implications for the validity of Hajj differ. The lesson also explores the Shafi'i counter-position and its evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Determine the exact ruling: the person is not muhsar, meaning no hady for ihsar is owed. This applies whether he can perform Wuquf or Tawaf.
Note: 'Not muhsar' here refers to the obligation to send a sacrificial animal, not to the validity of Hajj.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that prevention from either Wuquf or Tawaf alone constitutes ihsar, requiring a hady.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i school cites an athar (narration) from Imam Malik where various conditions (broken foot, dysentery, divorce) are treated as causes of ihsar.
The athar is mentioned in footnote (a) of the source text.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school distinguishes: the athar refers to prevention from both pillars, not just one. If one pillar can still be performed, the person is not fully prevented, so ihsar does not apply.
The reasoning is that ability to perform one allows either completion of Hajj (if Wuquf) or conversion to Umrah (if Tawaf).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis do not require a hady in this case; Shafi'is require a hady if prevented from either pillar.

Commentary
This ruling explains that if a person in Makkah is prevented from one of the two pillars (Wuquf or Tawaf) but can still perform the other, he is not considered muhsar. Ruling on Being Muhsar When Prevented from Both Wuquf and Tawaf in Makkah
States the ruling of ihsar for a Makkan prevented from both key rites

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ihsar for a Makkan who is prevented from both wuquf and tawaf, and explain the proof from Imam Malik.

Core Idea
A Makkan prevented from both wuquf and tawaf is muhsar, just like a non-Makkan.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Hajj: a resident of Makkah who has entered ihram for Hajj is prevented from performing both the standing at Arafat (wuquf) and the circumambulation (tawaf). The Hanafi school rules that such a person is considered muhsar (prevented), and the rules of ihsar apply, including the obligation of sacrificing an animal. We will examine the legal reasoning and the proof cited from Imam Malik's Muwatta.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
The scenario: a person in Makkah who has entered ihram for Hajj and is prevented from both wuquf and tawaf. The ruling: he is considered muhsar (prevented).
The ruling applies regardless of whether the person is from Makkah or elsewhere.
2
Understand why missing both rites leads to ihsar
The Hajj requires wuquf; missing it invalidates the Hajj. The tawaf is also necessary to complete the rites; without it, one cannot become halal by performing Umrah. Thus, the person is stuck in ihram and becomes muhsar.
If only one rite is missed, the person might still complete the other and exit ihram.
3
Examine the proof from Malik
The proof is an athar (report) from Imam Malik in the Muwatta. He was asked about a Makkan who suffers a fracture, dysentery, or divorce, and he ruled that such a person is muhsar, same as those from distant regions.
The Hanafis accept this as a valid proof (dalil naqli) for the ruling.
4
Apply the ruling to real situations
The ruling applies to any Makkan who cannot perform both wuquf and tawaf due to illness, injury, or other obstacles.
The rules of ihsar include sending a sacrifice to Makkah and making up the Hajj later.

ومن احصر بمكة وهو ممنوع عن الحج والوقوف والطواف كان محصرا
(۱) کیونکہ وقوف عرفہ نہیں کیا تو ج نہیں ہوا اور طواف نہ کر سکا تو عمرہ کر کے بھی حلال نہیں ہو سکے گا تو گویا کہ وہ لوگ جوصل میں محصر ہوتے ہیں ان کی طرح محصر ہو گئے (۲) سئل مالك عن من أهل من أهل مكة بالحج ثم أصابه كسر أو بطن متخرق أو امرأة تطلق قال من أصابه هذا منهم فهو محصر يكون عليه مثل ما يكون على أهل الآفاق إذا هم أحصروا (الف) موطا امام مالك، باب ما جاء فيمن أحصر بغير عدو ص۳۸۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اہل مکہ حج کرنے سے اور طواف کرنے سے روک دیئے گئے تو وہ بھی آفاقی کی طرح محصر ہوں گے۔

And whoever is prevented in Makkah, and he is prevented from Hajj, standing at Arafat, and circumambulation, he is muhsar. (1) Because he did not perform wuquf, so his Hajj is not completed, and he could not perform tawaf, so he cannot become halal by performing Umrah either, so he becomes muhsar like those who are muhsar in the open country. (2) Malik was asked about one who entered ihram for Hajj from the people of Makkah, then he suffered a fracture, or dysentery, or a woman was divorced. He said: Whoever among them is afflicted with this, he is muhsar; upon him is the same as upon the people of the distant regions when they are muhsar. (Muwatta Imam Malik, Chapter on What Came Regarding One Who Is Prevented Other Than by an Enemy, p. 380) From this athar it is known that the people of Makkah, when prevented from performing Hajj and circumambulation, they are muhsar like the people of distant regions. Footnote: (a) Imam Malik was asked: The one who entered ihram for Hajj among the people of Makkah, then his foot broke, or he got dysentery, or a woman was divorced? He said: Those among them who are afflicted with these ailments, they are muhsar. Upon them is the same as upon the distant people when they are muhsar.

Commentary
The passage presents a ruling regarding ihsar (being prevented) for a person who is in Makkah. The ruling: If a person in Makkah is prevented from both the essential rites of Hajj—wuquf at Arafah and tawaf al-ziyarah—then he is considered muhsar. The reason is that he missed wuquf, so his Hajj is invalid, and he cannot complete it with tawaf and sa'y to become halal via Umrah, so he is like a muhsar from outside. The footnote clarifies that Imam Malik was asked about various afflictions, and he ruled that such a person is muhsar. The lesson teaches that ihsar is not limited to those from distant lands; it applies to Makkans as well if they cannot perform both wuquf and tawaf.

وقوف عرفة (wuqūf 'Arafah): The standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, an essential pillar of Hajj.
طواف (ṭawāf): Circumambulation of the Ka'bah, specifically tawaf al-ziyarah in this context.

Ruling on Not Being Muhsar When Able to Perform One of the Two Rites
Clarifies that ability to perform either wuquf or tawaf negates ihsar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on ihsar when a person can perform only one of the two main rites, and apply the Hanafi ruling to determine whether hady is required.

Core Idea
If you can perform either wuquf or tawaf, you are not muhsar — no hady required, regardless of whether Hajj is completed or missed.

This lesson clarifies a critical nuance in the Hanafi law of ihsar (blockage from completing Hajj). Many assume that missing one of the essential rites automatically makes one muhsar, but the Hanafi school distinguishes based on ability. The passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri explains that as long as you can perform either wuquf or tawaf, the ruling of ihsar does not apply. We will unpack the two scenarios and the disagreement with Imam Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
State the two scenarios
Identify the two situations: (a) able to perform wuquf; (b) able to perform tawaf but not wuquf.
2
Determine the ruling for each
For (a): Hajj is valid, person is not muhsar. For (b): Hajj is missed, but the person is not muhsar because they can exit ihram by performing Umrah (tawaf and sa'y).
3
Note the consequence of not being muhsar
If not muhsar, there is no obligation to offer the hady (sacrificial animal) of ihsar.
The 'hady of ihsar' is a specific compensation for being blocked from completing Hajj.
4
Compare with Shafi'i view
Imam Shafi'i holds that prevention from either wuquf or tawaf makes one muhsar, thus requiring hady. This is based on an athar from Imam Malik.
5
Apply the Hanafi rule
Given the two scenarios, the Hanafi ruling is that if a person can perform either wuquf or tawaf, they are not muhsar and do not owe hady.
The key is the ability to perform at least one of the two main rites.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان قدر علی ادراک احدهما فليس محصرا
وقوف عرفہ کر سکتا ہوتو حج ہو گیا، اب طواف زیارت باقی ہے تو وہ کبھی بھی کر سکتا ہے، اس لئے گویا کہ وہ محصر نہیں ہے۔ اور اگر طواف بیت اللہ کر سکتا ہے اور وقوف عرفہ نہیں کر سکتا تو حج تو فوت ہو جائے گا لیکن عمرہ کا طواف اور سعی کر کے حلال ہو سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے اب اس کو احصار کی ہدی لازم نہیں ہوگی تو گویا کہ محصر نہیں ہوا۔ یہی مطلب ہے فلي سي محصر کا کہ اس کو احصار کی ہدی لازم نہیں ہوگی ۔ یہ مطلب نہیں ہے کہ اس کا انج ہو گیا اور وہ واقعی محصر نہیں ہے۔ نانہ امام شافعی کے نزدیک وقوف عرفہ ، یا طواف دونوں میں سے ایک سے روک دیا جائے تو مصر ہوگا۔ ان کی دلیل مسئلہ نمبر ۱۳ میں اثر امام مالک ہے۔
And if he is able to perform one of them, he is not muhsar. If he can do wuquf, then his Hajj is complete; now tawaf al-ziyarah remains, and he can do it anytime, so he is not muhsar. And if he can do tawaf of the House but cannot do wuquf, then his Hajj is missed, but he can become halal by performing the tawaf and sa'y of Umrah. Therefore, he is not obligated to offer the sacrificial animal of ihsar; so he is not muhsar. This is the meaning of 'he is not muhsar' — that the hady of ihsar is not obligatory. It does not mean that his Hajj became valid and he is actually not muhsar. In the view of Imam Shafi'i, if prevented from one of the two, wuquf or tawaf, he is muhsar. Their proof is the athar of Imam Malik in issue number 13.
Source pages p. 477

Commentary
This passage expands on the previous ruling. It explains that if a person is able to perform either wuquf at Arafat or tawaf, then he is not considered muhsar. Two scenarios: (1) If he can do wuquf, his Hajj is valid; tawaf can be done later, so no ihsar. (2) If he can do tawaf but not wuquf, his Hajj is missed, but he can exit ihram by performing Umrah (tawaf and sa'y). In this case, he does not owe the hady (sacrificial animal) of ihsar because he is not muhsar. The text clarifies that 'not muhsar' means he does not have to offer hady; it does not mean his Hajj is complete. The passage also mentions that Imam Shafi'i differs: he considers being prevented from either one as ihsar, citing the same athar from Malik. The Hanafi position is that ability to do one rite removes the ihsar ruling.

Key Terms
ادراک (idrāk): Ability to perform or reach the rite within its time.
ہدی (hady): The sacrificial animal offered as compensation in Hajj.
إحصار (ihsār): Blockage from completing Hajj or Umrah due to illness, enemy, or other unavoidable circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage
