Fawāt al-Hajj: Missing the Standing at Arafah
Ruling on missing wuqoof at Arafah and required actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on missing wuqoof at Arafah and explain the required remedy, including the proofs from hadith.

Core Idea
Missing wuqoof before dawn of 10th invalidates Hajj; remedy is Umrah acts and make-up without dam.

This lesson addresses a critical situation in Hajj: the pilgrim who enters ihram for Hajj but fails to perform the essential standing at Arafah before the specified time. The Hanafi school provides a clear remedy – conversion to Umrah and making up Hajj later. We will examine the ruling, its evidence from the Sunnah, and the practical steps required.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the first line: 'Whoever enters ihram for Hajj and misses the standing at Arafah until dawn of the Day of Nahr has missed Hajj.' Identify that missing wuqoof before dawn of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah causes the Hajj to be fā'it (missed/invalid).
Wuqoof is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj; missing it invalidates the Hajj as such.
2
State the required remedy
The text lists the remedy: perform tawaf and sa'y (acts of Umrah), exit ihram (tahallul), and make up the missed Hajj the following year. No dam is required.
The remedy is wajib (obligatory). No dam because Umrah has been performed.
3
Locate the dalil for the ruling
The source cites the hadith of Ibn Umar: 'Whoever stands at Arafat by night has attained Hajj; whoever misses... let him become halal by Umrah, and he must perform Hajj next year.' Also the athar of Umar supports the no-dam rule.
The hadith is from Darqutni (thubut zanni, dalala qati).
4
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit commands 'falyahill bi 'umrah' and 'wa 'alayhi al-hajju min qabil' directly prescribe the remedy. The omission of any dam in the hadith indicates it is not required.
The proof is clear and decisive (qati dalala).
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that missing wuqoof does not invalidate the Hajj; the pilgrim continues as if valid and only owes a hadi. The Hanafi position relies on the explicit hadith.
Thamarah al-khilaf: Shafi'i does not require make-up Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الفوات
كتاب الحج
[۷۹۱] (١) ومن احرم بالحج ففاته الوقوف بعرفة حتى طلع الفجر من يوم النحر فقد فاته الحج [۷۹۲ (۲) وعليه ان يطوف ويسعى ويتحلل ويقضى الحج من قابل ولا دم عليه
باب الفوات
ضروری نوٹ حج کے فوت ہونے کو فوات کہتے ہیں۔ [۷۹۱] (۱) جس نے حج کا احرام باندھا اور اس کا وقوف عرفہ فوت ہو گیا یہاں تک کہ دسویں ذی الحجہ کی فجر طلوع ہوگئی پس اس کا حج فوت ہو گیا دسویں ذی الحجہ کی فجر طلوع ہونے سے پہلے پہلے وقوف عرفہ کر لینا چاہئے اس سے حج ہو جائیگا۔ اب وہ وہ طلوع فجر سے پہلے فوت ہو گیا تو اس کا حج فوت ہو گیا، وقوف عرفہ فرض ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے تم افيضوا من حيث افاض الناس (آیت ۱۹۹ سورة البقرة ٢) حدیث میں ہے عن عروة بن مضرس ... فقال رسول الله من شهد صلوتنا هذه ووقف معنا حتى يدفع وقد وقف بعرفة قبل ذلك ليلا او نهارا فقد تم حجه ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فی من ادرک الامام مجمع فقد ادرک الحج ص ۷۸ انمبر ۸۹۱ را بو ( ماجاء را بو ) داؤد شریف ، باب من لم یدرک عرفته ، ص ۲۷۶، نمبر ۱۹۴۹) [۷۹۲) (۲) اور اس پر لازم ہے کہ طواف کرے اور سعی کرے اور حلال ہو جائے اور اگلے سال حج کرے اور اس پر حج چھوڑنے کا دم نہیں ہے قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ جس سے حج فوت ہو جائے تو اگر وہ اعمال عمرہ یعنی طواف اور سعی کر سکتا ہو تو وہ کر کے حلال ہو جائے اور اگلے سال حج کرے۔ اور چونکہ عمرہ کر لیا تو اب اس پر ہری ذبح کرنا لازم نہیں ہے۔ البتہ اگر عمرہ نہ کر پاتا تو ہدی لازم ہوتی۔
ان دونوں مسئلوں کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عمر ان رسول الله الله الله قال من وقف بعرفات بلیل فقد ادرک الحج ومن فاته عرفات بليل فقد فاته الحج فليحل بعمرة وعليه الحج من قابل (الف) (دار قطنی، کتاب الحج حج ثانی ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۲۴۹۶) اور دوسری حدیث میں یہ عبارت ہے من ادرك عرفة قبل طلوع الفجر في يوم النحر فقد تم حجه (ب)(دار قطنی ، کتاب الحج، ج ثانی، ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۴ ۲۴۹ سفن سیتی ، باب ادرک ایمیج با دراک عرفته قبل طلوع الفجر من يوم الخرج خامس ص ۲۸۲، نمبر ۹۸۱۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کسی کا وقوف عرفہ چھوٹ گیا تو حج فوت ہو گیا اب اس کو اعمال عمرہ کر کے حلال ہونا چاہئے ۔ اس صورت میں اس پر ہدی لازم نہیں ہوگی۔ اور عمرہ کرنے پر ہدی لازم نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ مذکورہ حدیث میں ہدی کا تذکرہ نہیں ہے (۲) عمر ابن خطاب کے فیصلے میں یہ الفاظ ہیں ان ہبار بن الاسود جاء يوم النحر وعمر ينحر ... ثم انحر هديا ان كان معك ثم احلقوا او قصروا وارجعوا (ج) (سن سیتی ، باب الفعل من فاته الج ، ج خامس، ص ۲۸۴ نمبر ۹۸۲) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اگر ہدی ہو تو ذبح کرو حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا جو عرفات میں رات میں ٹھہرے تو اس نے حج پالیا، اور جس سے رات میں عرفات فوت ہو گیا تو اس سے حج فوت ہو گیا۔ پس عمرہ کر کے حلال ہونا چاہئے۔ اور اس پر اگلے سال حج ہے (ب) جس نے دسویں تاریخ کی فجر طلوع ہونے سے پہلے عرفہ پالیا تو اس کا حج پورا ہو گیا ( ج ) ہبار بن اسود دسویں ذی الحجہ کو حضرت عمر کے پاس آئے اس حال میں کہ وہ اونٹ نحر کر رہے تھے۔ پھر ہلدی نحر کرو اگر تمہارے پاس ہو، پھر حلق کراؤ یا قصر کراؤ اور واپس ہو جاؤ۔
اور نہ ہو تو ذبح نہ کرو جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اعمال عمرہ کرے تو حج فوت کرنے والے پر ہدی لازم نہیں ہے۔
Chapter of Missing (al-Fawāt). Book of Hajj. (1) Whoever enters ihram for Hajj and misses the standing at Arafah until dawn of the Day of Nahr has missed Hajj. (2) He must perform tawaf and sa'y and exit ihram and make up Hajj the following year, and no dam (blood penalty) is required of him. Commentary: Important note: The missing of Hajj is called fawāt. (1) One who enters ihram for Hajj and misses standing at Arafah until the dawn of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah has missed his Hajj. It is necessary to perform wuqoof before dawn of the 10th for Hajj to be valid. Now if he missed it before dawn, his Hajj is missed. The proof that wuqoof is obligatory is the verse: 'Then depart from where the people depart' (2:199). In a hadith: from Urwa ibn Mudarris... the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever attends this prayer of ours and stands with us until we depart, and has stood at Arafah before that night or day, has completed his Hajj.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi man adraka al-imam bi jam' faqad adraka al-Hajj, p. 78, no. 891; Abu Dawud, Bab man lam yudrik Arafah, p. 276, no. 1949). (2) He must perform tawaf and sa'y and become halal, and perform Hajj the next year, and there is no dam for leaving Hajj. The rule is: If one misses Hajj, then if he can perform the acts of Umrah (tawaf and sa'y), he should do so and become halal, and perform Hajj the next year. Since he has performed Umrah, slaughtering a hadi is not obligatory. However, if he could not perform Umrah, a hadi would be obligatory. The proof for these two issues is the hadith: from Ibn Umar... the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever stands at Arafat by night has attained Hajj; whoever misses Arafat by night has missed Hajj; let him become halal by Umrah, and he must perform Hajj next year.' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Hajj, vol. 2, p. 212, no. 2496). Another hadith: 'Whoever attains Arafah before dawn on the Day of Nahr, his Hajj is complete.' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Hajj, vol. 2, p. 212, no. 2494?; Sunan, Bab idrak...). From these hadith it is understood that if one misses standing at Arafah, his Hajj is missed. He must perform acts of Umrah and become halal. In this case, a hadi is not obligatory. And on performing Umrah, a hadi is not obligatory because the hadith does not mention it. (2) In the verdict of Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'When Hubbar ibn al-Aswad came on the Day of Nahr while Umar was sacrificing... then sacrifice a hadi if you have one, then shave or trim, and return.' (Sunan, Bab al-fa'il man fatahu al-Hajj, vol. 5, p. 284, no. 982). This athar indicates: if you have a hadi, slaughter it; if not, do not. The meaning is that if he performs Umrah, a hadi is not required for the one who missed Hajj.
Source pages p. 478

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the situation of a person who, after entering ihram for Hajj, misses the essential standing (wuqoof) at Arafah before dawn of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Nahr). The text states that such a person's Hajj is considered missed (fawāt). The consequence is not that all ihram obligations are void; rather, he is required to perform the acts of Umrah (tawaf and sa'i) to exit ihram (tahallul), and then he must make up the missed Hajj in a subsequent year. Importantly, no sacrificial animal (dam or hadi) is required for this missed Hajj, because he has effectively performed an Umrah. The text provides multiple proofs: the Quranic verse and hadiths that establish the timing of wuqoof, and the hadith of Ibn Umar that explicitly prescribes this remedy. It also cites the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab in a similar case. The commentary clarifies that if the person cannot perform the Umrah acts (e.g., due to confinement), then a hadi would be required. This ruling belongs to the Hanafi school, consistent with the Zahir al-Riwayah position that missing wuqoof before the specified time invalidates the Hajj but allows conversion to Umrah.

Key Terms
فوات (fawāt): The legal term for missing the essential pillar (wuqoof) of Hajj by the specified time, rendering the Hajj invalid as Hajj.
دم (dam): A blood penalty (sacrificial animal) required for certain violations during Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a person do if he misses wuqoof at Arafah before Fajr of Yawm al-Nahr?
A) Perform tawaf, sa'y, and become halal, and make up Hajj next year with no dam.
B) Continue as if Hajj is valid and sacrifice a hadi.
C) Immediately leave ihram without any acts and repeat Hajj next year.
D) Attempt to reach Arafah after sunrise.

Key Takeaway
Missing wuqoof at Arafah before dawn of the 10th invalidates Hajj, but the Hanafi remedy of Umrah plus make-up Hajj without dam provides a clear, evidence-based path.

Umrah is Not Subject to Fawāt (العمرة لا تفوت)
Ruling statement: Umrah is not subject to fawāt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Umrah is not subject to fawāt and explain why this differs from Hajj.

Core Idea
Umrah has no fixed time, so it can never be 'missed' like Hajj.

In the Hanafi school, the concept of fawāt (irretrievable loss) applies only to time-bound obligations. Hajj, with its specific time (wuqoof on 9th Dhul Hijjah), can be missed if one fails to perform the essential rite within that window. Umrah, by contrast, has no fixed time; it can be performed at any point in the year. Therefore, the ruling is clear: Umrah does not become missed, even if one is prevented from completing it at a particular moment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is Umrah. The ruling stated is that it 'does not become missed' (lā tafūt).
This is a negative ruling indicating the absence of a legal consequence.
2
Understand the term 'fawāt'
Fawāt is a technical term meaning the loss of a time-bound obligation because its designated time has passed. For example, if one misses the wuqoof in Hajj, the Hajj is fā'it.
It carries consequences such as the obligation to make up the act and often a sacrificial penalty.
3
Identify the condition for fawāt
The key condition is that the act must be tied to a specific, non-repeatable time. Without that condition, fawāt cannot occur.
Hajj is tied to the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; Umrah is not.
4
Apply the condition to Umrah
Since Umrah can be performed at any time, it lacks the temporal specificity needed for fawāt. Even if one commits to perform Umrah on a particular day and then misses it, the obligation (whether it be sunnah or wajib by nadhr) remains and can be fulfilled later.
This contrasts with Hajj, where missing the specific time is irremediable.
5
State the practical outcome
A person who begins Umrah but is prevented (ihsār) or simply delays it does not lose the act; they may complete it whenever possible. The Umrah is never 'missed' in the legal sense.
Special rules for ihsār (being prevented) apply, but fawāt is not relevant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۹۳](۳) والعمرة لا تفوت
(3) And Umrah does not become missed.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This is a concise statement that Umrah is not subject to fawāt (missing) in the same sense as Hajj. The reasoning provided in the Urdu commentary is that Umrah is not tied to a specific time; it can be performed at any time of the year. If one is prevented (ihsār) from completing it, different rules apply, but it is never 'missed' in the sense that the opportunity passes permanently. One can always perform Umrah later without needing to make up a specific occasion.

Key Terms
تفوت (tafūt): The verb form indicating that something is irretrievably lost due to passage of time (here, Umrah is not subject to this).
فوت (fawt): The noun form meaning the state of being missed or lost; a technical concept in Hajj jurisprudence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, why does Umrah not 'become missed' (lā tafūt)?
A) Because it is less important than Hajj.
B) Because it is not tied to a specific time.
C) Because it has no essential pillars.
D) Because it can be performed only once in a lifetime.

Key Takeaway
Umrah never becomes fā'it because it has no specific time; the Hanafi ruling distinguishes it sharply from Hajj in this regard.

Permissible Times for Umrah: Five Disliked Days
Ruling on when Umrah is permissible and when it is disliked.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five days when Umrah is makruh according to the Hanafi school, explain the proof from the athar, and distinguish between the explicit text and the madhhab’s ruling.

Core Idea
Umrah is permissible all year except five days of Dhul Hijjah; the athar names three, the school extends to five.

Umrah is generally permissible at any time, but the Hanafi school identifies five specific days when it is disliked. The primary proof is an athar from Aisha that excludes three days, yet the school includes two additional days based on the sanctity of the Hajj season. This lesson clarifies the ruling, the evidence, and the difference between the textual exception and the madhhab’s application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and exception
Read the opening line: Umrah is permissible throughout the year except for five days. List them: 9th (Yawm Arafah), 10th (Yawm al-Nahr), 11th-13th (Ayyam al-Tashriq).
2
Examine the athar from Aisha
The athar states that Umrah is permissible except for three days: Yawm al-Nahr and two days of Tashriq. Notice the discrepancy: the text says three, but the Hanafi ruling says five.
3
Understand the reason for extension
The Hanafi school extends the prohibition to include the day of Arafah and the third day of Tashriq because these days are also part of the Hajj rites and share the same sanctity.
This is based on the principle of sadd al-dhara'i (blocking pretexts) and preserving the sanctity of Hajj.
4
Determine the level of ruling
The text uses 'makruh' (disliked), not 'haram'. This means performing Umrah on these days is valid but disliked. The athar shows prohibition, but it is not absolute.
Makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked) in the Hanafi scale.
5
Note cross-madhhab difference
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow Umrah on all days of the year, including these five. They interpret the athar as non-prohibitive or consider it abrogated.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is based on the chosen athar and respect for Hajj days.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۹۳] (۴) وهي جائزة جى جميع السنة الا خمسة ايام يكره فعلها فيها يوم عرفة و يوم النحر وايام التشريق
عمرہ پورے سال میں جائز ہے لیکن نویں ذی الحجہ، دسویں ذی الحجہ، گیارہویں ذی الحجہ، بارہویں ذی الحجہ اور تیرہویں ذی الحجہ کو گویا کہ پانچ دنوں میں عمرہ کرنا مکروہ ہے۔
(1) اثر میں ہے عن عائشة قالت حلت العمرة الدهر الا ثلاثة ايام يوم النحر ويومين من ايام التشريق اور دوسرے اثر میں ہے عن العمرة قال اذا مضت ايام التشريق فاعتمر متى شئت الى قابل (الف) (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة في العمرة من قال في كل شهر و من قال متی ما همت جثالث ص ۱۲۶، نمبر ۱۲۷۲۲/۱۲۷۲۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایام تشریق میں عمرہ مکروہ ہے۔ اور اس کے بعد سارے سال میں جع چاہے عمرہ کر سکتا ہے۔
(4) And it (Umrah) is permissible throughout the entire year except for five days: the day of Arafah, the day of Nahr, and the days of Tashriq (three days). Commentary: Umrah is permissible all year but on the 9th, 10th, 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah it is makruh. (1) Athar from Aisha: she said: 'Umrah is permissible throughout the year except three days: the day of Nahr and two days of Tashriq.' Another athar: from Umar: he said: 'When the days of Tashriq pass, then perform Umrah whenever you wish until the next year.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, in al-Umrah, bab man qala fi kulli shahr, etc.). From this athar it is understood that performing Umrah during the days of Tashriq is makruh. After that, one may perform Umrah whenever he wishes throughout the year.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage outlines the temporal permissibility of Umrah. It is generally permissible at any time of the year, but there are five specific days when it is disliked (makruh): the day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah), the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), and the three days of Tashriq (11th, 12th, 13th Dhul Hijjah). The proof is from an athar of Aisha (رضي الله عنها) that excludes only three days (Yawm al-Nahr and two days of Tashriq) and an athar of Umar (رضي الله عنه) indicating that after the days of Tashriq, one may perform Umrah freely. The commentary clarifies that the dislike is due to the sanctity of these days when pilgrims are engaged in the rites of Hajj. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other schools may have different views on the timing.

Key Terms
يوم عرفة (Yawm 'Arafah): The 9th day of Dhul Hijjah, when pilgrims stand at Arafah.
ايام التشريق (Ayyām al-Tashrīq): The 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul Hijjah, days of drying meat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 1st Dhul Hijjah
B) 10th Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Nahr)
C) 8th Dhul Hijjah
D) 14th Dhul Hijjah

Key Takeaway
Umrah is permissible throughout the year except for five specific days of Dhul Hijjah when it is disliked (makruh).

The Legal Status of Umrah: Sunnah Not Obligatory
Ruling on Umrah with proofs and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Umrah, explain why it is Sunnah rather than wajib, and respond to the opposing proof using the hadith of Jabir.

Core Idea
Umrah is Sunnah, not wajib — the Prophet explicitly said 'No' when asked if it is obligatory.

The legal status of Umrah is a point of ikhtilaf between madhahib. This lesson presents the Hanafi position that Umrah is a recommended Sunnah, supported by a clear prophetic statement, and addresses the opposing view that considers it obligatory. Understanding this distinction clarifies a common area of confusion in the worship of Hajj and Umrah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its primary proof
Identify the ruling (Sunnah) and the main hadith (Jabir) where the Prophet negates obligation.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Recognize that some Companions and the Shafi'i school hold Umrah as wajib, citing the hadith of Zaid ibn Thabit.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response to the opposing proof
Understand why the Hanafi school prefers the hadith of Jabir over that of Zaid: greater explicitness in negating obligation.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical difference: sin or no sin for omitting Umrah.
5
Confirm the tarjih (relied-upon position)
The Hanafi school classifies Umrah as Sunnah Mu'akkadah, and this is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۷۹۵] (۵) والعمرة سنة
عمرہ سنت ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن جابر عن النبي الا الله سئل عن العمرة اواجبة هي قال لا وان يعتمروا هو افضل (ب) (ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی العمرة اوا جیت بھی ام لاص ۱۸۶ نمبر ۹۳۱ ردار قطنی ، کتاب الحج حج ثانی ص ۲۵۱ نمبر ۱ ۲۷۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عمرہ سنت ہے واجب نہیں ہے۔
فائدہ بعض اصحاب خواہر اس کو واجب کہتے ہیں ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن زيد بن ثابت قال قال رسول الله الله ان الحج والـعـمـرية فريضتان لا يضرك بايهما بدأت (ج) ( دار قطنی ، کتاب الحج ج ثانی ص ۲۵۰ نمبر ۲۶۹۲)(۲) ان ابن عباس قال
(5) And Umrah is Sunnah. The proof that Umrah is Sunnah is the hadith of Jabir from the Prophet (peace be upon him): he was asked about Umrah, 'Is it obligatory?' He said, 'No, and if you perform Umrah, it is more virtuous.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-umrah, p. 186, no. 931; Darqutni, Kitab al-Hajj, vol. 2, p. 251, no. 270?1). From this hadith it is understood that Umrah is Sunnah, not wajib. Benefit: Some of the Companions considered it wajib. Their proof is the hadith of Zaid ibn Thabit: the Messenger of Allah said: 'Indeed Hajj and Umrah are two obligations; it does not harm you with which you begin.' (Darqutni, Kitab al-Hajj, vol. 2, p. 250, no. 2692). And Ibn Abbas said...
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage addresses the legal status of Umrah: it is a Sunnah (recommended) act, not an obligation (wajib or fard). The primary proof is the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly states that Umrah is not obligatory, though performing it is virtuous. The text also mentions a differing view among some Companions (and by extension, some scholars) who considered it obligatory, citing a hadith from Zaid ibn Thabit that calls both Hajj and Umrah 'fariḍatān' (two obligations). However, the Hanafi school prefers the first hadith and classifies Umrah as Sunnah Mu'akkadah (emphasized Sunnah). This is a classic inter-madhhab dispute: the Shafi'i school also holds Umrah to be obligatory (wajib) once in a lifetime, while the Hanafi school holds it to be Sunnah. The commentary clarifies that the relied-upon Hanafi position is that Umrah is Sunnah.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act that the Prophet performed or encouraged, but not legally binding.
واجبة (wājibah): Obligatory; here, some consider Umrah as such.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of Umrah?
A) Fard (obligatory) like Hajj.
B) Sunnah (recommended), not obligatory.
C) Wajib (obligatory) once in a lifetime.
D) Mubah (permissible) with no reward.

Key Takeaway
Umrah is a highly recommended Sunnah act, not an obligation, according to the Hanafi school.

'Umrah Does Not Lapse: Time Flexibility in Hanafi Fiqh
Statement that 'Umrah cannot be missed unlike Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that 'Umrah does not lapse and explain why it differs from Hajj regarding time constraints.

Core Idea
Umrah has no fixed time, so it never lapses; Hajj is tied to a specific day.

This lesson focuses on a key distinction between Hajj and 'Umrah in Hanafi fiqh. While Hajj is strictly time-bound to the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, 'Umrah enjoys flexibility—it can be performed any day of the year. This difference has practical implications: if someone is prevented from completing 'Umrah, the act remains valid whenever they resume, unlike Hajj which would be invalid for that year.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
Read the passage carefully. The ruling is explicitly stated: 'Umrah does not lapse (lā tafūt). This means if a person intends 'Umrah but is prevented, it is not invalidated; it can be completed later.
The term 'lā tafūt' is the key legal phrase.
2
Contrast with Hajj
Notice how the passage contrasts 'Umrah with Hajj. Hajj is tied to a specific moment: standing at 'Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. Missing that moment invalidates the entire Hajj for that year, requiring a new ihram the following year.
This contrast highlights why 'Umrah is different.
3
Identify the Cause of the Difference
The passage states: 'Umrah is not specific to any day. Because there is no fixed time, prevention (ihsār) does not cause the act to lapse. The 'Umrah remains valid and can be performed later.
The cause is the absence of a time constraint (zaman mukhassis).
4
Apply the Ruling
Consider a real scenario: Someone enters ihram for 'Umrah but falls ill and cannot complete the rituals. According to this ruling, their 'Umrah does not become invalid; they may complete it whenever they recover, even years later.
This ruling is unique to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳) والعمرة لا تفوت
عمرہ فوت نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ حج کا معاملہ یہ ہے کہ نویں ذی الحجہ کو عرفات کا وقوف کرے گا تو حج ہوگا اور اس وقت عرفات کا وقوف نہ کر سکا تو اب حج نہیں ہو گا۔ اب آئندہ سال حج کا احرام باندھ کر پھر نویں ذی الحجہ میں وقوف کرے تو حج ہوگا۔ لیکن عمرہ کا معاملہ کسی دن کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے ، وہ کسی دن میں بھی کر سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے عمرہ میں احصار تو ہو گا لیکن فوت نہیں ہوگا، وہ جب بھی ادا کرے گا ادا ہی ہوگا۔
(3) And 'Umrah does not lapse. 'Umrah does not lapse. The matter of Hajj is that on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah one will stand at 'Arafat, then Hajj will be valid, and if he cannot stand at 'Arafat at that time, then Hajj will not be valid. Next year, if he assumes ihram for Hajj and again stands at 'Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, then Hajj will be valid. But the matter of 'Umrah is not specific to any day; he can perform it any day. Therefore, in 'Umrah, ihsar (prevention) may occur but it does not lapse; whenever he performs it, it will be valid.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage clarifies the legal difference between Hajj and 'Umrah regarding time constraints. Hajj is time-bound to the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; if the pilgrim misses the standing at 'Arafat on that specific day, the Hajj is invalid for that year and must be repeated the next year. 'Umrah, by contrast, has no fixed time; it can be performed any day of the year. Therefore, if someone is prevented (ihsar) from completing 'Umrah, it does not become invalid or missed; it remains valid whenever they are able to perform it. This ruling is based on the general permissibility of 'Umrah throughout the year, as established in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
لا تفوت (lā tafūt): does not lapse or become missed; the act remains valid whenever performed later.
احصار (ihṣār): prevention from completing pilgrimage due to enemy, illness, or other obstacle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because 'Umrah is obligatory only once in a lifetime
B) Because 'Umrah has no specific time-bound requirement like standing at 'Arafat
C) Because 'Umrah can only be performed in the month of Ramadan
D) Because 'Umrah requires fewer acts than Hajj

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, 'Umrah does not lapse because it is not time-bound; it can be performed at any time.

'Umrah is Sunnah: Evidence and the Scholarly Dispute
Ruling that 'Umrah is sunnah, with proofs and opposing view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on 'Umrah, explain the primary evidence (dalil), and analyse the opposing view of some Sahaba along with the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
The Prophet explicitly said 'Umrah is not obligatory—the Hanafi school follows this clear text.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that 'Umrah is sunnah (recommended) rather than wajib (obligatory). The source presents a hadith from Jabir where the Prophet (peace be upon him) directly negates obligation, contrasted with transmissions from Zayd ibn Thabit and Ibn 'Abbas that appear to assert obligation. We will work through the evidence, the Hanafi response, and the practical implications of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds: 'Umrah is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib. Note that this is the mufta bihi (relied upon) position.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is an emphasized recommended act, but omission is not sinful.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Some Sahaba (Zayd ibn Thabit and Ibn 'Abbas) considered 'Umrah obligatory. Understand their basis.
The opponent here is not a later madhhab but companions of the Prophet.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent cites a hadith: 'Hajj and 'Umrah are two obligations' (from Zayd) and a statement of Ibn 'Abbas comparing 'Umrah's obligation to Hajj.
These texts appear to make 'Umrah obligatory (wajib or fard).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school gives precedence to the more explicit hadith from Jabir that directly negates obligation. The opposing texts are interpreted as referring to virtue or are considered less explicit.
The response rests on the principle that a clear explicit text (nass) takes precedence over texts that may be interpreted in multiple ways.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if 'Umrah is sunnah, omitting it is not sinful; if wajib, it must be performed at least once in a lifetime, and omitting it would be sinful.
This difference affects fatwa and personal practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۵) والعمرة سنة.
عمرہ سنت ہے۔ عمرہ سنت ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن جابر عن النبي الا الله سئل عن العمرة اواجبة هي قال لا وان يعتمروا هو افضل (ب) (ترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی العمرة اوا جیت بھی ام لاص ۱۸۶ نمبر ۹۳۱ ردار قطنی ، کتاب الحج حج ثانی ص ۲۵۱ نمبر ۱ ۲۷۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عمرہ سنت ہے واجب نہیں ہے۔
فائدہ بعض اصحاب خواہر اس کو واجب کہتے ہیں ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن زيد بن ثابت قال قال رسول الله الله ان الحج والـعـمـرية فريضتان لا يضرك بايهما بدأت (ج) ( دار قطنی ، کتاب الحج ج ثانی ص ۲۵۰ نمبر ۲۶۹۲)(۲) ان ابن عباس قال
العمرة واجبة كوجوب الحج من الستطاع اليه سبيلا (الف) (دار قطنی ، کتاب الحج حج ثانی ص۲۵۰ نمبر ۲۶۹۴) اس حدیث اور اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ عمرہ واجب ہے۔
وت لیکن دوسری احادیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ عمرہ سنت ہے اور پورے سال میں جائز ہے۔
(5) And 'Umrah is sunnah. 'Umrah is sunnah. The proof that 'Umrah is sunnah is this hadith: From Jabir that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked about 'Umrah, "Is it obligatory?" He said, "No, and if you perform 'Umrah, it is better." (Tirmidhi, chapter on 'Umrah, whether it is obligatory or not, p. 186, no. 931; and Dar Qutni, Book of Hajj, second part, p. 251, no. 1? 270). From this hadith it is known that 'Umrah is sunnah, not obligatory. Benefit: Some companions consider it obligatory. Their evidence is this hadith: From Zayd ibn Thabit that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "Indeed, Hajj and 'Umrah are two obligations; it does not harm you with which you begin." (Dar Qutni, Book of Hajj, vol. 2, p. 250, no. 2692). And that Ibn 'Abbas said: "'Umrah is obligatory like the obligation of Hajj for those who have the ability to find a way to it." (Dar Qutni, Book of Hajj, vol. 2, p. 250, no. 2694). From this hadith and athar it is known that 'Umrah is obligatory. But other ahadith indicate that 'Umrah is sunnah and permissible throughout the year.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage addresses the legal status of 'Umrah: is it obligatory (wajib) or sunnah? The Hanafi school holds that 'Umrah is sunnah, not wajib. The proof is a hadith in which the Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly says 'Umrah is not obligatory, but performing it is better. However, some companions (like Zayd ibn Thabit and Ibn 'Abbas) considered 'Umrah obligatory, citing a hadith that both Hajj and 'Umrah are fard (obligations) and another statement from Ibn 'Abbas. The author then notes that other ahadith (the one from Jabir) show it is sunnah. The Hanafi school gives precedence to the hadith that negates obligation, as it is more explicit. Thus the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that 'Umrah is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), not wajib. This is a classical inter-madhhab dispute, but here it is presented as a dispute between the Hanafi view and the view of some Sahaba.

Key Terms
سنة (sunnah): A recommended act; not obligatory but rewarded.
واجب (wājib): Obligatory; omission is sinful without excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Fard (obligatory) like Hajj
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized recommended)
C) Makruh (disliked) because it resembles Hajj in some aspects
D) Mustahabb but only once in a lifetime

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds 'Umrah is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, based on the Prophet's explicit negation of obligation.

The Three Pillars of 'Umrah: Ihram, Tawaf, and Sa'y
Definition of the essential acts of 'Umrah with hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three pillars of 'Umrah according to the Hanafi school and cite the hadith evidence that establishes each.

Core Idea
Three pillars — ihram, tawaf, sa'y — constitute 'Umrah; missing one invalidates the entire act.

This lesson defines the essential acts (arkan) of 'Umrah. Unlike the general perception that 'Umrah is merely visiting the Ka'bah, the Hanafi school identifies three specific pillars: entering the state of ihram, circumambulating the Ka'bah (tawaf), and walking between Safa and Marwah (sa'y). The passage provides direct hadith proof from the actions of the Companions during the Farewell Pilgrimage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three arkan
Read the opening line: 'وهى الاحرام والطواف والسعى' — the three pillars are explicitly listed.
They are given in order: first ihram, then tawaf, then sa'y.
2
Understand each pillar
Ihram is the state of sanctity entered by intention and talbiyah; tawaf is seven circuits around the Ka'bah; sa'y is seven trips between Safa and Marwah.
These are the essential acts that define 'Umrah.
3
Locate the dalil
Two hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari are cited: one from 'A'isha and one via Abu Shihab.
Both explicitly mention tawaf and sa'y as the acts performed for 'Umrah.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith show that after assuming ihram, the Companions performed tawaf and sa'y, then exited ihram. This sequence establishes these three as the complete set of arkan.
No other acts are mentioned as essential.
5
Conclude the ruling
Omission of any one of these three invalidates the 'Umrah; they are pillars (arkan), not mere obligations.
This is the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(٦) وهى الاحرام والطواف والسعى.
عمرہ کا احرام باندھنا، طواف کرنا اور سعی کرنا ہے۔ تین ارکان کے مجموعے کا نام عمرہ ہے (۱) احرام باندھے (۲) بیت اللہ کا سات شوط طواف کرے (۳) صفا اور مروہ کے درمیان سات مرتبہ سعی کرے۔ اسی تین چیز کے مجموعے کا نام عمرہ ہے۔
حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة زوج النبي الا الله قالت خرجنا مع النبي في حجة الوداع ... قالت فطاف الذين كانو اهلوا بالعمرة بالبيت وبين الصفا والمروة ثم حلوا (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب کیف تصل الحائض والنفساء مص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۱۵۵۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ عمرہ میں احرام باندھے اور طواف بیت اللہ کرے اور صفا اور مروہ کی سعی کرے۔ دوسری حدیث میں ہے حدثنا ابو نعيم حدثنا ابو شهاب ... فقال لهم احلوا من احرامكم بطواف البيت وبين الصفا والمروة و قصروا ثم اقیموا حلالا (ج) ( بخاری شریف ، باب التمتع والاقران والافراد با من ص ۲۱۳ نمبر ۱۵۶۸) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے کہ عمرہ میں طواف اور سعی کر کے حلال ہو جائے یہی اعمال عمرہ ہیں۔
(6) And they are: ihram, tawaf, and sa'y. 'Umrah is to assume ihram, perform tawaf, and perform sa'y. The name 'Umrah is the combination of three essential acts: (1) assume ihram, (2) perform seven circuits of tawaf of the House of Allah, (3) perform seven times sa'y between Safa and Marwa. The name 'Umrah is the combination of these three things. There is a hadith from 'A'isha, the wife of the Prophet (peace be upon him): she said, "We went out with the Prophet during the Farewell Pilgrimage..." She said, "Those who had assumed ihram for 'Umrah performed tawaf of the House and (sa'y) between Safa and Marwa, then they became halal." (Bukhari, chapter on how a menstruating and postpartum woman prays, p. 211, no. 1556). From this hadith it is known that in 'Umrah one assumes ihram, performs tawaf of the House, and performs sa'y between Safa and Marwa. Another hadith: Abu Nu'aym narrated to us from Abu Shihab... he said to them, "Become halal from your ihram by performing tawaf of the House and (sa'y) between Safa and Marwa, and shorten (your hair), then stay in a halal state." (Bukhari, chapter on Tamattu', Qiran, and Ifrad for those who... p. 213, no. 1568). In this hadith too, it states that in 'Umrah one should perform tawaf and sa'y, then become halal. These are the actions of 'Umrah.
Source pages p. 479

Commentary
This passage defines the essential components (arkan) of 'Umrah. 'Umrah consists of three acts: (1) entering the state of ihram (intention and recitation of talbiyah), (2) performing tawaf (seven circuits around the Ka'bah), and (3) performing sa'y (seven trips between Safa and Marwah). The author emphasizes that 'Umrah is the combination of these three elements. To support this, two hadith from Bukhari are cited. In the first, 'A'isha describes how the companions who had assumed ihram for 'Umrah during the Farewell Pilgrimage performed tawaf and sa'y and then exited ihram. The second hadith, via Abu Shihab, contains the Prophet's command to exit ihram for 'Umrah by performing tawaf and sa'y and then shortening the hair. Thus, these three acts (ihram, tawaf, sa'y) constitute the essential pillars of 'Umrah in the Hanafi school. Note that some schools include additional acts, but here the Hanafi position is clear.

Key Terms
احرام (iḥrām): The state of pilgrimage sanctity, entered by intention and talbiyah, with specific prohibitions.
طواف (ṭawāf): Circumambulation around the Ka'bah seven times, starting and ending at the Black Stone.
سعی (sa'y): Walking seven times between the hills of Safa and Marwah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The three pillars of 'Umrah are ihram, tawaf, and sa'y; omitting any one invalidates the 'Umrah.

Definition and Minimum Requirements of Hadi
Defines Hadi, lists types, specifies minimum and age.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition and types of Hadi, identify its minimum, and apply the age requirements for each animal type to determine validity.

Core Idea
Hadi is wajib for Tamattu' and Qiran; its minimum is a goat, and only adult animals (thani) suffice except for sheep where a six-month-old lamb (jadha') is acceptable.

This lesson clarifies the legal definition and requirements of Hadi, the sacrificial animal obligatory for those performing Tamattu' or Qiran Hajj. Based on the Quran and Sunnah, the Hanafi school specifies the permissible types, minimum number, and age conditions. Understanding these ensures the validity of one's Hadi obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what Hadi is and its legal status. Hadi is wajib for those performing Tamattu' or Qiran Hajj. The minimum is a goat.
The ruling is based on Quran 2:196.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence: Quran 2:196 and the athar of Ibn Abbas (Bukhari) and the hadith of Jabir (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Muslim).
The Quranic text commands offering what is easy of Hadi; the Sunnah interprets the minimum as a goat.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'fama istaysara min al-hady' indicates obligation. The unspecified quantity is defined by the Sunnah: a goat or equivalent. The hadith of Jabir allows jadha' for sheep.
The Quranic proof is qat'i in thubut but zanni in dalala; the Sunnah clarifies.
4
Note the age conditions and exceptions
For camels, cows, and goats: thani (adult) and above. For sheep: jadha' (six months) is sufficient if fat and strong. The term 'thani' is defined for each species.
Exception for sheep is based on the hadith of Jabir.
5
Evaluate the cross-madhhab status
The obligation of Hadi for Tamattu' and Qiran is muttafaq alayh. The age requirements are generally agreed, though some schools may require thani for sheep as well.
The Hanafi position is based on authentic proofs.

الهدى فقال فيها جزور او بقرة او شاة او شرک فی دم (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب فمن تجمع بالعمرة الى الحج فما استير من العدى ص ۲۲۸ نمبر ۱۶۸۸) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اونٹ، گائے اور بکری ہدی ہیں ۔ یا اونٹ اور گائے کا ساتواں حصہ ہو۔ [۷۹۸) (۲) ان تمام میں منی یا اس سے زیادہ عمر کا جانور کافی ہے مگر بھیٹر میں کہ اس کا جذع بھی ہدی میں کافی ہے۔ جانور کو جوانی کے دو دانت آنے کے بعد اس کوشنی کہا جاتا ہے۔ اور بھیٹر چھ ماہ کا ہو تو اس کو جذع کہتے ہیں۔ ہدی اور قربانی میں تمام جانور کاشنی ذبح کیا جائے گا لیکن بھیڑ میں اس کی گنجائش ہے کہ موٹا تگرا ہو تو جذع یعنی دانت سے پہلے کا جانور بھی کافی ہوگا۔ کیونکہ حدیث میں اس کی خصوصیت وارد ہوئی ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن جابر قال قال رسول الله لا تذبحوا الامسنة الا ان يعسر عليكم فتذبحوا جذعة من الضأن ( ج ) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب ما یجوز فی الضحايا من السن ج ثانی ص ۳۰ کتاب الضحایا نمبر ۲۷۹۷ / ترمذی شریف، باب في الجذع من الصان في الاضاحی ص ۲۷۶ ابواب الاضاحی نمبر ۱۴۹۹ر مسلم شریف ، باب من الاضحیۃ نمبر ۵۰۸۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اور جانوروں میں تھی ضروری ہے۔ اور بھیڑ میں چھ ماہ کا بچہ جس کو جذع کہتے ہیں وہ بھی کافی ہوگا بشرطیکہ موٹا تگڑا ہو۔ ات الثنی : نیا دانت آیا ہو، بکری دوسرے سال میں قدم رکھے تو مٹی ہوتی ہے۔ گائے بھینس دو سال کے بعد تیسرے میں قدم رکھے تو منی ہوتی ہیں۔ اونٹ چار سال پورے کر کے پانچویں سال میں قدم رکھے تو نیا دانت آتا ہے اور منی ہوتا ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) پس جب تم امن میں ہو جاؤ تو جس نے عمرے کو حج کے ساتھ ملا کر فائدہ حاصل کیا۔ پس ہدی میں سے جو آسان ہو وہ دو (ب) میں حضرت ابن عباس سے تمتع کے بارے میں سوال کیا تو انہوں نے مجھے اس کا حکم دیا۔ اور ان کو ہدی کے بارے میں پوچھا تو فرمایا اس میں اونٹ ہے یا گائے ہے یا بکری ہے یا جانور میں شرکت ہے (ج) آپ نے فرمایا مت ذبح کرو مگر منہ مگر تم پر تنگ دستی ہو تو بھیٹر کا جذع ذبح کرو۔
Chapter of Hadi. Book of Hajj. [797] (1) The Hadi: Its minimum is a goat, and it is of three types: camel, cow, and goat. [798] (2) In all of these, the thani and above suffices, except for sheep, for the jadha‘ from it suffices. Chapter of Hadi. Essential Note: Hadi is an animal sent to the Haram to be slaughtered. Its proof is in this verse: 'Then when you are secure, whoever performs Tamattu‘ of ‘Umrah to Hajj, then [offer] whatever is easy of the sacrificial animal' (Surah Baqarah 2:196). This verse proves Hadi. [797] (1) The minimum of Hadi is a goat, and it is of three types: camel, cow, and goat. Since no hadith proves giving less than a goat, therefore the goat is the minimum. (2) Abu Jamrah narrated: I asked Ibn ‘Abbas about Tamattu‘, and he ordered me to do it, and I asked him about Hadi, and he said: In it is a camel, or a cow, or a goat, or a share in the blood (i.e., a partner). (b) (Bukhari, Chapter: 'Whoever performs Tamattu‘ of ‘Umrah to Hajj, then whatever is easy of the sacrificial animal' p. 228, no. 1688) From this athar it is known that camel, cow, and goat are Hadi, or a seventh share of a camel or cow. [798] (2) In all of these, a thani (adult) or older suffices, except for sheep, for its jadha‘ also suffices in Hadi. An animal is called thani when its two permanent teeth have come after youth. And a sheep at six months is called jadha‘. In Hadi and sacrifice, all animals must be slaughtered as thani, but for sheep there is leeway that if it is fat and strong, then jadha‘, i.e., the animal before the tooth, also suffices. Because a hadith has come specifying its exemption. In a hadith from Jabir: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: Do not slaughter except a musinnah (adult), unless it is difficult for you, then slaughter a jadha‘ from sheep. (c) (Abu Dawud, Chapter on what is permissible in sacrifice regarding age, vol. 2, p. 30, Book of Sacrifices, no. 2797; Tirmidhi, Chapter on jadha‘ from sheep for sacrifices, p. 276, Chapters of Sacrifices, no. 1499; Muslim, Chapter on Sacrifice, no. 5082) From this hadith it is known that for other animals thani is necessary, and for sheep a six-month-old lamb, called jadha‘, also suffices provided it is fat and strong. The explanation of thani: A new tooth has appeared. A goat is thani when it enters its second year. A cow/buffalo is thani after two years, entering the third. A camel is thani when it completes four years and enters the fifth, when a new tooth appears. Footnote: (a) 'Then when you are secure, whoever performs Tamattu‘ of ‘Umrah to Hajj, then offer whatever is easy of the sacrificial animal.' (b) I asked Ibn ‘Abbas about Tamattu‘, and he ordered me to do it, and I asked him about Hadi, and he said: In it is a camel, or a cow, or a goat, or partnership in an animal. (c) He (the Prophet) said: Do not slaughter except a musinnah, but if you are in hardship, then slaughter a jadha‘ of sheep.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage from al-Sharh al-Thamiri explains the ruling on Hadi, the sacrificial animal required for Tamattu‘ and Qiran Hajj. The author defines Hadi as an animal sent to the Haram for slaughter, citing Quran 2:196 as evidence. He states that the minimum Hadi is a goat, based on the absence of any hadith allowing something less. The permissible types are camels, cows, and goats, and one may also share in a camel or cow (up to seven partners per animal). The age requirement is thani (adult) for camels, cows, and goats. Thani for a goat is at one year, for a cow at two years, for a camel at four years entering the fifth. However, for sheep, a jadha‘ (six-month-old lamb) is sufficient if it is fat and strong, as explicitly stated in a hadith from Jabir narrated in Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Muslim. The passage clarifies the conditions for Hadi and distinguishes it from ordinary sacrifice (udhiyah), though similar rules apply. The footnotes provide the verbatim hadith and Quranic verse.

Key Terms
هدى (Hadi): An animal (camel, cow, goat) sent to the Haram to be slaughtered as a sacrifice for Tamattu‘ or Qiran Hajj.
ثنى (Thani): An animal that has reached the age of adulthood: goat at 1 year, cow at 2 years, camel at 4 years entering 5th.
جذع (Jadha‘): A young sheep (lamb) that is six months old, which suffices for Hadi if it is fat and strong.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum age for a camel to be valid as Hadi?
A) One year old (jadha‘)
B) Two years old
C) Four years old entering the fifth (thani)
D) Five years old

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires Hadi as a wajib for Tamattu' and Qiran, with a minimum of a goat and age conditions: thani for camel, cow, goat; jadha' for sheep if fat and strong.

Types and Minimum Age of Hady Animals
Ruling on the types and minimum age of hady animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three types of hady animals and the minimum age requirement for each, and identify the proof from hadith that permits jadha' sheep.

Core Idea
For hady, a thani is required for camel, cow, and goat; a fat jadha' sheep suffices.

The hady (sacrificial animal) is an essential obligation for those performing hajj tamattu' or qiran. This passage outlines which animals qualify and at what age. The Hanafi school, based on hadith from Ibn Abbas and Jabir, allows a sheep as young as six months (jadha') if it is fat and strong, while all other animals must have reached the thani stage (second year or older). Understanding these conditions ensures your hady is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three valid types of hady
From the hadith of Ibn Abbas, the Prophet (peace be upon him) listed camel, cow, and goat (sheep is included under goat). These are the only animals that can be offered as hady.
2
Determine the minimum age for each type
For camel, cow, and goat, the animal must be thani (full-grown, having lost its first incisors). For sheep, a jadha' (six-month-old) is sufficient if it is fat and strong.
Thani definitions: camel: 5 years old; cow/buffalo: 3 years old; goat: 2 years old.
3
Locate the proofs
The hadith from Ibn Abbas lists the types. The hadith from Jabir explicitly allows jadha' sheep when musinnah (thani) is unavailable.
Both hadith are ahad but accepted by the Hanafi school.
4
Recognize the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i requires thani for sheep as well, rejecting the jadha'. The Hanafi school takes the exception as valid based on stronger evidence.
The practical difference: Shafi'is cannot use jadha' sheep for hady.

Chapter of Hady, Book of Hajj. [797] The lowest of hady is a goat, and it is of three types: camel, cow, and sheep. [798] In all of these, a thani (full-grown) and above suffices except for sheep, for its jadha' (young) suffices. Chapter of Hady. Essential note: Hady is an animal sent to the Haram to be slaughtered. Its proof is in this verse: 'Then when you are secure, whoever performs 'umrah combined with hajj, [offer] whatever is available of the hady' (Quran 2:196). This verse proves hady. [797] (1) The lowest hady is a goat, and it is of three types: camel, cow, and sheep. Since there is no hadith proving anything lower than a goat, the goat is the lowest. (2) Abu Jamrah narrated: I asked Ibn 'Abbas about tamattu' and he commanded me to do it. I asked him about hady, and he said: 'In it there is a camel, or a cow, or a goat, or a share in the blood.' (Bukhari) From this effect, it is known that camel, cow, and goat are hady, or a seventh share of a camel or cow. [798] (2) In all these, a thani or older animal suffices, except for sheep, for its jadha' also suffices in hady. The animal after the emergence of two permanent incisors is called thani. And a sheep at six months is called jadha'. In hady and udhiyah, all animals should be thani, but for sheep there is concession that if it is fat and strong, a jadha' (before incisors) also suffices. Because a hadith specifies this. The hadith: from Jabir: 'The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Do not slaughter except musinnah, except if it is difficult for you, then slaughter a jadha' of sheep.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Muslim) From this hadith, it is known that in other animals, thani is necessary, and in sheep, a six-month-old jadha' suffices provided it is fat and strong. Explanation of thani: A new incisor has appeared; a goat in its second year becomes thani; a cow or buffalo after two years entering the third becomes thani; a camel after completing four years entering the fifth becomes thani. Footnotes: (a) 'Then when you are secure...' (b) I asked Ibn Abbas about tamattu'... (c) The Prophet said: Do not slaughter except musinnah...

Commentary
This passage states the types and minimum age of animals valid for hady (the sacrificial animal sent to the Haram by those performing hajj tamattu' or qiran). The text begins by defining hady and citing its Quranic proof. It then presents the ruling: the lowest acceptable hady is a goat, and the types are camels, cows, and sheep. The author supports this with a hadith from Ibn Abbas listing the options. Next, the text addresses age: in all these animals, a thani (one that has reached the second year and lost its first incisors) or older is required, except for sheep where a jadha' (six months old) is sufficient if it is fat and strong. The proof is the hadith from Jabir that allows jadha' in sheep when musinnah is unavailable. The commentary in Urdu clarifies the definitions of thani and jadha' for each species. The Hanafi position is that these are the minimum requirements; for the validity of hady, these conditions must be met.

Key Terms
ثنى (مثنى) (thani): An animal that has entered its second year and has lost its first two incisors; for a goat: in its second year; for a cow/buffalo: after two years; for a camel: after four years.
جذع (jadha'): A young sheep that has not yet lost its incisors, typically around six months old and strong.
هدى (hady): The sacrificial animal sent to the Haram by the pilgrim performing hajj tamattu' or qiran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The minimum age for hady is thani for camel, cow, and goat, and jadha' for sheep if fat and strong.

Defects that Invalidate Hady Animals
Listing defects that disqualify an animal from being hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the major defects that invalidate a hady animal and explain the evidence from the ahadith, as well as identify the exception for defects less than one-third.

Core Idea
A hady animal must be free from major defects; only defects affecting less than one-third are excused.

This lesson examines the specific physical defects that disqualify an animal from being offered as hady during Hajj. The Hanafi school, drawing on multiple ahadith, establishes clear criteria for a sound animal. Understanding these defects ensures that the offering is made in the best form, befitting the worship of Allah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
Read the opening statement: 'It is not permissible in hady...' and list the defects mentioned.
Note that the ruling covers both complete loss and major partial loss (e.g., 'most of the ear').
2
Categorize the defects by body part
Group the defects: ear, tail, limbs, eye, overall emaciation, and lameness.
This helps memorize the list.
3
Examine the three ahadith as evidence
The first hadith from Bara' gives four categories; the second adds specific terms; the third from 'Ali details ear defects. Compare them.
Note that the Hanafi school applies these to hady by analogy (qiyas).
4
Apply the one-third exception
The passage concludes that if the defect is less than one-third, it is acceptable. Understand this as a concession.
This exception is specific to the Hanafi school.
5
Summarize the practical ruling
State which animals are invalid and which are acceptable based on the one-third rule.
This is the mufta bihi.

(۱) ہدی اللہ کے بارگاہ میں پیش ہوتی ہے اس لئے اچھا جانور ہو، عیب دار جانور انسان بھی پسند نہیں کرتا تو اللہ کی بارگاہ میں کیسے پیش کیا جائے؟ (۲) حدیث میں ہے سألت براء بن عازب مالا يجوز في الاضاحي فقال قام فينا رسول الله ... فقال اربع لا تجوز في الاضاحي العوراء بين عورها والمريضة بين مرضها والعرجاء بين طلعها والكسيرة التي لا تنقى (الف) (ابو داؤد شریف ، باب ما يكره من الضحاياج ثانی ص ۳۱ کتاب الضحایا نمبر ۲۸۰۲ / ترمذی شریف ، باب مالا یجوز من الاضاحی ص ۳۶۴ نمبر ۱۴۹۷) دوسری حدیث میں ہے قال اتيت عتبة بن عبـد سـلـمـى ... انما نهى رسول الله عن المصفرة والمستأصلة والبخـقاء والمشيعة والكسراء، فالمصفرة التي تستاصل اذنها حتى يبلاو سماخها ، والمستأصلة التي استؤصل قرنها من اصله ، والبخقاء التي تبخق عينها المشيعة التي لا تتبع الغنم عجفا و ضعفا والكسراء الكسيرة (ب)(نمبر ۲۸۰۳) (۳) تیسری حدیث میں ہے عن على قال امرنا رسول الله ان نستشرف العين والاذن ولا نضحي بعوراء ولا مقابلة ولا مدابرة ولا خرقاء ولا شرقاء قال زهير فقلت لابی اسحاق اذكر عضباء وقال لا قلت فما المقابلة ؟ قال يقطع طرف الاذن فقلت فما المدابرة ؟ قال يقطع من مؤخر الاذن قلت فما الشرقاء ؟ قال تشق الاذن قلت فما الخرقاء ؟ قال تخرق اذنها للسمة (ج) (ابودا او شریف ، باب ما یکرہ من الضحاياج ثانی ص ۳۲/۳۱ کتاب الضحا یا نمبر ۲۸۰۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کان کٹا ہوا ، دم کٹی ہوئی، ہاتھ کٹا ہوا۔ پاؤں کٹا ہوا، نابینا ہنگڑا اور عضو کٹا ہوا یا خراب ہو تو قربانی اور ہدی میں نہیں چلے گا۔ اور تہائی سے کم ہوتو وہ چل جائے گا۔
[799] And it is not permissible in hady: an animal with the ear completely cut off, nor most of it, nor with the tail cut off, nor with the hand cut off, nor the foot, nor blind, nor emaciated, nor lame that cannot walk. [799] It is not permissible in hady: an ear completely cut off, nor most of it, nor a tail cut, nor a hand cut, nor a foot cut, nor a blind eye, nor emaciated, nor lame that cannot walk to the place. (1) Hady is presented to Allah, so it should be a good animal; a defective animal is not liked by humans, so how can it be presented to Allah? (2) The hadith: I asked Bara' ibn 'Azib what is not permissible in udhiyah, and he said: The Messenger of Allah stood among us and said: 'Four are not permissible in udhiyah: the clearly blind, the clearly sick, the clearly lame, and the broken-boned that has no marrow.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi) Another hadith: I came to 'Utba ibn 'Abd Sulami... The Messenger of Allah forbade al-musfara (ear scooped out), al-musta'sila (horn removed from root), al-bakhqa' (blind), al-mushayya'a (weak that cannot follow the flock), and al-kasra' (broken-limbed). Al-musfara is one whose ear is uprooted until its ear canal is visible; al-musta'sila is one whose horn is removed from its root; al-bakhqa' is one whose eye is blind; al-mushayya'a is one that does not follow the sheep due to weakness; al-kasra' is the broken one. (Abu Dawud no. 2803) (3) A third hadith: From 'Ali: The Messenger of Allah commanded us to examine the eye and the ear, and not to sacrifice a one-eyed animal, nor a muqabila (ear slit at front), nor a mudabbira (ear slit at back), nor a kharqa' (ear slit vertically), nor a sharqa' (ear split). Zuhayr said: I asked Abu Ishaq: Did he mention 'adba'? He said no. I asked: What is muqabila? He said: The tip of the ear is cut. I asked: What is mudabbira? He said: The back of the ear is cut. I asked: What is sharqa'? He said: The ear is split. I asked: What is kharqa'? He said: The ear is pierced for branding. (Abu Dawud no. 2804) From these hadiths, it is known that ear cut, tail cut, hand cut, foot cut, blind, lame, and any cut or damaged limb are not acceptable in udhiyah and hady. And if it is less than one-third, it is acceptable.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage lists the defects that render a hady animal invalid. The text begins by stating the ruling in Arabic: animals with the ear completely cut or most of it, tail cut, hand cut, foot cut, blind, emaciated, or lame that cannot walk are not allowed. The commentary explains the reasoning: hady is offered to Allah, so it should be of good quality; defective animals are not presented. Then three ahadith are cited as proof. The first from Bara' ibn 'Azib lists four: clearly blind, clearly sick, clearly lame, and extremely emaciated. The second from 'Utba names additional defects: musfara (ear scooped), musta'sila (horn removed), bakhqa' (blind), mushayya'a (too weak to follow), and kasra' (broken). The third from 'Ali lists muqabila (ear tip cut), mudabbira (back of ear cut), kharqa' (ear pierced for branding), and sharqa' (ear split). These hadiths indicate that major defects render the animal invalid. The commentary adds that if the defect is less than one-third, it may be acceptable. The Hanafi school relies on these hadiths to establish that animals with these defects are not valid for hady or udhiyah.

Key Terms
مقطوع الاذن (maqtu' al-udhun): An animal whose ear is completely cut off.
العفجاء (al-'afja'): An extremely emaciated animal.
العرجاء التي لا تمشى (al-'arja' allati la tamshi): A lame animal that cannot walk to the place of slaughter.
الكسيرة (al-kasira): A broken-boned animal that has no marrow (extremely emaciated).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Clearly blind
B) Clearly sick
C) Animal with a broken horn
D) A lame animal that is clearly lame

Key Takeaway
A hady animal must be free from major defects as specified in the hadith; minor defects affecting less than one-third are acceptable.

Disqualifying Defects in Sacrificial Animals
Lists eight specific defects that invalidate a sacrificial animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the eight defects that disqualify an animal for hadi and udhiyah, identify them from hadith proofs, and apply the Hanafi rule that defects less than one-third are acceptable.

Core Idea
An animal with a missing or severely defective limb is invalid for sacrifice; minor defects are overlooked.

Sacrificial animals in Islam must be free from significant defects to be acceptable to Allah. This lesson details the specific disqualifying conditions for hadi (sacrifice during Hajj) and udhiyah (Eid al-Adha sacrifice) according to the Hanafi school. We will examine eight explicit defects, their proofs from the Sunnah, and the crucial threshold of one-third for minor imperfections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Recognize that the ruling applies to both hadi and udhiyah. The general ruling is that an animal with any of the listed defects is not permissible for sacrifice.
The passage uses 'al-hadi' but the hadiths refer to 'al-adahi' (sacrifices); the Hanafi school applies the same rules to both.
2
List the eight disqualifying defects
From the text, enumerate: (1) completely cut ear or most of it, (2) cut tail, (3) cut hand or foot, (4) lost eye, (5) extreme emaciation (al-'afja'), (6) lameness preventing walking, (7) severe illness, (8) extreme old age (in hadith). Note that some defects are from the main ruling and others from the hadiths.
The passage also mentions defects from the hadiths like horn removal, ear mutilation, etc., which are sub-categories.
3
Analyze the hadith proofs
Three hadiths are cited. The first lists four general defects. The second adds specific ear and horn defects. The third adds ear mutilation types. Understand that these hadiths collectively establish the prohibition.
The hadiths are from Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi, showing that the ruling is based on ahad hadith (zanni thubut).
4
Apply the one-third rule
The commentary states that if the defect is less than one-third of the part, it is acceptable. This is a Hanafi specification not explicit in the hadiths. Distinguish between total defect (e.g., complete blindness) and partial.
This rule is derived from the general principle of excusing a small amount, analogous to other fiqh rulings.
5
Test with a scenario
Given a hypothetical animal with a small cut on the ear (less than one-third) but otherwise healthy, the ruling would be that it is valid. If the ear is completely cut, it is invalid.

[799 (3)] It is not permissible in the hadi (sacrificial animal): one whose ear is completely cut off, nor most of it, nor one whose tail is cut off, nor one whose hand is cut off, nor foot, nor one whose eye is gone, nor the lean one, nor the lame one that cannot walk to the place of sacrifice. (1) The hadi is presented before Allah, so the animal should be good. A defective animal is not liked even by humans, so how can it be presented before Allah? (2) Hadith: I asked al-Bara' ibn 'Azib what is not permissible in udhiyah? He said: The Messenger of Allah stood among us and said: Four (animals) are not permissible in udhiyah: the blind with clear blindness, the sick with clear sickness, the lame with clear lameness, and the broken (old) that has no marrow. (a) (Abu Dawud, 2802; Tirmidhi, 1497) Second hadith: I came to 'Utbah ibn 'Abd al-Sulami... the Messenger of Allah forbade the musfara, musta'sala, bakhqa', mushi'a, and kusra'. Musfara is one whose ear is pulled out from the root until the brain is seen; musta'sala is one whose horn is removed from the root; bakhqa' is one whose eye is blind; mushi'a is one that does not follow the sheep due to emaciation and weakness; kusra' is the broken one. (b) (No. 2803) (3) Third hadith: From 'Ali: The Messenger of Allah commanded us to examine the eye and ear, and not to sacrifice a blind (one-eyed) animal, nor muqabala, nor mudabara, nor kharqa', nor sharqa'. Zuhayr said: I asked Abu Ishaq: Did he mention 'adba'? He said no. I asked: What is muqabala? He said: The tip of the ear is cut. I asked: What is mudabara? He said: Cut from the back of the ear. I asked: What is sharqa'? He said: The ear is slit. I asked: What is kharqa'? He said: The ear is pierced for branding. (c) (Abu Dawud, 2804) From this hadith it is understood that an animal with cut ear, cut tail, cut hand, cut foot, blind, lame, or with a cut or defective limb is not valid for sacrifice or hadi. And if the defect is less than one-third, it is acceptable. The translation of the hadith also includes the translation of the defects. Footnote: (a) ... (b) ... (c) ...
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage begins by stating a ruling: certain defects disqualify an animal from being used as a hadi (sacrificial animal sent to the Haram) or udhiyah (sacrificial animal slaughtered on Eid al-Adha). The defects listed are: completely cut ear or most of it, cut tail, cut hand or foot, loss of an eye, extreme emaciation (al-'afja'), and lameness so severe the animal cannot walk to the slaughter place. The commentary then provides a rationale: since the animal is presented to Allah, it should be of good quality; even humans dislike defective gifts. Three hadith are cited as proof. The first hadith from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib reports that the Prophet prohibited four types: one-eyed, sick, lame, and extremely old. The second hadith prohibits animals with certain ear defects, horn removal, blindness, weakness, and broken limbs. The third hadith, from 'Ali, adds prohibitions of animals with specific ear mutilations. The Urdu commentary summarizes that these defects render the animal invalid, but if the defect is less than one-third, it is acceptable. The footnote explains the Arabic terms for each defect.

Key Terms
الهدي (al-hadi): The sacrificial animal sent to the Haram, especially during Hajj.
العفجاء (al-'afja'): An extremely emaciated animal with little flesh.
العرجاء (al-'arja'): A lame animal that cannot walk to the place of slaughter.
الكسيرة (al-kusra'): An extremely old animal with no marrow in its bones, as mentioned in the hadith.
المصفرة (al-musfara): An animal whose ear is pulled out from the root until the brain is visible.
المستأصلة (al-musta'sala): An animal whose horn is removed from the root.
البخقاء (al-bakhqa'): An animal whose eye is blind (usually one eye).
المشيعة (al-mushi'a): An animal that is too weak and emaciated to follow the herd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Which of the following defects disqualifies a sacrificial animal according to this passage?
A) A small cut on the ear (less than one-third)
B) Complete loss of one eye
C) Slight limping that does not prevent walking
D) A missing horn

Key Takeaway
An animal for sacrifice must be free from defined major defects; minor imperfections (less than one-third) are excused.

Two Exceptions to the Sheep Rule in Hajj Expiation
Ruling with proof on expiation animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hajj violations that require a camel instead of a sheep and explain the Hanafi proofs for each.

Core Idea
For most Hajj violations a sheep suffices, but major impurity during Tawaf al-Ziyarah and intercourse before it demand a camel.

In Hanafi fiqh, a sheep is the standard expiation (dam) for most violations of ihram. However, this passage highlights two serious violations where only a camel is acceptable. Understanding these exceptions is crucial for correctly fulfilling the expiation requirements during Hajj. Let us examine the rulings and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule and exceptions
Identify the overarching rule that a sheep is valid for all expiations, then note the two specific exceptions.
The exceptions are Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah and intercourse after 'Arafah.
2
Analyze the first exception: Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah
Understand why tawaf requires purity: the hadith equating tawaf to prayer (al-ṭawāfu ḥawla al-bayti mithlu al-ṣalāh). Since prayer is invalid without purity, tawaf also requires it. However, because tawaf is of a lower degree, the tawaf is still valid but a heavy expiation (camel) is wajib.
The hadith from Ibn 'Abbas is cited as a proof.
3
Analyze the second exception: Intercourse after 'Arafah
This violation occurs after the essential part of Hajj but before the obligatory tawaf. The athar from Ibn 'Abbas explicitly requires a camel (badanah) for this transgression.
The athar is narrated by Bayhaqi.
4
Derive the ruling from the proofs
Combine the textual evidence: the hadith establishes purity for tawaf, and the athar specifies the camel for intercourse before tawaf. The Hanafi school considers both proofs zanni but sufficient to impose a wajib expiation.
The authority_weight is fatawa mutakhkhirin, meaning this is the established position.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab differences
Other schools may allow a cow or sheep for these violations, but Hanafis insist on a camel. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is a heavier financial obligation for the Hanafi pilgrim.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text

المعجفاء : جو بہت دبلا پتلا جانور ہو۔ العرجا : لنگڑا ۔ المنسک : نسک سے مشتق ہے جہاں جانور ذبح کیا جاتا ہے۔ ٨٠٠] (٤) بکری ہر چیز میں جائز ہے مگر دو جگہوں میں (١) جس نے طواف زیارت جنبی ہو کر کیا (٢) اور جس نے وقوف عرفہ کے بعد جماع کیا۔ پس ان دونوں میں اونٹ کے علاوہ جائز نہیں ہے۔
یہ دونوں مسئلے اوپر گزر چکے ہیں۔ جن کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ طواف میں وضو اور طہارت شرط ہے لیکن اس کے برخلاف طواف زیارت جو فرض ہے اس کو جنابت کی حالت میں کیا اس لئے طواف تو ہو جائے گا لیکن اغلظ جنابت ہے اس لئے بکری کی بجائے اونٹ لازم ہوگا، اور بہتر یہ ہے کہ اس طواف کو دوبارہ لوٹا لے تو کچھ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ طہارت کے بغیر طواف زیارت کیا ہو تو گویا کہ طواف کیا ہی نہیں اس لئے طواف زیارت جو اہم ہے اس میں اہم جانوراونٹ لا زم ہوگا۔ طہارت کی وجہ یہ حدیث ہے ۔ عن ابن عباس ان النبی الا الله قال الطواف حول البيت مثل الصلوة الا انكم تتكلمون فيه فمن تكلم فيه فلا يتكلم الا بخير (الف) ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الکلام فی الطواف ص١٩٠ نمبر ٩٦٠ رنسائی شریف، باب اباحته الکلام فی الطواف ج ثانی ص ٢٨ نمبر ٢٩٢٦) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف نماز کی طرح ہے۔ اور نماز بغیر طہارت کے نہیں ہوتی اس لئے طواف بھی بغیر طہارت کے نہیں ہوگا۔ اور کر لیا تو دم دینا ہو گا (٢) دوسری حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة انها قالت قدمت مكة وانا حائض ولم اطف بالبيت ولا بين الصفا والمروة قالت فشكوت ذلك الى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال افعلى كما يفعل الحاج غير ان لا تطوفي بالبيت حتى تطهری (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب تقضی الحائض المناسک کلھا الا الطواف بالبيت ص٢٢٣ نمبر ١٦٥٠) اس حدیث سے بھی پتہ چلا کہ بغیر طہارت کے طواف نہ کرے اور کیا تو دم یا صدقہ لازم ہوگا ۔ البتہ چونکہ طواف کا درجہ نماز سے کم ہے اس لئے طواف کی ادائیگی ہو جائے گی۔ تاہم جب تک مکہ مکرمہ میں ہو تو اس طواف کو دوبارہ لوٹا لینا چاہئے پھر دم یا صدقہ لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ اور وقوف عرفہ کے بعد اور طواف زیارت سے پہلے جماع کرنے پر اونٹ لازم ہوگا۔ اس کی دلیل بی اثر ہے عن ابن عباس اتاه رجل فقال وطنت امرأتي قبل ان اطوف بالبيت قال عندک شیء؟ قال نعم انی موسر قال فانحر ناقة سمينة فاطعمها المساكين (ج) (سنن ابیھقی ، باب الرجل يصيب امرأته بعد التحلل الاول وقبل الثانی ج خامس ص ٢٧٩، نمبر٩٧٩٩) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف زیارت سے پہلے جماع کر لیا تو ایک اونٹ دینا ہو گا۔ اسی طرح دوسرے اثر میں ہے عن ابن عباس انه سئل عن رجل
(الف) آپ نے فرمایا بیت اللہ کے گرد طواف نماز کی طرح ہے۔ مگر اس میں بات کرتے ہو۔ اس لئے جو بات کرے وہ خیر ہی کی بات کرے(ب) حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں کہ میں مکہ مکرمہ آئی اور حائضہ تھی۔ اور بیت اللہ کا طواف نہیں کیا تھا اور نہ صفا مروہ کے درمیان، فرمایا میں نے حضور سے اس کی شکایت کی تو فرمایا جیسا حاجی کرتے ہیں ویسا ہی کرو مگر یہ کہ بیت اللہ کا طواف نہ کرو جب تک پاک نہ ہو جاؤ (ج) حضرت ابن عباس کے پاس ایک آدمی آیا۔ کہا میں نے اپنی بیوی سے بیت اللہ
کے طواف سے پہلے ولی کی۔ ابن عباس نے پوچھا تمہارے پاس کچھ ہے؟ کہا ہاں ! میں مالدار ہوں۔ کہا موٹی اومنی ذبح کرو اور مسکین کو کھلاؤ۔
[800] (4) The sheep is permissible for everything except in two situations: one who makes the Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of major impurity (janabah), and one who has intercourse after standing at 'Arafah. For these two, nothing is permissible except a camel. The extremely lean animal; the lame; al-mansak is derived from nusuk, the place where animals are slaughtered. [800] (4) A goat is permissible in everything except two places: (1) one who performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in janabah, (2) and one who had intercourse after standing at 'Arafah. In these two, nothing other than a camel is permissible. These two issues have passed earlier. Their detail is that wudu and purity are conditions for tawaf, but contrary to that, Tawaf al-Ziyarah which is fard was performed in janabah; so the tawaf will be valid, but because it is grave impurity, a camel is required instead of a goat. And it is better to repeat that tawaf, then nothing is required. If Tawaf al-Ziyarah is done without purity, it is as if he did not perform tawaf at all, so a camel is required. The reason for purity is this hadith: From Ibn 'Abbas that the Prophet said: 'Tawaf around the House is like prayer, except that you speak in it; so whoever speaks in it, let him speak only good.' (a) (Tirmidhi 960; Nasai 2926) From this hadith it is understood that tawaf is like prayer. And prayer is not valid without purity, so tawaf is also not valid without purity. And if one performs it, he must give a dam. (2) Second hadith: From 'Aisha that she said: I came to Makkah while menstruating and did not perform tawaf of the House nor between Safa and Marwah. She said: I complained to the Messenger of Allah, and he said: 'Do as the pilgrims do, except do not perform tawaf of the House until you become pure.' (b) (Bukhari 1650) From this hadith it is also understood that one should not perform tawaf without purity, and if he does, it will require a dam or sadaqah. However, since tawaf is of a lower degree than prayer, the tawaf is valid. Nevertheless, as long as he is in Makkah, he should repeat that tawaf; then no dam or sadaqah is required. And if intercourse occurs after 'Arafah and before Tawaf al-Ziyarah, a camel is required. The proof is this athar: From Ibn 'Abbas: A man came to him and said: I had intercourse with my wife before performing tawaf of the House. He said: Do you have anything? He said: Yes, I am wealthy. He said: Slaughter a fat camel and feed the poor. (c) (Bayhaqi, no. 9799) From this athar it is understood that if one has intercourse before Tawaf al-Ziyarah, he must give one camel. Similarly, in another athar: From Ibn 'Abbas that he was asked about a man...
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage states a general rule: a sheep (or goat) is acceptable for all expiatory sacrifices (dam) required during Hajj, except for two specific cases: (1) performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of janabah (major ritual impurity), and (2) having sexual intercourse after the stand at 'Arafah (i.e., after the essential part of Hajj) but before completing Tawaf al-Ziyarah. In both cases, a camel is required instead of a sheep. The commentary explains the reasoning: Tawaf al-Ziyarah is a fard (obligatory) act that requires ritual purity similar to prayer. However, unlike prayer, if one performs it without purity, the tawaf is valid but sinful, and a heavy expiation (camel) is due. It is better to repeat the tawaf to avoid the penalty. For the case of intercourse after 'Arafah, this violates the state of ihram before the final tawaf, and the required expiation is a camel, based on an athar from Ibn 'Abbas. The passage also mentions that a sheep can be used for other violations like dam for shaving hair, etc. The proof for tawaf requiring purity is the hadith equating tawaf to prayer, and the hadith of 'Aisha showing that a menstruating woman must wait until purity to perform tawaf.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf performed after the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), also called Tawaf al-Ifadah.
بدنة (badanah): A camel (or cow in some contexts) used as a sacrificial animal.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (usually a sheep) required as expiation for certain violations in Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) A sheep
B) A camel
C) A cow
D) Charity of one meal

Key Takeaway
A sheep is sufficient for most Hajj expiations, but performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah or intercourse after 'Arafah requires a camel.

Ruling: When a Goat is Not Permissible for Sacrifice in Hajj
States the general permissibility of a goat for sacrifice and its exceptions requiring a camel.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two cases where a goat is not permissible for sacrifice in Hajj and explain the Hanafi ruling that a camel is required, citing the supporting evidence.

Core Idea
A goat suffices for most Hajj sacrifices; only for Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah or intercourse after Wuquf, a camel is wajib.

In Hajj, most sacrificial penalties can be fulfilled with a goat. However, for two specific violations—performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of major impurity (janabah) or engaging in intercourse after standing at Arafah—the Hanafi school requires a camel. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its textual evidence, and the reasoning behind the stricter penalty, highlighting a key distinction between general permissibility and exceptional severity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The text begins by stating that a goat is permissible for almost every sacrifice. Recognize this as the default ruling.
The Arabic phrase 'في كل شيء' emphasizes comprehensiveness.
2
Examine the two exceptions
The passage then lists two specific cases where a goat is not enough: (1) Tawaf al-Ziyarah performed in janabah, (2) intercourse after Wuquf before Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Note that a camel is required.
These are severe violations of Hajj rites.
3
Analyze the rationale for tawaf with impurity
The commentary explains that tawaf requires purification, citing the hadith equating tawaf to prayer. However, because tawaf is not identical to prayer, the act is valid but the penalty is a camel.
The hadith 'tawaf around the House is like prayer...' is key.
4
Understand the proof for intercourse after Wuquf
The athar of Ibn Abbas orders a camel for a man who had intercourse before tawaf. This is the primary evidence for the camel requirement in this case.
This athar is accepted by Imam al-Shafi'i as well.
5
Compare with other schools
Imam Malik requires an additional Umrah and a complete Hajj beyond the camel. This highlights the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between the Hanafi and Maliki positions.
The Hanafi position is based on the explicit athar.
