[800] (4) And the goat is permissible in everything except in two cases: one who performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of janabah, and one who has intercourse after standing at Arafah. For these two, nothing but a camel is permissible. / Al-mu'jifaa: an extremely thin animal. Al-'arjaa: lame. Al-mansik: derived from nusk, the place where an animal is slaughtered. [800] (4) A goat is permissible in everything except in two places: (1) one who performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in janabah, and (2) one who had intercourse after Wuquf at Arafah. So for these two, nothing but a camel is permissible. / These two issues have passed above. Their detail is that wudu and purification are conditions for tawaf, but contrary to that, Tawaf al-Ziyarah which is obligatory was performed in a state of janabah, so the tawaf will be valid, but it is a severe janabah, so instead of a goat, a camel becomes incumbent. And it is better to repeat this tawaf, then nothing will be incumbent. If Tawaf al-Ziyarah is performed without purification, it is as if he did not perform tawaf at all, so since Tawaf al-Ziyarah is important, an important animal, a camel, becomes incumbent. The reason for purification is this hadith: from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet ﷺ said, 'Tawaf around the House is like prayer except that you speak in it, so whoever speaks should only speak good.' (at-Tirmidhi) From this hadith it is learned that tawaf is like prayer, and prayer is not valid without purification, so tawaf is also not valid without purification. And if he did it, he must give a dam. (2) In another hadith, from Aisha that she said, 'I came to Mecca while I was menstruating and I did not perform tawaf of the House nor between Safa and Marwa.' She said, 'I complained about that to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, and he said, "Do as the pilgrim does except do not perform tawaf of the House until you become pure."' (Bukhari) From this hadith also it is learned that one should not perform tawaf without purification, and if he did, then a dam or sadaqah becomes incumbent. However, since the rank of tawaf is lower than prayer, the performance of tawaf will be valid. Nevertheless, as long as he is in Mecca, he should repeat that tawaf, then dam or sadaqah will not be incumbent. And for intercourse after Wuquf at Arafah and before Tawaf al-Ziyarah, a camel becomes incumbent. Its proof is this athar: from Ibn Abbas that a man came to him and said, 'I had intercourse with my wife before I performed tawaf of the House.' He said, 'Do you have anything?' He said, 'Yes, I am wealthy.' He said, 'Slaughter a fat she-camel and feed the poor.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi) From this athar it is learned that if one has intercourse before Tawaf al-Ziyarah, he must give one camel. Similarly, in another athar, from Ibn Abbas that he was asked about a man who had intercourse with his family while he was in ihram and he was in Mina before he returned (ifadah), and he ordered him to slaughter a camel. Imam al-Shafi'i said: 'We take this.' Imam Malik said: 'Upon him is an Umrah, a camel, and a complete Hajj.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Muwatta Malik) From this athar it is learned that if one has intercourse before Tawaf al-Ziyarah, a camel is incumbent.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with supporting evidence. It states that a goat is generally permissible for sacrifice (hadi) except in two specific cases: (1) performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of janabah (major impurity), and (2) engaging in sexual intercourse after Wuquf at Arafah but before Tawaf al-Ziyarah. In both cases, only a camel suffices. The commentator explains the reasoning: Tawaf al-Ziyarah is an obligatory rite and performing it without purification is a severe offense, so a more significant animal is required. The hadith equating tawaf to prayer (from Ibn Abbas) establishes the need for purity, and the hadith of Aisha (from Bukhari) reinforces that tawaf should not be performed without purity. The athar from Ibn Abbas regarding intercourse before tawaf shows the requirement of a camel. The text also mentions the opinions of Imam al-Shafi'i (who agrees) and Imam Malik (who requires an Umrah, a camel, and a complete Hajj). The Hanafi position is that a camel is wajib in these two cases, and the ruling is based on the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
شاة (shah): A goat, permissible for most sacrifices
بدنة (badana): A camel, required for the two exceptional cases
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf of Hajj performed after Wuquf
جنب (junub): State of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl
وقوف بعرفة (wuquf bi-arafah): Standing at Arafah, the essential pillar of Hajj

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Tawaf al-Qudum and Tawaf al-Wada'; a camel is required
B) Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah and intercourse after Wuquf before Tawaf al-Ziyarah; a camel is required
C) Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah and intercourse after Tawaf al-Ziyarah; a goat is still permissible
D) Intercourse before Wuquf and after Tawaf al-Ziyarah; a cow is required

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a goat is generally valid for Hajj sacrifices, except for Tawaf al-Ziyarah in janabah and intercourse after Wuquf, where only a camel suffices.

Sharing a Camel or Cow for Sacrifice: The Condition of Qurbah
Ruling with proof from hadith and qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on sharing a camel or cow for sacrifice and explain the consequence if one partner intends meat instead of qurbah.

Core Idea
A shared sacrifice requires all partners to intend qurbah; one partner's meat intention invalidates the whole.

You may be asked whether a single cow can be sacrificed on behalf of a large family. The Hanafi school has a clear ruling: one camel or cow can suffice for up to seven persons, but only if every partner intends an act of worship (qurbah). If even one person merely wants meat, the entire sacrifice becomes invalid for all. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof from the Sunnah, and the reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sharing a camel or cow for sacrifice (hadi, udhiyah, or aqiqah). The ruling: it suffices for seven persons if all intend qurbah. If one intends meat, it does not suffice for the rest.
The ruling is about validity, not obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah: 'We sacrificed with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ at Hudaybiyyah a camel for seven and a cow for seven.'
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted as proof.
3
Understand the condition (qurbah)
Qurbah means the intention to draw near to Allah. All partners must have this intention. If even one intends meat (i.e., not qurbah), the sacrifice is invalid for all.
The animal is a single unit; defect in one share corrupts the whole.
4
Trace the qiyas (analogy) with salah
Just as missing one rukn invalidates the entire salah, so one partner's defective intention invalidates the entire sacrifice.
This is a shabahah qiyas based on the unity of the act of worship.
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Some schools allow sharing without the condition of all partners intending qurbah. The Hanafi school is strict: all must intend qurbah.
The practical consequence: if one partner's intention is doubtful, the entire sacrifice is in jeopardy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[801] (5) والبدنة والبقرة يجزئ كل واحد منهما عن سبعة انفس اذا كان كل واحد من الشركاء يريد القربة فاذا اراد احدهم بنصيبه اللحم لم يجز للباقين عن القربة [80](2) و يجوز الاكل من هدى التطوع والمتعة والقران
ا اونٹ اور گائے سات سات آدمیوں کی جانب سے کافی ہیں۔ اس سے زیادہ کی جانب سے نہیں۔ لیکن شرط یہ ہے کہ تمام شرکاء نے قربت کی نیت کی ہو۔ مثلا ہدی یا قربانی یا عقیقہ ادا کرنا چاہتے ہوں، اگر ان میں سے ایک نے بھی گوشت کھانے کی نیت کی تو ایک کے فساد کی وجہ سے باقی شرکاء کا بھی فساد لازم آئے گا اور کسی کی بھی قربت یعنی ہدی یا قربانی یا عقیقہ ادا نہیں ہوگا۔
جانور ایک ہے اس لئے ایک حصہ دار کی خامی سے پورے جانور میں خامی آئے گی اور ایک حصہ کے قربت کی ادائیگی نہ ہونے سے کسی کی بھی قربت کی ادائیگی نہیں ہوگی۔ جیسے نماز کے ایک رکن کی کمی سے پوری نماز فاسد ہوتی ہے۔ ایک اونٹ میں سات آدمی اور ایک گائے میں سات آدمی شریک ہونے کی حدیث یہ ہے عن جابر بن عبد الله قال نحرنا مع رسول الله الله عام الحديبية البدنة عن سبعة والبقرة عن سبعة (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب جواز الاشتراك فى الهدى واجزاء البدية والبقرة كل واحدة منها عن سبعة ، كتاب الحج ص 4224 نمبر 1318 /ابو داؤد شریف، باب البقر والجزور عن كم تجربی ج ثانی ص32 نمبر 2808) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اونٹ اور گائے اور بھینس سات حصہ داروں کی جانب سے کافی ہو سکتے ہیں۔ اس سے زیادہ کے نہیں۔
نصیب : حصہ
[801] (5) And the camel and the cow, each one of them suffices for seven persons, provided that each of the partners intends qurbah. So if one of them intends meat with his share, it does not suffice for the rest for qurbah. [80](2) And it is permissible to eat from the Hadi of tatawwu', tamattu', and qiran. / A camel and a cow are sufficient for seven persons each. Not more than that. But the condition is that all partners have the intention of qurbah. For example, they want to offer Hadi, sacrifice, or Aqiqah. If even one of them intended to eat meat, then due to the invalidation of one, the invalidation of the rest of the partners also becomes necessary, and none of their qurbah (i.e., Hadi, sacrifice, or Aqiqah) will be fulfilled. / The animal is one, so due to the defect of one partner, a defect arises in the entire animal, and since one share's qurbah is not fulfilled, no one's qurbah is fulfilled. Just as the deficiency of one pillar of prayer invalidates the entire prayer. The hadith about a camel and a cow being shared by seven persons is: from Jabir ibn Abdullah, he said: 'We sacrificed with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ in the year of Hudaybiyyah a camel for seven and a cow for seven.' (Muslim, no. 1318; Abu Dawud, no. 2808) From this hadith it is learned that a camel, a cow, and a buffalo can suffice for seven partners. Not more than that. / Nasib: share.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on sharing sacrificial animals. It states that one camel or cow is sufficient for up to seven persons, but only if all of them intend qurbah (drawing near to Allah) — i.e., they are performing an act of worship such as Hadi, Udhiyah (Qurbani), or Aqiqah. If even one partner intends merely to obtain meat (not worship), then the sacrifice is invalid for all, because the animal is a single unit and an invalid intention for part corrupts the whole. The commentator draws an analogy with prayer: if one rukn is missing, the entire prayer is invalid. The proof is the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah about sacrificing at Hudaybiyyah where a camel or cow was shared by seven people. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah. The Hanafi position is that the intention of qurbah is a condition for the validity of the sacrificial act when sharing.

Key Terms
قربة (qurbah): Intention of drawing near to Allah through an act of worship
بدنة (badana): A camel, can be shared by up to seven persons
بقرة (baqarah): A cow, can be shared by up to seven persons
نصيب (nasib): Share or portion in the animal

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) All partners must be wealthy
B) All partners must intend qurbah
C) The animal must be a male
D) The animal must be slaughtered at Mina

Key Takeaway
One camel or cow can be shared by up to seven persons, but all must intend qurbah; otherwise the entire sacrifice is invalid for everyone.

Permissibility of Eating from Voluntary, Tamattu' and Qiran Hadi
States the ruling that one may eat from the Hadi of tatawwu', tamattu', and qiran because they are not penalties

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the types of Hadi from which the donor may eat and explain the Hanafi rationale distinguishing these from penalty sacrifices.

Core Idea
The donor may eat from voluntary, tamattu', and qiran Hadi because they are gifts, not penalties.

This passage states a clear Hanafi ruling: the donor of certain types of sacrificial animals (Hadi) may eat from their meat. The key is understanding which Hadi types are included and why. This lesson will help you distinguish between Hadi offered as a gift of gratitude and penalty sacrifices, which have different rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is eating from the meat of a Hadi. The ruling is permissibility (ja'iz). Determine the hukm level: mubah.
Not obligatory or prohibited.
2
Distinguish the three permitted types
List the three types mentioned: Hadi al-tatawwu' (voluntary), Hadi al-tamattu', and Hadi al-qiran. Understand each context.
These are not penalties but offerings of joy.
3
Identify the rationale
The passage explains why: these Hadi are not 'dam al-jazaa' (penalty sacrifices) but rather gifts and celebrations.
This rationale is crucial for fiqh reasoning.
4
Contrast with penalty Hadi
Note the opposite ruling: for penalty sacrifices (e.g., dam for violating Hajj rules), the donor cannot eat; the meat must be given entirely in charity.
This distinction is often misunderstood.

[802] (6) And it is permissible to eat from the Hadi of tatawwu', tamattu', and qiran. / It is permissible to eat from the voluntary Hadi, and the Hadi of tamattu' and qiran. The Hadi of tatawwu', tamattu', and qiran are not as penalties but as gifts and joy, so the one who offers the Hadi can eat its meat and feed the poor and needy.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This passage is a simple ruling stating that the meat of certain types of Hadi (sacrificial animals) can be consumed by the donor. These are: (1) Hadi al-tatawwu' (voluntary sacrifice not required by Hajj), (2) Hadi al-tamattu' (sacrifice offered by one performing Hajj al-tamattu'), and (3) Hadi al-qiran (sacrifice offered by one performing Hajj al-qiran). The reason given is that these are not penalty sacrifices (dam al-jazaa) but rather offerings of gratitude and celebration. Therefore, the donor may eat from them and also give to the poor. This is the Hanafi position. The opposite would be penalty sacrifices like dam for violations, which must be given entirely in charity and cannot be eaten by the donor.

Key Terms
هدى التطوع (hadi al-tatawwu'): A voluntary sacrificial animal offered to seek Allah's pleasure
هدى التمتع (hadi al-tamattu'): The sacrifice required from a pilgrim performing Hajj al-tamattu'
هدى القرآن (hadi al-qiran): The sacrifice required from a pilgrim performing Hajj al-qiran

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Voluntary, tamattu', and qiran Hadi

D) All Hadi including penalty

Key Takeaway
The donor may eat from voluntary, tamattu', and qiran Hadi because these are gifts of gratitude, not penalty sacrifices.

Camel and Cow Sufficient for Seven Persons in Sacrifice
Ruling on sharing large animals among seven participants for devotional sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sharing a camel or cow among seven for a devotional sacrifice, identify the condition of unanimous devotional intent, and apply the hadith proof to determine validity.

Core Idea
If even one partner intends meat instead of devotion, the whole sacrifice is invalid.

This lesson examines a foundational ruling from the Hanafi matn: a camel or cow can be shared by up to seven people for an act of worship such as hady, qurbani, or aqiqah. However, the validity hinges on every single partner intending a devotional act (qurbah). The text provides the hadith of Jabir to support this ruling and draws an analogy to the integrity of prayer. Understanding this ruling is crucial for those performing collective sacrifices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is sharing a camel or cow for sacrifice. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) for up to seven persons.
2
Locate the condition
The text states the condition: each partner must intend qurbah. If one intends meat, the sacrifice is invalid for all.
3
Examine the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Jabir from Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud. Identify the operative phrase 'عن سبعة' which establishes permissibility of sharing among seven.
4
Understand the consequence
The commentary explains through an analogy: just as a missing pillar invalidates prayer, one partner's corrupt intention invalidates the whole animal because the animal is one unit. Also, exceeding seven partners invalidates.
Similarly, if the number exceeds seven, the act is invalid even with qurbah.

The camel and the cow, each one of them suffices for seven persons when each of the partners intends devotional act. So if one of them intends meat for his share, it does not suffice for the rest for the devotional act.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn stating that a camel or cow can be shared by up to seven people for a devotional sacrifice (hady, qurbani, aqiqah). The condition is that every partner must intend a devotional act, not merely obtaining meat. If even one partner intends the meat for consumption without devotional intent, the entire sacrifice becomes invalid for all. The text then provides the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah that they sacrificed with the Prophet at Hudaybiyyah, proving the permissibility of sharing. The commentary explains the analogy: just as one missing pillar invalidates the entire prayer, one partner's corrupt intention invalidates the whole animal.

بقرة (baqarah): A cow.
قربة (qurbah): Devotional act intended to draw near to Allah.
شركاء (shuraka'): Partners sharing in the sacrifice.

Eating from Voluntary, Tamattu, and Qiran Hady
Ruling permitting consumption of meat from certain types of hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating from voluntary, tamattu', and qiran hady and cite the proof from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
You may eat from voluntary and gratitude hady, but not from penalty sacrifices.

Many assume that all hady (sacrificial animals) in Hajj must be given away entirely to the poor. However, the Hanafi school teaches that the meat from certain types of hady – voluntary (nafl), tamattu', and qiran – may be consumed by the offerer. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its evidenciary basis from the Prophet's own practice.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Begin by identifying the core permission: it is permissible (ja'iz) to eat from the hady of tatawwu', tamattu', and qiran.
This applies only to these three types; other types (penalty, vow) have a different ruling.
2
Identify the types of hady
Distinguish between obligatory hady that is a penalty (jurm, jaza', nadhr) and those that are expressions of gratitude or devotion. The text specifies that voluntary, tamattu', and qiran are not penalties.
Tamattu and qiran hady are obligatory, but their nature is gratitude, not penalty.
3
Locate the evidence
Find the hadith quoted: the Prophet (peace be upon him) ate from meat and drank from broth of his hady. This action establishes permission.
The hadith is from Muslim and Abu Dawud; its chain is ahad, but sufficient for a ruling of permissibility.
4
Note the distinction from penalty hady
Examine the footnote citing Ibn Umar, who held that meat from penalty hady (badal al-sayd, nadhr) should not be eaten. This distinguishes the permission from those types.
The Hanafi position aligns with this distinction: penalty hady are not for the offerer's consumption.
5
Consider cross-madhhab differences
Recognize that some early scholars (e.g., Ata') allowed eating from tamattu hady as well. The Hanafi position is consistent with the majority view allowing consumption from these three types.
The ruling is not universally agreed; always check the specific type of hady.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز الاكل من هدى التطوع والمتعة والقران

نفلی ہدی اور تمتع کی ہدی اور قرآن کی ہدی جرمانے کے طور پر نہیں ہیں بلکہ انعام اور خوشی کے طور پر ہیں اس لئے ان کا گوشت خود ہدی کرنے والا کھا سکتا ہے۔ اور غرباء ومساکین کو بھی کھلا سکتا ہے۔

(حدیث) قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله فسأل عن القوم ... ثم انصرف الى المنحر فنحر ثلثا وستين بيده ثم اعطى عليا فنحر ما غبر واشركه فى هديه ثم ام من كل بدنة ببضعة فجعلت في قدر فطبخت فاكلا من لحمهما وشربا من مرقها (مسلم شریف، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۳۹۹ نمبر ۱۲۱۸ / ابوداؤد شریف، باب صفة حجته النبی ص ۲۷۱، نمبر ۱۹۰۵)
اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور نے ہدی کا گوشت کھایا اس لئے نقلی ہدی، قران اور تمتع کی ہدی کا گوشت کھانا جائز ہے۔

حاشیہ : (ب) ابن عمر سے منقول ہے کہ نہ کھایا جائے شکار کے بدلے کا گوشت اور نذر کی ہدی کا گوشت اور ان کے علاوہ کھایا جائے ، اور حضرت عطا نے فرمایا تمتع کا گوشت کھائے اور دوسروں کو کھلائے
And it is permissible to eat from the hady of voluntary (nafl), tamattu, and qiran.
Source pages p. 484

Commentary
This ruling states that one may consume the meat from three types of hady: voluntary sacrifice (nafl), the hady of tamattu, and the hady of qiran. The reason provided in the commentary is that these are not penalties (jurmāna) but rather gifts and expressions of joy. Therefore the person offering the sacrifice may eat from it and also feed the poor. The evidence is the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet ate from the meat of his hady during his farewell pilgrimage. The footnote also cites Ibn Umar and Ata' distinguishing between meat from penalties (not to be eaten) and other types (permissible to eat).

Key Terms
هدي التطوع (hady al-tatawwu'): Voluntary sacrifice offered in Hajj or Umrah, not obligatory.
هدي المتعة (hady al-tamattu'): Sacrifice required for one performing tamattu' Hajj.
هدي القران (hady al-qiran): Sacrifice required for one performing qiran Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Hady of nathr (vow)
C) Hady of tamattu'
D) Hady of shukr (thanksgiving)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the pilgrim to eat from the meat of voluntary, tamattu', and qiran hady because they are sacrifices of gratitude, not penalties.

Prohibition of Eating from Obligatory Penalty Hady
Ruling forbidding consumption of penalty hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on eating from obligatory penalty hady and identify the dalil that supports this ruling.

Core Idea
Obligatory penalty hady is expiation, not reward—its meat may not be eaten, only given to the poor.

In this lesson, we examine a key distinction in the types of hady: those offered as gifts or gratitude, and those offered as penalties for violations during ihram. The Hanafi school holds that the meat of penalty hady is prohibited for the one offering it, and must be distributed to the poor. The proof is drawn from a prophetic instruction concerning a defective sacrificial animal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is eating from 'the rest of the hady' (penalty hady). The ruling is impermissible (لا يجوز).
The term 'بقية الهدايا' refers to obligatory penalty hady as opposed to voluntary ones.
2
Distinguish the type of hady
Understand why this hady is different: it is a penalty (jinaya ka badla), an expiation (jurm), not a gift (in'am).
This distinction is crucial: voluntary hady (e.g., tamattu', qiran, nafl) are allowed to be eaten, but penalty hady are not.
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith where a man's hady became defective. The Prophet instructed him to sacrifice it and said: 'Do not eat from it, you nor any of your companions.'
The hadith is from Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, and Muwatta Malik.
4
Apply the analogy (qiyas)
The underlying cause (illa) is that the animal is obligatory upon the offerer as a penalty. The defective hady is also obligatory, so the same ruling applies.
This qiyas extends the specific incident to all obligatory penalty hady.
5
Conclude the obligation
The meat must be given to the poor, not eaten by the offerer. The ruling is haram.

Source Text

And it is not permissible to eat from the rest of the hady (i.e., the obligatory ones).
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This ruling distinguishes between two categories of hady: those that are gifts (nafl, tamattu', qiran) and those that are penalties (such as compensation for hunting or jinaya). The meat of the latter may not be eaten by the one offering it; it must be distributed to the poor. The proof is the hadith where a person had a defective hady and the Prophet instructed him to sacrifice it and not eat from it nor allow his companions to eat. The commentary reinforces that these are expiations, not rewards, hence the prohibition.

Key Terms
بقية الهدايا (baqiyyat al-hadaya): The rest of the hady – specifically those that are obligatory as penalties, not voluntary or gratitude sacrifices.
جنایت کا بدلہ (jinayat ka badla): Compensation for wrongs committed during ihram, such as killing game or sexual intercourse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) It must be distributed to the poor and not eaten by the offerer.
C) It may be eaten only by the offerer's family.
D) It may be sold and the proceeds used for charity.

Key Takeaway
Penalty hady is an expiation, so its meat is prohibited for the offerer and must be given entirely to the poor.

Ruling on Eating from Different Types of Hadi
States prohibition of eating from certain Hadi and permissibility from others

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between voluntary and compulsory Hadi and state the Hanafi ruling on eating from each type.

Core Idea
Voluntary Hadi is a gift you may eat; penalty Hadi is a fine you must give away.

Many pilgrims assume all sacrificial meat during Hajj is permissible to eat. However, Hanafi fiqh draws a critical distinction based on the purpose of the Hadi. This lesson examines the textual proofs from the Prophet's practice and commands to classify Hadi into two categories: those from which the donor may eat and those that must be given entirely in charity. Understanding this distinction prevents a common mistake and aligns practice with the Shari'ah's intent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of Hadi
First, recognize that the passage divides Hadi into two broad categories: voluntary (nafl, tamattu', qiran) and compulsory (penalty for errors or hunting compensation). The ruling on eating depends on this classification.
The Arabic terms used: نفل, قران, تمتع for voluntary; جنایات, جزاء الصيد for compulsory.
2
State the ruling for each type
For voluntary Hadi, eating is permissible (mubah). For penalty and compensation Hadi, eating is prohibited (haram) for the one who owes it.
The prohibition is limited to the donor; others may eat if given.
3
Examine the proofs
The Prophet's action of eating from his own Hadi (in the hadith of Jabir) establishes permissibility for voluntary types. The command not to eat from a defective Hadi (in the hadith of Musa al-Hudhali) indicates prohibition for compulsory types, as a defective animal is akin to a penalty.
Both ahadith are from Muslim and Abu Dawud respectively, with zanni thubut and dalala.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
Some companions (Ibn Umar, Tawus) prohibited eating from all Hadi, while others (Ata) permitted tamattu'. The Hanafi school adopts the distinction based on the combined evidence, and this is the mufta bihi position.
The Hanafi position is considered strongest because it reconciles both proofs.

It is not permissible to eat from the rest of the Hadi. (1) For example, the meat of the sacrifice (Qurbani) is a reward, so one can eat it and feed the poor. (2) It is mentioned in a hadith that the Prophet (PBUH) ate from the meat of Hadi: He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah and asked about the people... then he went to the place of sacrifice and sacrificed 63 with his hand, then gave to Ali who sacrificed the rest and made him share in his Hadi, then he took a piece from each camel and put it in a pot, cooked it, and both ate from the meat and drank the broth. (Muslim, etc.) From this hadith it is understood that the Prophet ate Hadi meat, so it is permissible to eat from nafl, qiran, and tamattu' Hadi. As for penalties and compensation for game, it is not permissible for the one who caused the penalty to eat. For this, there is the athar from Ibn Umar: 'One should not eat from the compensation for game and from vowed Hadi, but should eat from other than that.' And Ata said: 'He may eat and feed from tamattu'. (Bukhari) (3) It is narrated from Ibn Abbas regarding a pigeon that a sheep (is due) and it should not be eaten but given in charity. We also narrated from him regarding one who had intercourse with his wife before Tawaf: 'Slaughter a fat camel and feed the poor.' And we narrated from Tawus and Sa'id ibn Jubayr that they said: 'One should not eat from the compensation for game nor from the ransom.' (Bayhaqi) From this athar it is learned that one should not eat the meat of the penalty himself but should feed the poor. [80] (7) It is not permissible to eat from the rest of the Hadi. The meat of compensation for crime and game is not permissible to eat. These are fines, not rewards, so do not eat yourself; after slaughter, leave it for the poor to eat. The evidence for this issue has passed in issue no. 4. (2) This hadith is also evidence: He said: Musa ibn Salama al-Hudhali narrated... and said: O Messenger of Allah, what should I do with that which becomes defective from my Hadi? He said: 'Slaughter it, then dip its sandals in its blood, then place them on its hump, and do not eat from it, neither you nor anyone from your traveling companions.' (Abu Dawud, etc.) From this hadith it is learned that for penalties... Footnote: (a) Then the Prophet returned to the place of sacrifice and sacrificed 63 camels with his hand, then gave to Ali and he sacrificed the rest, and he made him share in his Hadi. Then he ordered that a piece from each camel be put in a pot, then cooked, and both ate from the meat and drank the broth. (b) It is narrated from Ibn Umar: 'Do not eat from the compensation for game and the Hadi of a vow, but eat from other than that.' And Ata said: 'Eat from tamattu' and feed others.' (c) Ibn Abbas said: 'For a pigeon, a sheep, not to be eaten, to be given in charity.' And from him regarding one who has intercourse before Tawaf: 'Slaughter a fat camel and feed the poor.' Tawus and Sa'id ibn Jubayr said: 'Do not eat from compensation for game nor from ransom.' (d) He asked: 'O Messenger of Allah, how should I act if something from my Hadi becomes defective?' He said: 'Slaughter it, then dip its sandals in its blood, then place them on its hump, then do not eat from it, neither you nor anyone from your traveling companions.'
Source pages p. 485

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding eating from Hadi (sacrificial animals). The Sharih (commentator) explains that the ruling depends on the type of Hadi. Voluntary (nafl), tamattu', and qiran Hadi are gifts; therefore, the owner may eat from them and feed others. This is proven by the Prophet's practice. In contrast, Hadi brought as a penalty (for errors during Hajj) or compensation for hunting is a fine (jurm), not a gift. Therefore, the one who owes it may not eat from it; rather, it must be given to the poor. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet ordered not to eat from an animal that became defective, indicating that compulsory Hadi is for charity. The commentary also cites companions and successors who held similar distinctions.

Key Terms
هدي (Hady): A sacrificial animal brought to the Haram during Hajj.
جزاء الصيد (Jaza' al-Sayd): Compensation for hunting within the Haram or during Ihram.
نذر (Nathr): A vow; vowed Hadi is compulsory and the donor may not eat from it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Permissible (mubah), because the donor needs the food
B) Prohibited (haram), because it is a fine that must go to the poor

D) Obligatory (wajib) to eat to show gratitude

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of eating Hadi meat depends on its cause: voluntary Hadi may be eaten, while compulsory Hadi must be entirely given in charity.

Time for Slaughter of Voluntary, Tamattu', and Qiran Hadi
Specifies that these types must be slaughtered on Yawm al-Nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required day for slaughtering the Hadi of tamattu', qiran, and voluntary, and explain the Quranic evidence from Surah al-Hajj 22:29.

Core Idea
The Hadi of tamattu', qiran, and voluntary must be slaughtered only on Yawm al-Nahr.

This lesson clarifies a specific timing requirement for certain types of Hadi (sacrificial animals) in Hajj. While some Hadi may be slaughtered on any day of Dhul Hijjah, the Hanafi school holds that voluntary, tamattu', and qiran Hadi are restricted to the 10th (Yawm al-Nahr). The proof is drawn from the Quranic sequence of acts, linking slaughter to the shaving of the head, which occurs on that day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine which Hadi are discussed (voluntary, tamattu', qiran) and the ruling: slaughter is only permissible on Yawm al-Nahr.
The text uses 'la yajuz' (not permissible), indicating prohibition on other days.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the Quranic verse (Surah al-Hajj 22:29) which mentions slaughter, shaving, and tawaf.
The verse is 'thumma liyaqdu tafathahum waliyufu nudhurahum waliyattawwafu bilbayti al-atiq'.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse implies a sequence: slaughter → shave → tawaf. Since shaving (taking the head) occurs on the 10th, slaughter must precede it on the same day.
The link is through the word 'thumma' (then) showing order.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars allow slaughter on the days of Tashriq (11th-13th) for all Hadi. The Hanafi school restricts these three types to Yawm al-Nahr.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi view is based on the specific proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۸۰] (۸) ولا يجوز ذبح هدى التطوع والمتعة والقران الا في يوم النحر
نہیں جائز ہے نفلی تمتع اور قرآن کی ہدی کا ذبح کرنا مگر دسویں ذی الحجہ کو۔
چونکہ رمی جمار کے بعد ہی نفلی ہدی تجمع کی ہدی اور قران کی ہدی ذبح کرے گا اور وہ دسویں ذی الحجہ کو ہوگا اس لئے ان ہدی کو بھی دسویں ذی الحجہ ہی کو ذبح کرے گا (۲) آیت میں اس کا اشارہ موجود ہے فكلوا منها واطعموا البائس الفقير ثم ليقضوا تفثهم وليوفوا نذورهم وليطوفوا بالبيت العتيق (الف) (آیت ۲۹ سورۃ الحج ۲۲) اس آیت میں ہے کہ ہدی کا گوشت غرباء کوکھلاؤ پھر سرمنڈواؤ اور بیت اللہ کا طواف کرو۔ تو سرمنڈوانا دسویں ذی الحجہ کو ہوتا ہے اس لئے ہدی کو ذبح کرنا بھی دسویں ذی الحجہ کو ہو گا۔
حاشیہ : (الف) ہدی سے کھاؤ اور فقیروں کو کھلا ؤ اور گندگی کو ختم کرو اور اپنی نذر پوری کرو اور پرانے گھر کا طواف كرو
It is not permissible to slaughter the Hadi of voluntary, tamattu', and qiran except on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). It is not permissible to slaughter the Hadi of nafl, tamattu', and qiran except on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. Because after stoning the Jamarat, one will slaughter the Hadi of nafl, tamattu', and qiran, and that will be on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, so these Hadi should also be slaughtered on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. (2) There is an indication in the verse: 'So eat from them and feed the miserable poor, then let them complete their rites and fulfill their vows and circumambulate the Ancient House.' (Surah al-Hajj 22:29) In this verse, it says to feed the poor the Hadi meat, then shave your heads and circumambulate the Kaaba. Shaving the head takes place on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, so slaughtering the Hadi also takes place on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. Footnote: (a) Eat from the Hadi and feed the poor, and remove your filth, and fulfill your vows, and circumambulate the Ancient House.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the time of slaughter for specific types of Hadi. The Sharih states that the Hadi of voluntary, tamattu', and qiran must be slaughtered only on Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). The reason is that these Hadi are performed after the stoning of the Jamarat, which is on the 10th. The proof is from the Quranic verse that mentions slaughter, shaving, and Tawaf. Shaving occurs on the 10th, so slaughter precedes it. This timing is specific to these Hadi; other Hadi (such as penalties) are not restricted to this day.

Key Terms
يوم النحر (Yawm al-Nahr): The 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) 8th of Dhul Hijjah
D) 9th of Dhul Hijjah

Key Takeaway
The Hadi of tamattu', qiran, and voluntary must be slaughtered exclusively on Yawm al-Nahr based on the Quranic sequence of Hajj rites.

Time for Slaughter of Other Hadi
Permits slaughter of penalty and other Hadi at any time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time for slaughtering penalty Hadi and cite the Prophetic precedent from Hudaybiyyah.

Core Idea
Penalty Hadi is not restricted to Yawm al-Nahr; it can be sacrificed at any time.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position that certain types of Hadi—penalty, confinement (ihsar), and hunting compensation—are not bound to the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The ruling is derived from the Prophet's own action during the Hudaybiyyah incident, where he sacrificed his Hadi in Dhul Qa'dah. This flexibility distinguishes these Hadi from voluntary, tamattu', and qiran Hadi, which have specific times.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of Hadi covered
The passage distinguishes between nafl/tamattu'/qiran Hadi (time-specific) and penalty/ihsar/hunting compensation Hadi (flexible). List the latter three.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that these Hadi can be slaughtered at any time the owner wishes, not restricted to a particular day.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the Prophet's action at Hudaybiyyah, where he was prevented (muhsar) and sacrificed his Hadi in Dhul Qa'dah, which is not within the days of Nahr.
The incident is cited as a precedent for penalty Hadi.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's act shows that penalty Hadi is not tied to Yawm al-Nahr, as he deliberately chose a non-standard time. This establishes permissibility at any time.

Source Text

۸۰۵] (۹) ويجوز ذبح بقية الهدايا في اي وقت شاء
اور باقی ہدی کو جب چاہے ذبح کرو۔ نقلی ہدی تجمع کی ہدی اور قرآن کی ہدی کے علاوہ جو ہدی ہوں گی وہ جنایات کی ہدی ، احصار کی ہدی اور شکار کے بدلہ کی بدی ہوں گی۔ چونکہ یہ ہدی کسی دن کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہے اس لئے کسی دن بھی ان کو ذبح کی جاسکتی ہیں۔ دسویں ذی الحجہ کے ساتھ خاص نہیں ہیں حضور صلح حدیبیہ کے عمرہ کے موقع پر مصر ہوئے اور ہدی ذیح کی حالانکہ وہ دسویں ذی الحجہ کا دن نہیں تھا بلکہ ذی قعدہ کا دن تھا اس لئے معلوم ہوا کہ باقی ہدی کو کسی دن ذبح کر سکتا ہے۔
And it is permissible to slaughter the rest of the Hadi at any time he wishes. And regarding the remaining Hadi, slaughter them when you wish. Apart from the Hadi of nafl, tamattu', and qiran, the other Hadi are those of penalties, confinement (ihsar), and compensation for hunting. Since these Hadi are not specific to a particular day, they can be slaughtered on any day. They are not specific to the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The Prophet, on the occasion of the Umrah of Hudaybiyyah, was prevented and sacrificed his Hadi, even though that was not the day of 10th Dhul Hijjah but rather the month of Dhul Qa'dah. So it is known that the remaining Hadi can be slaughtered on any day.
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the time of slaughter for Hadi other than voluntary, tamattu', and qiran. The Sharih clarifies that penalty Hadi, Hadi for ihsar (being prevented), and compensation for hunting are not restricted to Yawm al-Nahr. The proof is the incident of Hudaybiyyah where the Prophet slaughtered his Hadi in Dhul Qa'dah. Thus, these Hadi can be slaughtered at any time, even outside the Hajj season.

Key Terms
احصار (Ihsar): Being prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to enemy or illness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Only 10th Dhul Hijjah
B) Any day
C) Only during Hajj
D) Only in Dhul Qa'dah

Key Takeaway
Penalty, ihsar, and hunting compensation Hadi can be slaughtered at any time, as demonstrated by the Prophet's action at Hudaybiyyah.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
Place of Slaughter for All Hadi
Requires all Hadi to be slaughtered within the Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement that all Hadi must be slaughtered within the Haram and identify the Quranic evidence for this ruling.

Core Idea
Every Hadi must be slaughtered within the Haram; outside is invalid.

This passage establishes a crucial rule for Hajj: the location of slaughter for the Hadi (sacrificial animal) is not optional. According to the Hanafi school, all types of Hadi – whether voluntary, obligatory due to tamattu', qiran, compensation for game, or other penalties – must be sacrificed within the sacred precincts of Makkah (the Haram). The proof is drawn directly from the Quran and supported by early practice. Understanding this requirement ensures that your hajj rituals are complete and valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on the permissibility of slaughtering Hadi. According to the Hanafi school, it is wajib to slaughter every Hadi within the Haram. Slaughtering outside is invalid.
The ruling applies to all categories of Hadi: nafl, tamattu', qiran, compensation for game, penalties, and ihsar.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two Quranic verses: Surah al-Baqarah 2:196 ("until the Hadi reaches its place") and Surah al-Ma'idah 5:95 ("a Hadi reaching the Kaaba").
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Hanafi interpretation reads "its place" (mahillahu) as the Haram, and "reaching the Kaaba" as requiring arrival at the Kaaba itself, i.e., the Haram. Thus the verses mandate the Haram as the location.
The dalala (indication) is zanni because the word 'mahillahu' could be interpreted differently by other schools.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi position is mukhtalaf fih: some schools allow slaughter outside the Haram for certain types of Hadi.
The passage also cites Imam Malik's view for support, though the Hanafi position is independently established.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, when performing Hajj, ensure that any Hadi you offer is slaughtered within the boundaries of the Haram. If slaughtered outside, the Hadi is not valid and the obligation remains unfulfilled.
The Haram is not limited to Mina; it includes all areas within the Haram boundaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۸۰۶] (۱۰) ولا يجوز ذبح الهدايا الا في
ہدی ذبح کر کے چھوڑ دے اور خود نہ کھائے اور نہ اس کے ساتھی کھائے بلکہ غرباء کے لئے چھوڑ دے۔ کیونکہ پھاڑ کھانے والے جانوروں کے لئے چھوڑنا اچھا نہیں ہے۔
نہیں جائز ہے کسی ہدی کو ذبح کرنا مگر حرم میں ۔
نقلی ہدی تمتع کی ہدی ، قرآن کی ہدی، شکار کا بدلہ ہدی ، جنایات کی ہدی اور احصار کی ہدی ان سب کو حنفیہ کے نزدیک حرم ہی میں ذیح
کرنا ضروری ہے۔ آیت میں ہے ولا تحلقوا رؤوسكم حتى يبلغ الهدى محله (ب) ( آیت ۹۶ اسورة البقرة) دوسری آیت میں ہے يَحْكُمُ بِهِ ذَوَا عَدْلٍ مِّنْكُمْ هَدْيًا بَـٰلِغَ الْكَعْبَةِ (ج) ( آیت ۹۵ سورة المائدة (۵) اس آیت سے پتہ چلا کہ ہدی کعبہ تک پہنچے اور وہاں ذبح ہو (۳) اثر میں ہے قال مالك والذي يحكم عليه بالهدى فى قتل الصيد او يجب عليه الهدى في غير ذلك فان هدیه لا يكون الا بمكة كما قال الله تعالى هديا بالغ الكعبة (د) (موطا امام مالک، باب جامع الھدی ص ۴۰۹ ) اس اثر میں ہے کہ شکار
حاشیہ : (الف) ہدی سے کھاؤ اور فقیروں کو کھلا ؤ اور گندگی کو ختم کرو اور اپنی نذر پوری کرو اور پرانے گھر کا طواف کرو (ب) سرمت منڈواؤ جب تک ہدی مقام تک نہ پہنچ جائے یعنی حرم نہ پہنچ جائے (ج) شکار کے بدلہ کا فیصلہ کریں گے دو انصاف در آدمی ہدی کا جو کعبہ تک پہنچنے والی ہو (و) حضرت امام مالک نے فرمایا جو ہدی کا فیصلہ کیا جائے شکار کے قتل میں یا اس پر ہدی واجب ہو اس کے علاوہ میں تو اس کی ہدی نہ ذبیح ہو مگر مکہ مکرمہ میں، جیسا کہ اللہ تعالی نے فرمایا ہدی جو مکہ مکرمہ تک پہنچنے والی ہو۔
It is not permissible to slaughter the Hadi except in... He should slaughter the Hadi and leave it, not eat from it, nor should his companions, but leave it for the poor because leaving it for animals that tear apart is not good. It is not permissible to slaughter any Hadi except in the Haram. According to the Hanafis, it is necessary to slaughter the Hadi of nafl, tamattu', qiran, compensation for game, penalties, and ihsar only in the Haram. The verse says: 'And do not shave your heads until the Hadi reaches its place [of sacrifice]' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:196). Another verse says: 'Two just persons among you shall judge, a Hadi reaching the Kaaba' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:95). From this verse it is understood that the Hadi must reach the Kaaba and be slaughtered there. The athar is: Malik said: 'That which is judged as Hadi for killing game or for which Hadi is due otherwise, its Hadi is not but in Makkah, as Allah said: a Hadi reaching the Kaaba.' (Muwatta) In this athar it is that for game... Footnote: (a) Eat from the Hadi and feed the poor, and remove your filth, and fulfill your vows, and circumambulate the Ancient House. (b) Do not shave your heads until the Hadi reaches its place, i.e., reaches the Haram. (c) Two just persons among you will judge a Hadi that reaches the Kaaba. (d) Imam Malik said: 'That which is judged as Hadi for killing game or for which Hadi is due otherwise, its Hadi is not slaughtered except in Makkah, as Allah said: a Hadi reaching the Kaaba.'
Source pages p. 486

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the place of slaughter for all types of Hadi. The Sharih states that, according to the Hanafi school, it is necessary to slaughter every Hadi within the Haram (the sacred precincts of Makkah). The evidence is from two Quranic verses: one requiring the Hadi to 'reach its place' (interpreted as the Haram), and another requiring it to reach the Kaaba. The Sharih also cites Imam Malik's opinion for support, though the Hanafi position is clear. The place of slaughter must be within the boundaries of the Haram. This includes all types: voluntary, tamattu', qiran, penalties, and compensation.

Key Terms
حرم (Haram): The sacred area around Makkah where certain Hajj rituals are performed.
هدي (Hadi): Sacrificial animal offered during Hajj.
محله (mahillahu): Its place (of sacrifice); interpreted by Hanafis as the Haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where must all Hadi be slaughtered according to the Hanafi school?
A) Only at Mina
B) Within the Haram
C) Anywhere in Makkah
D) Outside Makkah

Key Takeaway
All Hadi, regardless of type, must be slaughtered within the Haram boundaries to be valid.
